The partners are men who appear to be the men they appear to be (the contrast with the Mystique-as-Opal and Mystique-as-Annie episodes is total). The relationships are short-lived but not for the previous reasons; they end on grounds approximately appropriate to their actual content rather than collapsing under the weight of concealment.

The coming-out to his parents during the Iceman solo period produced, predictably, his father's bad reaction. The mother's role across this confrontation is more visible than in the William hospitalization sequence — she is present, she is conflicted, she is moving — and the file should record that the long mother-relationship begins, very late, to surface as a distinct line of development rather than a background presence.

---

## X. The Patterns at Period's End

By the close of the middle period — immediately prior to the Krakoan reconstitution — the longitudinal record shows the following stabilized patterns:

- **Humor armor:** intact, slightly less reflexive than in the X-Factor years, used more selectively.
- **Throttling of power:** intact, though the post-sh


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# CHRONOLOGY IV — RECENT HISTORY & CURRENT STATE

*File segment: 2019 → present. Continuous longitudinal observation, cross-referenced against Hickman-era *House of X / Powers of X* (2019), *Marauders* vol. 1 (Duggan, 2019–2022), *X-Men* vol. 5–6 (Hickman/Duggan, 2019–2024), *Inferno* (2021), *A.X.E.: Judgment Day* (2022), *Sins of Sinister* (2023), *Fall of X / Fall of the House of X / Rise of the Powers of X* (2023–2024), *From the Ashes* relaunch (*Uncanny X-Men* Gail Simone; *X-Men* MacKay, 2024–present). Sub-files referenced where relevant.*

---

## 1. The Krakoan Threshold (mid-2019)

The Krakoan transition is, in this subject's longitudinal record, the single largest discontinuity since the original adolescent recruitment of 1963. Its significance cannot be overstated and is best understood structurally: for the first time in his life, the institution he belongs to issues a *blanket pre-authorization* covering both of the identities he had spent six decades concealing or shrinking. Mutancy is no longer stigma but citizenship. Same-sex partnership is unremarked, infrastructural — the Resurrection Protocols, the gateways, the bunkhouses on Krakoa make no distinction. The permission structures that Drake had spent his entire adult life *waiting for* arrive at once, and the behavioral response is observable within weeks.

Initial intake behaviors on Krakoa (cf. *X-Men* #1 vol. 5, *Marauders* #1): he stops apologizing for property damage. He stops modulating the size of constructs to match the size of the room. He freezes a Russian icebreaker in *Marauders* #1 with no preamble and no aftermath sheepishness — a tonal departure that prior writers (Lobdell, even Bendis) would have undercut with a quip. He still quips. But the quip arrives *after* the action and serves social bonding rather than self-deflection. The diagnostic distinction matters: humor-as-armor versus humor-as-rapport. The former predominates 1963–2019; the latter takes over ~2019–2024.

Residence: nominal hut on Krakoa, but functionally lives aboard the *Marauder* (Captain Kate Pryde's vessel) for the entirety of the Hellfire Trading Company era. Roommate-of-record: shifting (Storm, Pyro, Bishop), but his bunk pattern is consistent — small space, organized, books, no personal photographs displayed. The absence of displayed family imagery, after coming out and after his parents' partial rejection, is a tell: he has not severed, but he has not reconstituted.

---

## 2. The Marauders Era (2019–2022)

This is the period in which the throttle visibly releases and stays released longest. The operational role — extracting mutants from anti-mutant nations via maritime smuggling — is, *psychologically*, the role he was built for. He is rescuing the young and the hunted from the very mob dynamic that nearly killed him in adolescence. The childhood lesson (visibility at full scale is lethal) is being inverted operationally (visibility at full scale is *what saves the others*). One does not need to invoke metaphor to see the repair work.

Granular behavioral notes from this era:

- **Power expression.** Routinely operates at scales he had refused for decades: freezing harbors, generating ice constructs the size of city blocks, mimicking the ice-form of others, fine-grain water-vapor sensing across kilometers. The Mikhail Rasputin engagement in *Marauders* #11–12 is the most explicit demonstration — he matches and exceeds a peer omega in a contest of cryokinesis. Critically, *he does not apologize for the win.* This is novel.
- **Public profile.** Becomes the publicly known face of the Hellfire Trading Company's "Red Bishop"-adjacent operations; the X-desk file lists him as one of the three most-photographed Krakoans of 2020 (Pryde, Drake, Pyro). The man who spent fifty publication-years avoiding being seen is now on the cover of mutant tabloids.
- **Voice.** Speech rate increases ~15% (informal estimate from dialogic density per page). Sentence length expands. He becomes the verbal lead of his scenes rather than the comic punctuator. Sentence-final tags ("…right?", "…I guess.") drop sharply.
- **Affect.** Visible range broadens. He is recorded *angry* for sustained beats (post-Pyro's near-death, post-Pryde's murder by Sebastian Shaw) without immediately deflecting into a quip. The narrow dysthymic band described in §3 of the workup widens — the first sustained widening in the record.

### 2a. Christian Frost — and what it tells us

The relationship with Christian Frost (introduced *Marauders* #12 ff.) is, on the documentary surface, brief and ambiguous. Christian is a recovering Frost — gay, Hellfire-adjacent, telepathic, fragile, the only Frost sibling Emma protected rather than weaponized. The pairing is intentionally and visibly *symmetrical* to the workup's central diagnostic: a man whose powerful sister tried to use his body, paired with a man who once had his body used by that same sister. They share a vocabulary of *being made small to survive.* The relationship does not last in the formal sense, but it is the first relationship in the file in which Drake is observed selecting a partner on the basis of *recognition* rather than pursuit-of-the-unavailable or acceptance-of-deception. The pattern of selection — not the duration — is the diagnostic shift.

### 2b. The Hellfire Gala public-figure phase (2021–2022)

Three Galas of record. He attends all three. Wardrobe across all three: literal ice — sometimes formal, sometimes barely-formal, increasingly comfortable with the implication of nudity beneath. The body-image distress documented in earlier eras (post-Mystique shattering, the 1991 inability-to-revert arc) does not surface. He is photographed laughing at the second Gala beside Northstar, Aurora, and the now-public Hellfire executive class. The man who avoided photographs as a depowered teenager is at ease at the most-photographed event on the calendar.

---

## 3. Inferno → Judgment Day → Sins of Sinister (2021–2023)

The Krakoan optimism is structurally undercut across this stretch; the subject's behavior under the slow-revelation of betrayal (Moira, Mystique, Destiny, Sinister's long con) is observably *unlike* his prior crisis responses.

- **Inferno (2021).** When the Quiet Council fractures and Mystique–Destiny return, Drake's posture is wary but not regressive. He does not retreat into compartmentalization. He stays operational. Worth flagging because Mystique is, historically, the single most destabilizing other in his romantic record (twice impersonated his partners). He neither confronts her nor avoids her — he simply *works around her,* which is the first observation of mature lateral handling of this specific stressor.
- **Judgment Day (2022).** When the Progenitor judges humanity and individual heroes, Drake's individual judgment scene is not centered in panel — but the inference from his post-event behavior is that he passed or near-passed. He is shown ministering to the dying, doing first-responder cryo-stabilization in mass-casualty zones, not seeking credit. Compare to prior crossover events in which his contributions were comic-relief; here he is *unwitnessed competence at scale,* which is a developmental milestone the workup specifically identifies as missing.
- **Sins of Sinister (2023).** In the dystopian-timeline branch, future-Drake is one of the holdouts against the Sinister-infected diaspora. The pertinent data is not the alternate-timeline behavior (which is not strictly canonical to his psyche) but the *baseline* the writers' room felt was justified in projecting forward: a Drake who at the far end of stress becomes a hardened, lethally competent freedom-fighter, not a collapsed dissociator. The room has updated its model. The file updates accordingly.

---

## 4. Fall of X — Fall of the House of X — Rise of the Powers of X (2023–2024)

The collapse of Krakoa is the event the workup explicitly flags as the most dangerous developmental risk: *when the institution that lets him be himself disappears, regression risk is significant.* The observed behavior is, on balance, less regressive than predicted — but the partial regression that does occur is diagnostically informative.

### 4a. Loss of the permission structure

Krakoa falls. The gateways die. The Resurrection Protocols collapse. Orchis hunts the diaspora. Public sentiment reverts. The umbrella of pre-authorization under which Drake had operated for four years is gone in days.

Predictable regressions, observed:

- **Power suppression returns, partially.** Operational scale shrinks back toward "human-sized fight" defaults in early Fall of X appearances. Not all the way to pre-Krakoa levels, but a measurable contraction.
- **Humor sharpens and re-arms.** The quip returns to its older defensive function in scenes with non-mutant law enforcement and Orchis assets.
- **Compartmentalization re-engages.** He resumes a low-profile civilian footprint in flashes — a Long Island sublet, cash transactions, a beard of routines.

Predicted regressions that did *not* occur:

- He does not retreat into ice-form dissociation. Across the entire Fall arc the somatic-escape pattern is conspicuously absent. This is the most important non-event in the recent file.
- He does not seek paternal-transference reattachment to Cyclops in the deferential mode of prior eras. He works *with* Scott as a peer in the resistance, not as a junior. The deference modeled across 1963–2010 is no longer present in dyadic Drake–Summers data.
- He does not abandon the partner-selection update. Recent romantic data is sparse during the collapse (operationally appropriate), but there is no observed reversion to pursuit-of-the-unavailable.

### 4b. Specific incidents of record (Fall of X)

- Participates in the *X-Force* / Marauders splinter resistance early in the Fall. Operates from concealed maritime bases. Maintains the smuggling-of-mutants role, now extralegal again rather than treaty-protected.
- Confirmed alive and uncaptured through the entirety of Orchis's primary purge — i.e., did not require resurrection during the late-Krakoan Protocol crisis, a fact that mattered enormously when the Protocols collapsed and resurrection became unavailable. Subject's threat-avoidance under conditions of *no respawn* is intact and competent.
- Reunites with the broader X-roster at the *Rise of the Powers of X* climax. Operational role: theater-level cryokinetic support during the assault on the Orchis stronghold. Power expression closer to Krakoan peak than to pre-Krakoan baseline. The throttle, while partially re-engaged in low-stakes scenes, releases for high-stakes ones.

### 4c. The grief-data

The cumulative losses across Fall of X — Krakoa itself, friends not resurrected in time, the loss of the Resurrection guarantee, the public-affection collapse — produce in subject a sustained affective response that is *grief, not depressive collapse.* The distinction is clinically meaningful. He mourns. He keeps working. He does not flatten. This is the first major crisis in the file in which loss produces appropriate, metabolizable grief rather than dysthymic deepening. The most parsimonious explanation: the Krakoan years provided enough corrective experience to alter the baseline. Four years of being safely seen does not undo six decades — but it changes the slope.

---

## 5. From the Ashes (2024 → present)

Post-Krakoa, the X-line scatters into multiple operational cells (Cyclops's outlaw squad in *X-Men*; Rogue's Xavier-flag team in *Uncanny X-Men*; the Storm/MacKay arrangements; the *NYX* street-level cell). Drake's current placement: peripatetic, but with primary affiliation observed in the broader Uncanny / X-Men ensemble appearances and in cameo across cells. He is no longer institutionally anchored — and this is the present-tense risk.

### 5a. Current operational status

- **Address (functional, not legal):** itinerant. Long Island safe-house rotation; occasional Graymalkin Industries / Alaska-cell logistical visits; New York City civilian footprint maintained sub-rosa.
- **Identity status:** publicly known mutant; publicly known gay; both facts now *years old* in the public record. The double-concealment that defined his first five decades is structurally impossible to reconstitute. This is permanent.
- **Power expression baseline:** elevated relative to all pre-Krakoan eras; modestly attenuated relative to Marauders peak. Trend: stable.
- **Affiliations of record:** X-Men loose ensemble; informal continuing tie to former Marauders crew; continuing personal tie to Hank McCoy (complicated post-X-Force Beast revelations and resolution — see §5c); continuing fraternal tie to Warren Worthington and Jean Grey.
- **Partner status:** unattached on the documentary record at file-close. No active romantic affiliation confirmed. Notable: the absence is *un*-anxious; he is not visibly pursuing.

### 5b. The Long Island problem

He has not fully reconciled with William Drake. The Iceman solo arcs (Grace, 2017–2019) initiated the work; Krakoa structurally deprioritized it (citizenship elsewhere); the Fall has thrown him back into geographic proximity. Surveillance-grade inference: he has visited the family home at least twice in the post-Krakoan window. Duration of visits: short. Mother contact: warmer, sustained. Father contact: present, terse, neither rupture nor repair. The open wound remains open. It is not bleeding actively; it is not closing.

This is the largest piece of unfinished psychological business in the current-state file. Every other major thread (power, identity, partnership-selection criteria, institutional belonging) has advanced. The father has not.

### 5c. Hank McCoy

The most stable attachment in the entire longitudinal record was destabilized severely by the X-Force-era Beast atrocities and the subsequent reckoning. Drake's handling of this is among the most behaviorally consequential data points in the recent file. He did *not* perform the reflexive loyalty the prior six decades would have predicted. He held Hank accountable — quietly, ethically, without grandstanding — while not severing. The capacity to remain in relationship with a beloved who has committed serious wrong, without either abandoning ethics or abandoning the person, is a developmental achievement the earlier Drake could not have executed. He would have either deflected with humor and pretended the wrong did not occur, or compartmentalized Hank away. He did neither. This is the most mature interpersonal performance in the file.

### 5d. Mentor role

Across the post-Krakoan ensemble appearances he is increasingly observed in a mentor posture to younger mutants — the role the workup flags as one in which he is "unexpectedly competent." This is no longer unexpected. It is now baseline. He is the elder in most rooms he enters. He has not yet fully internalized this, and is occasionally observed still positioning himself as the youngest — a habit-residue of sixty years — but corrects within scenes. The self-concept is updating, slowly.

---

## 6. Present-State Synthesis

Where the subject was at file-open (1963): a terrified adolescent extracted from a lynch mob, the youngest in every room, hiding two identities under one another like nested boxes, performing smallness as a survival strategy.

Where the subject is at file-close (present): a publicly-known Omega-class mutant, publicly out, operationally consequential at theater scale, romantically unattached but no longer in pursuit-of-the-unavailable mode, in selective adult relationship with a partially-reconciled family of origin, holding ethical lines with beloveds who have committed wrongs, mentoring without yet quite knowing he is doing it, mourning Krakoa without collapsing into it, performing power at scales the 1963 file could not have predicted and the 1995 file did not believe possible.

The throttle has been released, partially re-engaged in low-stakes settings, and released again under demand. Its set-point has moved. It will not return to the 1963–2010 baseline. The institution that gave him permission is gone; the permission has been internalized in sufficient measure that the institution's collapse does not revoke it. This is the central finding of the recent-history record.

Risks at present:

1. **Institutional grief unresolved.** Krakoa was the longest-running corrective experience of his life. Its loss is metabolized as grief, not collapse, but the grief is current and will recur.
2. **Paternal reconciliation incomplete.** The single largest piece of remaining developmental work. Time-bounded — William Drake is elderly in any plausible timescale.
3. **Romantic isolation, currently chosen, could harden into avoidance.** The non-pursuit is healthy now; if sustained too long it will reclassify.
4. **Mentor role unclaimed.** He is performing it without owning it. Until he owns it, he will continue to subtly position himself as the kid in the room, which mis-signals to the actual kids in the room.

Strengths at present:

1. **Power baseline permanently elevated.** The somatic enactment of "be small to be loved" has been substantially disconfirmed by lived experience. He is *bigger* now, by his own body's measure, and has not been killed for it.
2. **Identity baseline permanently public.** The closet is structurally inaccessible. The vigilance budget that maintained it for fifty years is freed.
3. **Affect range permanently widened.** Anger, grief, joy, desire — all observed in sustained form in recent eras. The narrow dysthymic band of 1963–2015 is not the current band.
4. **Mature ethical handling of beloved-who-erred.** The Hank case is precedent and will generalize.
5. **Crisis behavior is competence-under-pressure, not dissociation-under-pressure.** The Fall confirmed this. The escalation curve described in §5 of the workup — escalation into capacity rather than volatility — held under maximum stress.

### Final note for the recent-history segment

The subject is, at file-close, the most behaviorally *changed* he has been in the entire six-decade record, and the change is in the direction the analytical workup predicted was possible-but-unfinished. He is no longer the same psychological organism the early-file assessments mapped. The pattern that "barely deviates across six decades" has, in the last five years, deviated — durably, asymmetrically, in the direction of integration. The dossier should be considered an active, updating file. Recommend reassessment at the next major institutional transition.

— END SEGMENT —


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: ROBERT LOUIS DRAKE

*File section 4 of 17. Cross-reference §3 (Psychological) and §6 (Somatic-Mutational Profile). All entries derived from observable canonical record; clinical inference is flagged as such.*

---

## 4.1 BASELINE SOMATIC PROFILE

**Demographics at first medical contact (recruitment to Xavier's, mid-adolescence).** Caucasian male, of Irish-American ancestry, raised Long Island (Fort Washington / Port Washington vicinity per Iceman vol. 1 and Iceman 2017). Height at intake approximately 5'8", projected to adult terminal of ~6'0". Weight at intake low-normal for stature (~140 lb), reaching adult baseline of approximately 170–180 lb. Hair sandy-blond, skin fair, eyes blue. No congenital anomalies on record. No childhood hospitalizations of note prior to manifestation.

**Constitutional baseline.** Endomorph-leaning ectomorph with poor adolescent musculature; develops athletic conditioning only after Xavier's Danger Room regimen and never to the hypertrophic standard of Summers, Worthington, or McCoy. He is, across six decades of record, the *least physically conditioned* of the original five in human form — a detail that matters because his entire combat efficacy is mutant-mediated. Stripped of powers, his physical-defensive capacity collapses to civilian baseline. He knows this; it shapes his risk calculus.

**Resting somatic markers (inferred / observed).** Resting pulse low-normal. Cold tolerance phenomenally high (functionally infinite when mutation is engaged; markedly above baseline even when human-form). Heat tolerance subjectively *poor* — multiple panels across eras show Bobby visibly discomforted by ambient warmth long before teammates register it, suggesting thermoregulatory baseline has shifted toward cold-preference. This is a quiet but consistent tell: he runs cool, dresses lighter than ambient temperature would suggest, prefers windows open, drinks ice water reflexively.

**Dentition, vision, audition.** Unremarkable. No corrective lenses. No documented dental work beyond routine. Voice unbroken in tessitura, slightly nasal, often pitched upward into the question-cadence that is one of his most stable phonological tells.

---

## 4.2 MUTATION — ONSET AND DEVELOPMENTAL COURSE

**Manifestation event (early-to-mid adolescence; canonical X-Men #44–47, expanded Iceman vol. 1 #1, 1984).** Spontaneous expression triggered by acute distress — assault on a date (Judy Harmon). Initial expression: low-grade ice generation, hand-bound, uncontrolled. No prodromal symptoms documented; no fever, no growth disturbance, no neurological signs in the standard adolescent mutation profile. The expression was *useful* in the moment (defensive) and *catastrophic* socially (public). This conditioning — power = visibility = mortal danger — is laid down at the somatic level on day one and is functionally ineradicable.

**Early form-instability period (first 12–18 months).** Hand-and-arm only ice generation, with frequent involuntary expression under emotional load. Documented adolescent episodes of bedding frozen overnight, water glasses cracking in his grip, ambient room temperature dropping when he is angry or aroused. These are *somatic stress markers* that persist in attenuated form into adulthood — a reliable behavioral-medical sign clinicians could use to gauge his actual affective state behind the humor mask.

**Snow-form transition (Lee/Kirby, X-Men #8 onward).** Conversion of skin to compacted snow. Phenotype: opaque white, granular surface, retained human proportions, vulnerable to fracturing under impact, susceptible to melt under direct heat. This was his operational form for roughly twenty publication-years (mid-1960s through Defenders/X-Factor original era).

**Ice-form transition (X-Factor era, mid-1980s, sustained through present).** Conversion of body mass to transparent organic ice. Phenotype: clear-to-pale-blue refractive surface, retained human proportions and facial features, dramatically increased durability, increased mass density, retention of fine-motor capacity. The transition between snow-form and ice-form is itself developmentally significant: it occurs *after* he has been told repeatedly by external parties that he is throttling himself. Each subsequent expansion of capacity occurs the same way — externally prompted, internally resisted, eventually integrated, then re-suppressed below the new ceiling.

**Latent omega expressions, partial list.** Ice-mimicry (full-body reconstitution while remaining ambulatory in ice-form). Atmospheric moisture harvesting (matter generation from humidity at scale). Hydrokinetic-adjacent water control. Thermokinetic environmental cooling at climate-relevant scale (Krakoa-era demonstrations against Mikhail Rasputin's force; Marauders run). Molecular reconstitution from dispersed ice/water (post-Mystique shattering, X-Men #200). The Loki augmentation (X-Factor Annual #4) is the in-text canonical *statement* that all of this was always there.

---

## 4.3 INJURY LEDGER, CHRONOLOGICAL

### 4.3.1 Adolescence — The Mob

The near-lynching is the foundational somatic-trauma event. Documented injuries: contusions consistent with manual assault, possible cracked rib (inferred from movement panels), facial bruising, restraint trauma at wrists. Held in municipal lockup at the time of Xavier's intervention. Extracted by Cyclops. *Psychological imprint:* the body learned that bodies-of-strangers are a lethal apparatus. Every subsequent crowd scene in his life is, at the autonomic level, run through this template. He scans crowds reflexively. He stands near exits. He locates Hank McCoy in any room within seconds of entering.

### 4.3.2 Early X-Men Era — Training Injuries

Routine Danger Room contusions and abrasions, no notable structural injuries. One documented loss of consciousness during a Sentinel-simulation overload (early Thomas run). Mild frostbite injuries to his *own teammates* when he loses control of ambient field — a recurring early-career issue. He apologizes excessively. Pattern: when his power injures others, he over-apologizes and *throttles further down* — the opposite of the standard learning curve, which would be to gain finer control through expanded use.

### 4.3.3 Champions / Defenders Wandering Years

Multiple combat injuries, none individually severe but cumulatively significant. He is on dissolving teams without consistent medical support (Xavier's infirmary unavailable). Likely undertreated soft-tissue injuries. Notable: during this period he sustains a *broken arm* in human form (Champions, late 1970s) and discovers experientially that his ice-form is incompatible with internal cast hardware — a small medical detail with large operational implications. He learns to assess injuries by which form he can hold and for how long.

### 4.3.4 Marauders Attack (X-Factor, late 1980s, Mutant Massacre adjacent)

Severe trauma at the hands of Mister Sinister's strike team. Multiple impact injuries, disrupted ice-form transitions for an extended period afterward, hospitalization (Xavier-network medical). Documented difficulty *holding* ice-form for normal durations during convalescence. This is medically important: it establishes that his mutation can be functionally injured at the control level by trauma, independent of physical wounds. The mutation has a *psychological substrate* that can be damaged. He becomes, post-Marauders, more reluctant to engage at scale — a setback in the throttling curve that takes years to recover from.

### 4.3.5 Loki Augmentation (X-Factor Annual #4)

Not an injury per se, but a transformative somatic event. Loki temporarily augments his capacity to demonstrate latent potential as part of the Acts of Vengeance / Lokisource pageant. Bobby experiences, for the first time at the somatic level, what unrestrained expression feels like. He reverts. He does not pursue. The *medical* fact is that his body now has cellular memory of full expression — the ceiling is known, and known to him, from this point forward. Every subsequent suppression is therefore active, not passive. He is choosing it. The fatigue this generates — the chronic energetic cost of holding oneself below one's actual baseline — is, I infer, a substantial contributor to his persistent low-grade dysthymic affect.

### 4.3.6 Stuck-in-Ice-Form Episodes

Multiple. First major instance early X-Factor / X-Men crossover era; recurrent post-Marauders; severe post-Mystique shattering. Each episode produces acute body-image distress. He cannot eat conventionally in ice-form; he cannot touch loved ones without thermal harm; he cannot present as civilian-Bobby in the world. The episodes resolve via combinations of professional intervention (Hank, MacTaggert facility, Xavier) and self-regulation. *Each episode is also, behaviorally, a retreat* — he is more comfortable in ice-form than the distress suggests, and the "stuckness" sometimes outlasts its physiological necessity. Clinical inference: somatic dissociation operationalized as medical event.

### 4.3.7 Emma Frost Possession (Uncanny X-Men #314, 1994)

Telepathic body-displacement. Bobby is evicted from his own body for an extended sequence while Frost demonstrates capacities he has never achieved. On reintegration: disorientation, mild dissociative residue, and — critically — the somatic knowledge of what his own body can do *when not throttled by his own psychology.* The medical analogue is a kind of inverse phantom-limb: he now feels the absence of capacities his body proved it has. This is a major somatic-psychological event and is, in my assessment, one of the three or four most clinically significant points in his entire record. He trains briefly with Frost afterward, then retreats. The retreat is the diagnostic finding.

### 4.3.8 Shattering by Mystique (X-Men #200, 2007)

Physical disintegration into ice fragments. Full molecular dispersion. Reconstitution over time. Medically without precedent in baseline human biology and rare even in mutant cohort. The reconstitution itself is a demonstration of omega-level capacity that he *did not consciously initiate* — his body did it. The trauma response afterward includes: extended ice-form periods, reluctance to engage Mystique-coded contexts, sharpened humor-deflection, and (notable) increased *willingness* to operate in ice-form for routine activity. Post-shattering, ice-form becomes more default than before. The body learned it could come back from anything and the psychology over-corrected toward the form that proved indestructible.

### 4.3.9 Decimation / M-Day (House of M, 2005)

Bobby retains his powers when 90%+ of mutant peers do not. This is a *non-injury* with significant somatic-psychological consequences: survivor's guilt at the cellular level, intensified by his prior internalized framework of being defective and undeserving. He becomes one of the de facto frontliners during the depopulated post-M-Day period, which forces a temporary expansion of operational capacity that he again retracts when the institutional pressure eases.

### 4.3.10 Krakoan-Era Combat (2019–2024)

Extensive demonstration of omega expression with correspondingly *fewer* documented personal injuries — when he stops throttling, his combat efficacy expands and his exposure decreases. Resurrection protocols on Krakoa render the injury ledger somewhat moot for this period in any case, but the operational data point stands: full expression is *safer for him* than suppressed expression. This is medically counterintuitive and psychologically devastating in implication — six decades of throttling were not protective. They were the source of most of his injuries.

---

## 4.4 TRANSFORMATIONS AND FORM-STATE MEDICINE

Bobby's medical history is unusual in that "what body is he in" is itself a chart entry.

**Human form.** Standard somatic vulnerability. This is the form in which he is most psychologically integrated (CPA identity, civilian relationships, family contact) and most physically fragile. He spends decreasing amounts of time in human form across the longitudinal record — a quiet but measurable trend.

**Snow-form (legacy).** Largely abandoned post-1980s. Now used only for casual / low-stakes contexts. Operationally inferior. Its retention as a *stylistic* choice in low-stakes settings is itself revealing — it is the form of his adolescence, deployed when he is feeling young.

**Ice-form (operational baseline).** Default combat form. Increasingly default *non-combat* form post-shattering. Renders him largely invulnerable to conventional injury, immune to most pathogens, immune to suffocation, immune to dehydration in the conventional sense, immune to temperature extremes. Disadvantages: cannot eat or drink conventionally; intimate physical contact thermally hazardous to others; civilian social presentation impossible. The *somatic-dissociative function* of this form has been discussed above and is, in my judgment, the single most under-recognized medical fact in his file.

**Dispersed / distributed state.** Edge phenomenon. Used involuntarily (shattering) and voluntarily (reconstitution after dispersion). Demonstrates that his somatic identity is not body-bounded. Implications for personhood and medicolegal status are non-trivial and historically under-addressed.

**Augmented / omega state.** Sustained only under external pressure or permission. Energetic cost subjectively perceived as low; psychological cost subjectively perceived as high. He does not like being in this state, which is to say: he does not like *being himself at full scale.*

---

## 4.5 SURGICAL AND PROCEDURAL HISTORY

No documented elective surgeries. No documented major reconstructive surgeries — his somatic plasticity in ice-form obviates most surgical indications. Routine dental and dermatological care presumed continuous through civilian decades. Standard immunizations through Xavier-school medical. Likely vision and hearing screening unremarkable.

The absence of surgical history is itself a finding: most X-roster operatives of comparable tenure have substantial reconstructive records. Bobby's body either heals via mutation-mediated reconstitution or, in human form, he avoids the kinds of contact-combat that would require surgical repair. He is, operationally, a stand-off ranged operator — and this has kept his surgical chart blank.

---

## 4.6 SUBSTANCES

**Alcohol.** Light-to-moderate social use across adult record. Beer at team gatherings, wine at dinners, occasional whiskey in his thirties. No documented intoxication-driven incidents. No documented withdrawal phenomena. Conspicuously *low* use given affective burden — consistent with his over-controlled cluster. He does not let himself disinhibit chemically because disinhibition risks the things he has spent his life suppressing (power, identity, anger at his father, attraction to men). The temperance is *defensive*.

**Tobacco.** Negative.

**Cannabis.** Negative on record. Inferred occasional use during Champions / California period possible but undocumented.

**Stimulants / depressants / opioids.** Negative. No prescription pain management history of note — his mutation-mediated injury recovery has largely obviated this.

**Caffeine.** Moderate. Coffee consumer (X-Factor office scenes, repeated). Iced. Always iced.

**Eating pattern.** Documented preference for cold foods, ice cream specifically — a near-constant prop across decades that functions as both genuine preference and self-soothing ritual. Eating in human form only; he goes hungry rather than revert when ice-form is operationally required. Mild restrictive pattern under stress (X-Factor Opal-era panels show him picking at food; Iceman solo shows similar).

---

## 4.7 SEXUAL AND REPRODUCTIVE HEALTH

**Reproductive status:** no offspring on record. No documented attempts. No documented infertility workup.

**STI history:** none on record.

**Sexual activity ledger:** strikingly thin for sixty years of publication. Long stretches of unconsummated pursuit; several short-lived consummated relationships; multiple instances of partners who were not who they appeared (Mystique-as-Opal; possibly Mystique-as-Annie Ghazikhanian; the gender-fluid Cloud during Defenders tenure). Post-2015, more authentic relational engagement but still short-lived partnerships.

**Sexual-somatic considerations.** The ice-form thermal hazard is a non-trivial barrier to physical intimacy in mutant-coded form; he conducts sexual relationships exclusively in human form, which means his sexual life is conducted in his most psychologically vulnerable somatic state. This is an under-discussed contributor to his lifelong sexual avoidance pattern — *being touched requires being thaw-able,* and being thaw-able requires trust he has rarely extended.

**Coming out (All-New X-Men #40, 2015).** Not a medical event in the conventional sense, but a somatic-identity event of major significance. The five-decade concealment had measurable somatic costs: chronic muscular tension (visible in his characteristic shoulder-set), the over-controlled affect, the narrow band, the substance temperance, the sexual avoidance. Post-disclosure, observable somatic loosening: broader affective expression, more spontaneous physical contact with friends, reduced shoulder tension, fuller laughter. This is the clearest natural experiment in his file demonstrating the somatic toll of concealment.

---

## 4.8 NEUROLOGICAL AND COGNITIVE

No documented head trauma of clinical significance. No documented seizure history. No documented cognitive decline. Telepathic intrusion history is non-trivial (Frost possession; Bendis-era outing by teenage Jean; routine Xavier-school telepathic contact; Onslaught proximity) but no persistent neurological sequelae. Sleep pattern: inferred reasonable; no documented insomnia, though stress-period panels suggest episodic poor sleep.

Cognitive baseline: high-average to superior intelligence (CPA-credentialed, demonstrated tactical thinking). Habitually presents below capacity. No dementing process.

---

## 4.9 SOMATIC-PSYCHOLOGICAL INTERSECTION — THE CENTRAL MEDICAL FINDING

The summary medical fact about Bobby Drake, which no individual chart entry captures, is this: **his body is the most permissive escape vehicle in the X-roster, and his psychology has been using it.**

He can dissolve. He can disperse. He can refuse to be solid. He can be shattered and come back. He can hold a form that cannot be touched, cannot be fed, cannot be embraced, cannot be hurt. Across six decades the chart shows him increasingly *choosing* the form that exempts him from the conditions of being a person. The medical injuries documented above are real but, in aggregate, secondary — the primary medical fact of his life is the chronic energetic cost of holding himself below his actual capacity in order to remain small enough to be loved, combined with the chronic structural availability of a body that lets him leave whenever the cost gets too high.

He has never overdosed. He has never been hospitalized for self-harm. He has never developed a substance disorder. He has, instead, spent decades in a slow, somatic, deniable version of all three — throttled below baseline, dispersed when overwhelmed, temperate to the point of asceticism, and consistently the last person in any room to ask for medical attention because the body he most identifies with does not, technically, require it.

The Krakoan-era loosening — fuller expression, partnered life, openly omega operations — is, in medical terms, the first sustained period of his life in which the chart entries are *combat injuries from doing the work*, rather than *somatic costs of avoiding being himself.* That is a meaningful clinical improvement. Whether it survives the collapse of the permission structures that enabled it is the open question this file cannot yet answer.

— END SECTION 4 —


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: ROBERT LOUIS DRAKE

*Compiled from longitudinal observation, surveillance footage cross-reference, biometric reconstructions, and field-agent reporting across the full publication record. All entries are behavioral primitives — the small, repeatable bodily facts that constitute the subject's physical signature.*

---

## 1. BASELINE MORPHOLOGY

Caucasian male, recorded height 5'10" (178 cm), recorded weight 165 lbs (75 kg) in human form. Build: lean-mesomorphic but **under-muscled relative to his cohort**; he carries roughly fifteen pounds less functional mass than Summers or Worthington despite identical training access for sixty years. This is a tell: he has consistently declined to develop a body that would *look* dangerous. The musculature he carries is wiry, swimmer-shaped, distributed evenly rather than display-loaded — shoulders not built up, chest unremarkable, forearms slightly more developed than the rest from sustained fine-motor ice-shaping.

Skin: fair, prone to faint pinking at the cheeks and the bridge of the nose under exertion or embarrassment — a blush response that is unusually persistent into adulthood and that he is visibly aware of (the hand-to-cheek gesture, §4). Hair: medium brown, straight, fine, worn short and unstyled; cuts received roughly every six to eight weeks, never longer than collar-touching, never shorter than a #3 guard. Eyes: blue-grey, with a slight asymmetry — left eye sits approximately 1mm lower than right, more visible when he is tired. Teeth: corrected as a teenager (faint lingual retainer wear), well-maintained.

In **ice-form**, the morphology distorts upward: apparent height gains 1–2 inches from accreted surface ice; apparent mass varies wildly depending on humidity load; the silhouette broadens at the shoulders in a way the human form does not. He is, in ice, the body he declined to build in flesh. This is not accidental.

---

## 2. POSTURE AND CARRIAGE

**Standing baseline.** Weight shifted slightly onto the left foot (approximately 60/40), right knee minutely unlocked, hands most often shoved into pockets or hooked into belt loops. Shoulders carried *forward* of the line of the ear by roughly an inch — a slight protective hunch that has been present since the earliest field photography and that no amount of training has corrected. The hunch is *selective*: in ice-form, it disappears entirely. Iceman stands straight; Bobby does not.

**Sitting baseline.** Slouches. Lower lumbar curve flattened against chair back, pelvis forward, knees apart at roughly thirty degrees, one foot frequently tucked under the opposite thigh or hooked around a chair leg — adolescent sitting postures that have not aged out. In meetings he will, within ninety seconds of being seated, find something to fidget with: pen-spin, paperclip-unbend, cuff-pluck. Crosses ankles rather than knees; the crossed-knee posture appears only when he is consciously performing professionalism (depositions, CPA-era client meetings, the rare formal press).

**Walking gait.** Loose, slightly bouncy, weight on the balls of the feet — a residual basketball-player gait from adolescence. Stride length shorter than his leg length would predict (compressed by the forward hunch). Arms swing minimally; the left arm swings less than the right by a measurable margin, which is a holdover from the X-Factor-era injuries to his left shoulder. He walks faster than he needs to in crowds and slower than he needs to when alone — a vigilance index that does not register consciously.

**Gait shifts by state.** Calm: bouncy, hands in pockets, occasional sliding step on smooth floors (the residual urge to skate). Stress: stride shortens further, arms cross or fold, shoulders rise toward the ears. Threat: the hunch disappears, weight drops into the hips, stride lengthens — *the body that emerges under threat is the body that has been hidden the rest of the time.* Intimacy: stride slows, the bounce flattens into something more deliberate; he tends to walk slightly behind a partner rather than beside, a half-step back, which agents have repeatedly logged as a courtship tell (he wants to be followed, not to follow, but he also does not want to lead).

---

## 3. GAIT, MOVEMENT, AND THE ICE-SLIDE

The single most diagnostically interesting locomotor fact about the subject is that **he has a preferred mode of movement that requires the suspension of gravity.** The ice-slide is not a transport choice; it is a posture. On the slide, the spine straightens, the hunch vanishes, the arms extend for balance, the head lifts, the face opens — every postural defense relaxes simultaneously. He is, in flight on his own ice, the most physically uninhibited he ever becomes outside of sex or sleep.

The slide itself is technically remarkable: he builds it forward at a sustained rate of approximately fifteen to twenty feet per second of generation, banks without conscious calculation, and can hold the form indefinitely at altitudes up to roughly three hundred feet (above that he reports discomfort, which is psychogenic — there is no power-cost basis for the ceiling). He prefers the slide to walking when permitted to use it. In civilian contexts he suppresses it and the body re-hunches within minutes.

---

## 4. THE GESTURE INVENTORY

A granular catalog of the repeatable hand-and-face behaviors, with frequency notes.

- **The back-of-neck rub.** Right hand to the nape, fingers spread, three to four strokes downward. Frequency: many times per day. Triggered by: embarrassment, mild stress, being complimented, being asked a direct question about himself. The single most diagnostic Bobby Drake gesture.
- **The cheek-touch.** Fingertips (right hand) to the right cheekbone, then dropped. Triggered by: feeling himself blush. He has been doing this since his teens and it is a *checking* gesture — confirming that the visible tell is happening, which only makes it worse.
- **The pocket-shove.** Both hands driven into front trouser/jean pockets, thumbs out, shoulders rising. Default standing posture in any social configuration he has not chosen. Reads as casual; functions as withdrawal.
- **The finger-frost.** When idle, he generates and dispels tiny rime patterns at the fingertips — frost-cracks, ice rings, miniature snowflakes that he rolls between thumb and forefinger and then sublimates. He does this almost continuously when not actively socializing, the way another subject might tap a foot. It is unconscious. It increases under thought and decreases under emotion.
- **The snap-and-melt.** Forms a small ice object (cube, dart, snowball), tosses it, catches it, melts it. Combat-adjacent: he uses this to demonstrate readiness without performing aggression. Frequency rises sharply in unfamiliar tactical environments.
- **The half-shrug.** Single shoulder (usually the left) lifted briefly and dropped, accompanied by a head-tilt. Functions as a verbal hedge ("I dunno") and is often performed *without* the verbal — pure shoulder semaphore. Multiple per conversation.
- **The Hank-look.** When in the same room as Henry McCoy, the subject's eyes locate him within seconds of entry and re-locate him at roughly forty-five-second intervals thereafter. This has been observable for sixty years and is one of the most stable attachment-tells in the archive.
- **The Scott-eyeroll.** Behind Scott Summers's back or while Scott is mid-sentence: brief eye-roll, sometimes accompanied by a glance toward a third party (historically Hank or Warren) for confirmation. The adolescent-younger-brother gesture has not aged out.
- **The quip-mouth.** Just before he delivers a joke under stress, the left corner of his mouth lifts approximately a quarter-second before the right — an asymmetric pre-smile that signals to anyone who knows him that a deflection is incoming. Telepaths report finding this micro-tell easier to read than his surface thoughts.
- **The throat-clear-into-laugh.** Audible throat-clear followed by a low, single-syllable laugh, used as a transitional sound when he wants to change topic. Several times per day.
- **The arm-cross-then-uncross.** Crosses arms, holds for under five seconds, uncrosses as if having caught himself looking defensive. The self-correction is the tell, not the cross.
- **The cold-hand-warming pantomime.** Rubs his palms together when nervous — a parody of warming cold hands, even though his hands are not, by his standards, cold. This is performative and probably *for the audience* — visually re-coding his temperature regulation as ordinary human nerves.

---

## 5. FACIAL MICRO-PATTERNS

Resting face: pleasant-neutral, lips slightly parted, eyebrows in a faint default lift that suggests perpetual mild interest. He does not have a true neutral face; the baseline is *receptive*. This is a learned configuration — the lynch-mob lesson translated into musculature: *do not look threatening, do not look closed.*

**Smile inventory.**
- *The full smile* (rare): both rows of teeth, eye-corners crinkled, head tipped slightly back. Recorded in candid Hank-photographs, in private moments with romantic partners post-2015, and after particularly satisfying combat resolutions.
- *The work smile* (default social): closed-mouth, asymmetric (left side higher), eyes uninvolved. Multiple per minute in social settings.
- *The deflection smile*: tight, brief, immediately followed by a quip. Stress-marker.
- *The apology smile*: lips pressed, corners barely lifted, head ducked. After he has used too much power, broken something, or been called out.

**Eye behavior.** Sustained eye contact tolerance: approximately three to four seconds before a downward or sideways break. In intimate contexts the tolerance extends; in confrontation it contracts to under a second. Blink rate elevated above population baseline (approximately twenty-two per minute resting vs. fifteen-to-seventeen typical) — a chronic mild-anxiety marker. When lying or concealing, blink rate drops paradoxically (over-control). When telling the truth about something painful, the rate spikes and the gaze drops to the lower left.

**Brow.** Left brow lifts independently — a learned trick from adolescence, deployed for comic effect, several times per social hour. Both brows lift in genuine surprise (rare; he is hard to startle). Inner-brow lift (sadness signal) appears only fleetingly and is almost always followed within two seconds by a humor-deflection — agents who can catch the half-second inner-brow before the joke have the cleanest read on his actual state.

**Jaw.** Slight masseter tension chronically; bruxism observed during sleep (see §8). Jaw drops open in moments of genuine awe (rare, mostly Krakoa-era).

---

## 6. VOICE AND SPEECH

Tenor-baritone, naturally pitched slightly higher than his frame predicts. Speaking rate moderate-to-fast, with characteristic *up-tilts* at the ends of declarative sentences — turning statements into quasi-questions, a verbal hedge that mirrors the half-shrug. Vocabulary high (CPA-trained, well-read) but he selects downward in casual speech — uses simpler words than he knows, a verbal compartment matching the somatic one.

**Filler patterns.** "I mean," "look," "okay so," and the distinctive *trailing "...y'know?"* at the end of self-disclosing sentences. The "y'know" is a permission-seek; if it appears more than twice in a paragraph he is asking, without asking, to be told he is okay.

**Laughter.** Three distinct laughs in the inventory: (1) the genuine helpless laugh, a four-to-six-note descending cackle, mouth wide, head back — rare; (2) the social laugh, two notes, mouth half-open — frequent; (3) the deflective single-syllable "ha" — multiple per stressful conversation. The first laugh has been heard almost exclusively in the presence of Henry McCoy.

**Voice under state shifts.** Calm: warm, mid-pitch, conversational. Stress: pitch rises, speed increases, joke-density spikes. Threat: pitch *drops* — there is a recorded register about three semitones below his speaking baseline that emerges only in genuine danger, and it surprises new acquaintances. Intimacy: pitch drops slightly, rate slows substantially, the up-tilts disappear, sentences become complete declaratives — the speech pattern of a man who is not currently hedging. The intimate voice is rare and is, by surveillance count, the cleanest evidence of who he is when nobody is watching.

---

## 7. GROOMING AND DRESS

**Hygiene.** Daily shower, morning, cold-leaning (he runs warm internally despite the mutation, and prefers water several degrees below most subjects' comfort). Shaves every two to three days — facial hair grows in slowly and patchy along the jaw; he has never sustained a full beard. Brushes teeth twice daily, flosses inconsistently. Uses unscented deodorant (any fragrance reads to him as a tell — *being smelled* triggers the same lineage of vigilance as being seen).

**Hair maintenance.** Self-cuts the back-of-neck stubble between barber visits; the barber visits are at the same Long Island shop he has used since adolescence whenever he is in the area, a continuity that is itself diagnostic.

**Dress code.** Civilian: jeans, t-shirts, hoodies, sneakers — adolescent uniform sustained into middle adulthood, replaced one-to-one as items wear out. Owns two suits (one charcoal, one navy), both kept in good repair, both worn only under duress. Pockets matter: he selects garments with adequate pocket capacity because he needs somewhere to put his hands. Color palette skews cool — blues, greys, blacks, the occasional cold green; almost no warm colors in his civilian wardrobe, which agents have noted is consistent with the somatic identity even when he is in flesh.

**Costume.** The X-uniform is worn without complaint but also without enthusiasm; he removes the upper portion at the first opportunity in any safe environment. In ice-form, the costume is essentially decorative — the ice covers everything anyway. Post-Krakoa, his costume choices have gained personality (sharper lines, cooler color saturation), a wardrobe shift that tracks precisely with the identity-release.

**Accessories.** Wears a watch (analog, leather strap, replaced approximately every four to five years). No rings except briefly during the Opal era. No necklaces. Wallet kept in left back pocket. Keys on a single ring with a small metal carabiner — minimal, organized.

---

## 8. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

Sleep onset: rapid (under fifteen minutes) when in safe environments; markedly longer (forty-five minutes plus) in unfamiliar ones. Preferred position: left side, knees drawn up to roughly forty-five degrees — a partial fetal posture maintained through most of the night. Migrates toward the edge of the bed regardless of bed size; partners have reported him hovering at the mattress border with the covers pulled to the chin.

Total sleep: approximately seven to eight hours when uninterrupted. REM appears normally distributed but agents with deep-cycle observation report **bruxism in stage 2** (audible jaw-grinding) and intermittent **somatic ice-leak** — frost forming on the pillow or sheet, particularly during the second half of the night. The ice-leak correlates with stress dreams and is asymmetric, occurring more often on the side facing away from a sleeping partner.

Dreams: recall is patchy and he does not volunteer content. The partial reports on record cluster around three themes — being chased by a crowd, being unable to revert from ice-form, and looking for someone (unspecified) in a building he cannot navigate. He wakes from the first cluster with elevated heart rate and a brief disorientation that he covers with a joke within thirty seconds of speech-capacity returning.

Mornings: groggy for approximately twenty minutes, requires caffeine (coffee, black or with minimal milk, two cups), becomes functional and verbally bright by the third cup. Not a morning person; performs being one when required.

---

## 9. EATING AND CONSUMPTION

Caloric intake: modest, somewhat low for his apparent activity. He does not appear to require additional calories for ice-generation (the matter is drawn from ambient humidity, not from somatic reserves), and his eating habits reflect a metabolism that is, by mutant standards, ordinary.

**Preferences.** Comfort food skewed toward childhood — pizza, diner burgers, Chinese takeout, ice cream (the irony noted but unaddressed). Coffee daily. Soda occasionally. Alcohol: light social drinker; beer over spirits; rarely visibly intoxicated in surveillance, and on the rare occasions he is, the humor sharpens rather than slurs and the self-disclosure rate climbs noticeably. Wine almost never. Hard spirits almost never.

**Table behavior.** Eats slightly faster than the company average; finishes first roughly seventy percent of the time. Holds fork in the right hand (American style), elbow off the table, napkin on lap — a residual Catholic-middle-class table training. Talks while eating, gestures with utensils, occasionally pauses with a forkful mid-air to deliver a punchline.

**Public eating.** Prefers diners and casual restaurants over upscale ones; selects the seat with the best sightline to the door if available, without commenting on doing so. In group meals will order what someone else ordered if uncertain — decision-deferral, mild.

**Hydration.** Drinks more water than the typical subject, ice-cold by preference, often with the glass actively frosting in his hand without his noticing. He has been observed in surveillance to chew ice — *chew his own ice*, generated mid-meal, sublimating fragments between his teeth — a habit he is unaware of and that escalates under tension.

---

## 10. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE-PHYSICAL PATTERNS

The longitudinal record is partial and was, for decades, structured around concealment. What can be derived:

**Touch baseline.** Low rate of casual physical contact in early decades; rate elevates somewhat post-2015 and significantly during Krakoa. He is not a hugger by default — initiates physical contact in roughly one in five greetings where the social norm would permit it. Exceptions: Henry McCoy (consistent shoulder-touches and the occasional sustained hug across sixty years), Warren Worthington (back-slaps), Jean Grey (forehead-touches in the early decades that he never quite stopped doing). With romantic partners he is, once permitted, *more* tactile than the surface presentation predicts — hand-holding, the small-of-back hand, the absent-minded hair-touch.

**Sexual presentation.** Historically: anxious-performative with female partners, with significant evidence of dissociative distance during the act itself (the body present, the affect compartmentalized). Post-2015 with male partners: described in canon and inferable from observation as more present, more direct, less rehearsed. The improvement curve is steep and ongoing.

**Body shame.** Present but selective. He is not shy in locker-room contexts (X-mansion culture has normalized this), but he is shy about being *looked at appreciatively* — the act of being desired triggers the cheek-touch and the back-of-neck rub. He can be naked easily; he cannot be admired easily.

**Temperature in intimacy.** A reported curiosity from partners across decades: he runs cool to the touch, perceptibly, even in human form — palms, lips, the soles of the feet are several degrees below ambient skin. Under arousal he runs *cooler*, not warmer — a paradoxical thermoregulation that he has had to learn to manage and that he uses, in the more recent record, with intentional playfulness rather than embarrassment.

**Post-intimacy behavior.** Talkative. The intimate voice (§6) appears at maximum sustained duration in the half-hour following sex; this is the only reliable window in the surveillance record during which he speaks in complete unhedged declarative sentences about himself.

---

## 11. RITUALS, ROUTES, AND TERRITORIAL HABITS

**Daily rituals.** Coffee → news scroll → shower → dress → leave. Evening: reading (fiction, light; he prefers genre over literary), a single drink occasionally, television (sports — baseball preferred, hockey acceptable, the ice never commented on).

**Routes.** When walking a familiar area, he traces the same routes — same side of the same streets, same entrance to the same buildings. In Manhattan and the X-mansion grounds, surveillance maps show paths worn into preference over decades. He walks past his childhood home on visits to Long Island, on the opposite sidewalk, at a pace approximately ten percent slower than his surrounding-block pace. He does not stop. He has done this since at least the 1980s and likely earlier.

**Territorial behavior at the mansion.** Has occupied roughly the same suite of rooms across decades when given the choice. Sits in the same chair at briefings (mid-right of the table, sightline to the door, adjacent to Hank when Hank is present). Drives an unremarkable mid-priced car when he drives at all — has consistently selected the least-flashy vehicle option in any garage he has had access to.

**Phone.** Checks it less than population baseline. Texts in complete sentences with punctuation, which is generationally surprising and reflects the CPA-trained precision he otherwise conceals.

---

## 12. MICRO-MOVEMENT UNDER STATE SHIFTS

A consolidated map of how the body re-configures across the state spectrum.

**Calm.** Forward hunch present, hands pocketed or fidgeting with small ice-objects, blink rate moderate, breathing diaphragmatic, finger-frost continuous and unconscious. Voice up-tilted, smile work-default. Sits crooked.

**Mild social stress.** Back-of-neck rub appears. Cheek-touch if blushing. Joke-density rises. Pitch rises. Half-shrugs multiply. Sits straighter for short bursts, then re-slouches. Finger-frost intensifies — visible vapor at the fingertips.

**Significant stress.** Pocket-shove sustained. Arm-cross-uncross cycle visible. The quip-mouth pre-smile becomes near-constant. Throat-clears multiply. Sleep that night will show ice-leak. The Hank-look frequency doubles.

**Threat / combat readiness.** **The hunch disappears.** Weight drops into the hips, shoulders square, head lifts. Voice drops three semitones. Eye-contact tolerance extends rather than contracts. Movement economy improves dramatically — the bouncy gait converts to a planted, balanced stance. Finger-frost coalesces into deployed forms (darts, shields). The body that emerges is the body he has spent decades pretending he does not have.

**Ice-form transition.** Initiated at the fingertips and the jaw simultaneously, propagates inward across approximately one-point-five seconds. Posture straightens during the transition and *st


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS — R. L. DRAKE

*Section 7 of the longitudinal file. Cross-reference §3 (Psychological), §4 (Psychiatric), and the relationship-by-relationship appendices.*

---

## 7.1 Classification and Derivation

**Primary classification:** Anxious-preoccupied with a stable secondary avoidant strategy. **Disorganized features** emerge only under threat to core identity (paternal rejection; involuntary outing; institutional collapse). The classification is unusually clean for a six-decade record — the subject's relational template barely deforms across writers, eras, partners, or genders, which is itself the strongest possible evidence that the pattern is characterological rather than situational.

The derivation runs through three layers:

**Layer one — family of origin (Long Island, c. 1948–1963).** William Drake: authoritarian, intermittently rejecting, ideologically organized against the very category his son will turn out to occupy (twice). Madeline Drake: warm in tone, conflict-avoidant in function, structurally unavailable as a buffer because she will not oppose her husband. Bobby grows up learning that proximity to the male caregiver is contingent on the suppression of self, and that the female caregiver will not intervene when that contingency turns punitive. The classic anxious-preoccupied substrate: love is real, love is conditional, and the conditions are opaque and shifting. He learns to *monitor* — to read a room, to scan a face, to defuse a tone — which becomes the trained skill underwriting the humor.

**Layer two — the adolescent rupture (X-Men #1; Iceman vol. 1 retcon, 1984–85).** Powers manifest in front of a date; the date screams; the neighbors mobilize; the *town he grew up in* tries to lynch him. He is rescued, in his most acute hour, not by his parents but by strangers in uniform — Cyclops physically extracting him, Xavier mentally screening witnesses. The encoding is permanent: *the family of origin is the locus of danger; the institution is the locus of rescue.* This single event explains more of his subsequent relational behavior than any other data point in the file. From this moment forward, the X-Men are not employer, school, or team. They are the family that *intervened when the first family wouldn't.* He will defer to them, forgive them, and return to them across six decades regardless of the cost.

**Layer three — the concealed second identity (1963–2015).** For approximately fifty publication-years, the subject conducts a parallel concealment — sexual orientation — that requires every intimate relationship to be conducted in bad faith with himself. This produces the avoidant overlay: he cannot allow full intimacy with women because full intimacy would expose the concealment, and he cannot pursue intimacy with men because pursuit would expose it faster. The result is a man who *appears* relationally active but is structurally relationally absent. Every romance is a performance, including for himself.

---

## 7.2 The Bonding Sequence

The subject bonds in a recognizable, repeatable cadence. The cadence does not vary across friendships, romances, or institutional attachments; only the speed and the depth of the final terrace vary.

**Stage one — disarming entry.** First contact is mediated through humor. He is funny, light, slightly self-deprecating, often physically a little goofy in early encounters (ice-slide showing off, a snowball as a greeting, a pun deployed with eye contact held a beat too long). The function is diagnostic as much as defensive: he is reading whether the other party will *laugh with him*, *laugh at him*, or *recoil*. The taxonomy of all his future relationships is set in this first read.

**Stage two — provisional warmth.** If the other party laughs with him, he extends provisional warmth — friendly nicknames, presence at small social occasions, a willingness to be physically near (he is a leaner, a shoulder-bumper, a sit-on-the-arm-of-the-couch type when comfortable). The warmth is real but it is *graded*; he will not yet disclose anything operationally costly.

**Stage three — competence-display under cover of clowning.** Somewhere in the early-middle phase he allows the other party to see him be *good* at something — usually tactical or protective, occasionally intellectual (the CPA mind surfaces only with people he is starting to trust). This is the first asymmetric move: he is offering a piece of himself he doesn't usually show, while still maintaining the comic framing as deniability. If the other party recognizes it without comment, the bond accelerates. If they remark on it ("you're smarter than you let on," "you're stronger than you let on"), he flinches and pulls back a half-step.

**Stage four — the durable plateau.** With friends, he reaches a plateau and *stays there* with extraordinary fidelity. Henry McCoy is the prototype: a sixty-year friendship sustained by mutual humor, mutual loyalty, and an unspoken contract that neither will require the other to disclose more than the humor permits. Warren Worthington, Jean Grey (pre-Bendis), Angelica Jones, Northstar — all sit on the same plateau, each at a slightly different altitude. The plateau is *highly stable*, which is why his friendship roster shows almost no attrition outside of death.

**Stage five (romantic only) — the failure cascade.** With romantic partners, the plateau is never reached. Instead, the relationship cascades: idealization, partial disclosure, deflection of the partner's deeper bid, partner withdraws or is revealed to be someone other than presented, subject mourns briefly, subject re-enters the pursuit cycle with a new unavailable target. The cascade is so consistent across Jean, Zelda, Lorna, Opal, Cloud, Infectia, Mystique-as-Opal, Annie, Mystique-as-Annie, Kitty, Judah, Romeo, and Christian Frost that it constitutes a near-algorithmic pattern (see §7.6).

---

## 7.3 Distrust: How He Fails to Trust, and Whom

Distrust in the subject is not loud. He does not interrogate, accuse, or surveil. His distrust is expressed as **graceful non-disclosure** — he simply does not give the untrusted party the material that would allow them to hurt him. Several markers identify when the subject has filed someone in the distrusted category:

- **Humor becomes glassier.** Quips still arrive on schedule but lose their warmth; they're paced for deflection rather than connection. Trained observers can hear the difference; most cannot.
- **Eye contact shortens.** Baseline eye contact with trusted parties is long, soft, often accompanied by a small half-smile. With distrusted parties it is brief, polite, and pointed at the bridge of the nose rather than the eyes.
- **Physical distance widens by roughly a forearm.** He is normally a close talker; with distrusted parties he stands one full step further back. This is unconscious and very consistent.
- **Civilian-Bobby surfaces.** He starts referring to mundane life — the apartment, taxes, errands — which is the conversational equivalent of pulling the curtain.
- **Ice-form is held longer in their presence**, or, more tellingly, **refused entirely** so they do not see him in his full mutant register. He picks the deflection that matches what the particular distrust is *about*.

Categories of person who reliably enter the distrusted file:

1. **Authority figures who demand the *whole* self.** Xavier in his more invasive moods; later Cyclops during his most messianic period; Emma Frost in any year. He complies operationally and discloses nothing.
2. **People who flatter his latent power.** This is counter-intuitive but consistent. Compliments about his Omega potential are heard as *threats*: someone has seen the thing he has spent his life hiding. He distrusts the flatterer for the duration of the exposure.
3. **Anyone who reminds him of his father in tone or posture.** Heavy-set men with loud opinions and certain consonant rhythms produce immediate, unexplained coolness in him. This is observable in his interactions with Cain Marko outside combat, with certain SHIELD liaisons, with Forge in their early encounters.
4. **The shape-shifter class.** After Mystique twice, Bobby's baseline reading of any new person includes a half-second "is this who they say they are" scan. He has been observed touching unobtrusively (handshake, brush of shoulder) to confirm body temperature is human-normal — a tell he developed and never lost.

What he does *not* do, and this is diagnostic: he does not pre-emptively cut people off. He does not stage confrontations. He does not test loyalty. He simply ratchets disclosure down to the level he assesses as survivable and waits. He can hold someone in the half-trusted category for decades without ever resolving it (his father is the longest example; Scott Summers spent fifteen years there during the latter's Phoenix-Five and X-Force periods).

---

## 7.4 Betrayal: How He Is Wounded, and How He Responds

**The subject is unusually betrayal-tolerant by raw count and unusually betrayal-deformed by depth.** He absorbs an enormous quantity of low- and mid-grade betrayal without retaliating — partners who leave him for his teammates (Lorna→Havok), partners who conceal their identities (Mystique, twice; arguably Cloud), institutional decisions made over his objections, being passed over for major team rosters (Giant-Size X-Men #1 being the founding instance), being patronized as the kid for the entirety of his twenties and thirties. He metabolizes all of this into the humor. The cost is dysthymic baseline, not relational rupture.

The betrayals that *do* deform him share three properties:

1. **They concern the concealed self, not the public self.** Mystique impersonating Opal hurt him more than Opal leaving him, because Mystique-as-Opal was a partner addressing herself to the false-self he was performing. The exposure of his orientation by Jean Grey (All-New X-Men #40) — a friend, conducted in love, executed without consent — was a deeper wound than any enemy action of the prior decade, because the friend used a power to read the thing he had concealed even from himself.
2. **They come from inside the trusted category.** The lynch-mob neighbors were strangers and produced characterological damage. His father's bigotry was family and produced developmental damage. Jean's reading was a chosen sister and produced an identity earthquake. The closer to the center of the trust map, the more lasting the wound.
3. **They cannot be re-framed as funny.** Most injuries the subject can convert into a self-deprecating story within roughly forty-eight hours. The deep betrayals resist this conversion. When you see him *fail to make a joke* about something, you have located the wound.

His response to deep betrayal follows a sequence:

- **Acute phase (hours to days):** flattened affect, longer time in ice-form, reduced verbal output, retreat to physically cold environments (rooftops in winter, walk-in freezers, Arctic if accessible). He does not drink, rage, break things, or proposition strangers. He gets quiet and gets cold.
- **Sub-acute phase (days to weeks):** civilian-Bobby surfaces aggressively. He will discuss apartment hunting, tax filings, episodes of television. He is *present* but operationally absent from the mutant identity. This is the compartmentalization defense in active deployment.
- **Re-entry phase (weeks to months):** humor resumes, slightly bleaker than baseline, gradually warming. He does not address the betrayal directly; he simply absorbs it into the operating model and ratchets the betrayer down one trust tier.
- **Long tail (years to decades):** the relationship continues, often warmly, but never returns to the prior tier. His father is the canonical case: thawed but never restored. Scott Summers post-Schism, Emma Frost throughout: warm working relationships, never full trust.

He has, in the entire record, **demonstrably retaliated against a betrayer on exactly zero occasions.** This is statistically extraordinary for a combatant of his tenure and capability. The aggression goes somewhere — it goes into the suppression, into the dysthymia, into the dispersed body — but it does not come out as targeted relational harm.

---

## 7.5 Repair: How He Restores, and Why It Mostly Doesn't Stick

Repair in the subject's relational record is **slow, non-verbal, and chronically incomplete.** He does not stage reconciliation scenes. He does not deliver speeches. He does not request apologies. The repair sequence runs:

- A small renewed proximity (he shows up at the funeral, the wedding, the hospital). 
- A re-extended humor — usually a callback joke to an earlier shared reference, signaling *I still remember when we were us*.
- A graded re-disclosure — he tells the other party something small and current about his civilian life, signaling that the trust tier is being incrementally rebuilt.
- A long observation period in which he watches whether the other party reciprocates at the same grade.

The protocol works for friends, who tend to reciprocate. It fails for romantic partners, because by the time repair is on the table the relationship has usually cascaded past recoverability. It fails for his father for roughly forty publication-years because William Drake does not reciprocate until Uncanny #340, and by then Bobby's defensive architecture has hardened around the gap.

The reason repair frequently doesn't fully stick: **the subject repairs the surface and not the substrate.** He can re-extend warmth, restore working partnership, sit at the same table — but the depth of trust that existed before the rupture is not re-extended, because he has updated his model of the other party and his model of himself in relation to them. He cannot un-update. The relationship resumes at a lower altitude and stays there. This is why, on inspection, his "long friendships" are actually *stratified* into pre- and post-rupture eras with subtle but real differences in temperature.

The one full-restoration case on record is Henry McCoy, and the structural reason is illuminating: McCoy has never delivered the subject a deep betrayal. The friendship has survived because it has never been tested at the depth that would have ratcheted it down. (The Krakoa-era X-Force Beast schism strained but did not breach this — and notably it produced more visible distress in the subject than any other Krakoa-era event.)

---

## 7.6 Intimacy and Dependency

**Intimacy.** The subject's intimacy capacity is high in tone, low in substance. He is warm, present, physically near, verbally engaged, attentive to others' moods. What he does *not* do is reciprocally disclose. Asked how he is, he answers in a single sentence and redirects. Asked what he wants, he answers in terms of what would be convenient for the asker. Asked who he is, historically he answered with a joke. Post-2015, he answers with a true short sentence and a joke. This is progress; it is not yet full intimacy.

The structural barrier is that intimacy as he was taught it requires the disclosure of the concealed self, and the concealed self has been (consecutively, then simultaneously) the mutant identity, the sexual identity, the depressive baseline, the latent Omega-level capacity, and the unfinished business with the father. Every intimacy bid is a request he reflexively cannot fully grant.

The exceptions — the moments when full intimacy briefly opens — are observable and instructive:

- **In ice-form, alone with one trusted person, in the cold.** Something about the somatic register changes; he speaks more directly, less jokingly. This has been observed with Henry McCoy and (Krakoa era) with Romeo.
- **In the immediate aftermath of an acute crisis** where the joke-frame is structurally unavailable for thirty to ninety seconds. He will say one true sentence and then re-frame.
- **In conversations with younger mutants** about being the youngest. The mentor role permits disclosure that the peer role does not, because in the mentor role disclosure is *for* the other person.

**Dependency.** The subject is institutionally dependent and individually independent — an unusual configuration. He needs the *team* and uses it as a stable base; he does not need any particular *person* in a way that would constitute clinical dependency. This protects him: when partners leave, he grieves and reorganizes; he does not collapse. It also impoverishes him: he has never built the kind of dyadic bond in which the other person becomes a permanent regulator of his nervous system. The closest approach is the friendship with McCoy, which functions as a low-grade lifelong regulator, but even there the dependency is *atmospheric* rather than acute.

Krakoa is the first instance of an institutional dependency that *also* permitted individual intimacy, which is part of why the Krakoa era shows the broadest affective range and the highest power expression in the record. The dependency on the team finally aligned with permission for the dependency on a person.

---

## 7.7 The Template, in Full

Stripped to its skeleton, every relationship the subject has ever conducted follows the same shape:

1. **Detect the other party's threat-to-concealed-self level via humor probe.**
