- **Geographic drift.** Moves toward windows, doorways, balconies, rooflines. Will excuse himself to "get some air" with notable regularity. Air is real and welcome; the door is also a calculation.
- **Defers more readily to Cyclops in tactical settings while sniping more freely at him in social ones.** This is paradoxical only if one misreads the dynamic: tactical deference is comfort; social sniping is the safety valve.
- **Phone use increases.** The scroll becomes a screen — literal and metaphorical — through which he processes the room.
- **Sleep degrades first.** Even before mood drops measurably, the sleep degrades. Roommates report longer pre-sleep latency, more night waking, more sleep-talk.

---

## 3. ACUTE STRESS (significant but non-life-threatening)

### Pre-coming-out era (catalog through ~2015)

A predictable cascade unfolds across roughly two to seventy-two hours:

1. **Hour 0–2.** Humor at its sharpest and brittlest. The jokes are still landing but the eyes are no longer participating. The late-orbital tell becomes a *no*-orbital tell.
2. **Hour 2–12.** Verbal output *drops* — the first major inversion from the low-stress pattern. He goes quiet in groups, lingers at edges, takes longer alone-walks. Ice-form usage increases for ambient reasons: he "just feels like it." This is dissociative drift, not preference.
3. **Hour 12–48.** Compartment-Bobby surfaces. The civilian register comes forward: he will spontaneously bring up accounting, tax season, mortgage rates, things from his college-age normalcy fantasy. To trained observers this is alarming; to casual ones it reads as harmless banter. It is *not* harmless. The civilian register is the door he uses when the mutant-self becomes unbearable.
4. **Hour 48–72.** If unaddressed, somatic dissociation: prolonged ice-form, sleeping in ice-form, reluctance to revert. Affect flattens. Snark thins. He stops eating in front of others.

### Post-coming-out era (~2015–present)

The cascade still occurs but with a meaningful new variable: he is more likely to *name it* at hour 2–12 to a small trusted circle. Naming foreshortens the cascade. Stage 3 (civilian-register intrusion) and stage 4 (somatic dissociation) appear less often and less severely. This is not cure; it is harm reduction. Under sufficient compound stress (Krakoa's fall, paternal contact, romantic rupture) the full cascade still runs.

### Decision habits under acute stress

- **Risk-tolerance drops, not rises.** Counter-stereotypical for combat operatives. Subject becomes *more* conservative in tactical proposals under acute stress, *less* willing to commit to high-leverage maneuvers, more likely to volunteer for support rather than spearhead roles. The exception, important: when stress is *interpersonal-shame-coded* (someone has seen too much), risk-tolerance briefly spikes upward in a self-punitive register — he will take the dangerous flank, the long jump, the unnecessary exposure. Read: *if you saw me, let me prove I'm useful enough to deserve the seeing.*
- **Authority-deference deepens.** He looks to Cyclops, Storm, or in the Krakoan era the Quiet Council, for permission to do things he could decide alone. The deference is regressive; it is the eighteen-year-old in the holding cell waiting to be told what happens next.
- **Mentorship behavior becomes more reliable, not less.** Acute personal stress paradoxically *improves* his attentiveness to younger mutants — he locates a person smaller than himself in the configuration and stabilizes them, which stabilizes him. Documented across New Mutants, Generation X, Hellions, and Krakoan classroom rotations.

---

## 4. THREAT / COMBAT

### Pre-engagement (the last thirty seconds)

- Verbal output spikes briefly — one or two quips, often pre-rehearsed-feeling, sometimes recycled across battles. The quips function as breath-control and as a pre-emptive claim on the social register of the encounter: *this is not serious, I am not afraid, I am still the kid.*
- Ice-form transition begins at the extremities and travels inward — fingertips, forearms, then torso. The transition is faster than it used to be (by Krakoan era, near-instantaneous; in early-career, visibly progressive over 2–4 seconds). The slower legacy transition is a *choice* — performance of effort, performance of limit — that he has largely stopped making.
- Stance widens, weight centers, shoulders square. The spatial modesty drops. In combat the Subject *occupies* his volume; out of combat he does not.
- Eye contact with allies becomes brief and tactical; eye contact with the threat becomes prolonged and unblinking. The orbital muscles relax — he stops smiling with the mouth.

### In combat

- **Mercy as default.** First strikes are reliably non-lethal: encasement, slicks, immobilization, ice walls between combatants. He prefers to neutralize rather than destroy. Lethal-capacity strikes occur only under (a) immediate civilian endangerment, (b) explicit team authorization, or (c) the throttle-release condition (see §10). The mercy is principled, not squeamish — he has the capacity; he is choosing.
- **Humor as combat tool.** Continuous low-rate quipping at threats, even silent ones. This is not affect; it is rhythm-keeping, a metronome that paces his own breath and disrupts the opponent's.
- **Spatial generosity to allies.** Tracks teammate positions with high accuracy; ice walls reliably arrive *between* threat and ally rather than collapsing onto either. He is the most reliable shield-thrower on any team he has served on — measurably better than self-described tanks at preventing collateral injury.
- **Underuse of full capacity.** He throttles in combat by default. The throttle is so consistent that experienced opponents have learned to read his power level by *what he does not do*: no continental ice fields, no sub-zero atmospheric drops, no molecular ice reconstitution. The omissions are the tell. When the omissions stop (see §10), the engagement has changed category.
- **Verbal check-ins.** Will call out to specific teammates at irregular intervals — by name, briefly. The check-ins are attachment maintenance under threat: confirming the family is still there.

### Post-engagement (the first ten minutes after)

- Reverts to human form quickly — faster than tactically necessary — unless the throttle-release occurred, in which case the reversion is *slow*, embarrassed, and accompanied by self-deprecating cleanup talk ("sorry about the, uh, glacier").
- Seeks Henry McCoy first if McCoy is present; otherwise Worthington, otherwise Grey. The triage order has been stable for sixty years.
- Eats. Substantial caloric intake within thirty minutes of significant engagement. The post-combat appetite is real (thermokinetic metabolic load) and also a comfort behavior.
- Tells jokes about what happened. The jokes are the metabolization. If he is *not* joking within ten minutes of combat end, something is wrong; this is a Stage 3+ indicator.

---

## 5. INTIMACY

### Emotional intimacy (non-sexual)

- **Approach pattern: oblique.** He does not sit across from someone for a difficult conversation; he sits beside them, facing the same direction — on a roof, on a couch, on the edge of a Krakoan gate platform. The shared sight-line displaces the social pressure of the eye-line.
- **Disclosure pattern: humor-buffered.** Substantive emotional disclosures are reliably preceded and followed by a joke. The joke is the bumper. Listeners who pause inside the bumper to take the disclosure seriously will trigger a brief withdrawal (~5–15 seconds) before the Subject re-engages; experienced intimates (McCoy especially) have learned to receive the disclosure without breaking the comedic frame and to reflect it back inside the frame.
- **Touch tolerance: high with trusted intimates, low with new.** Initiates touch with McCoy, Worthington, Grey, Jones-Pyne, Northstar (post-Krakoa), and adopted younger mutants. Receives touch from these without flinch. With newer or uncalibrated parties, initial touch produces a half-degree lean-away and a temperature drop.
- **Listening posture: excellent.** When *receiving* disclosure from others, the deflection drops entirely. He is one of the better listeners on the team, ranked by frequency of long-form one-on-one solicitation by younger mutants. His own deflection is asymmetric — he applies it to himself, not to others.

### Sexual intimacy

- **Approach pattern (historical, with women): pursuit of the unavailable.** The pattern is the most over-determined in the file. Targets were reliably (a) involved with another (Grey/Summers; Polaris/Havok; Pryde/various), (b) deceptive about identity (Mystique-as-Opal; Mystique-as-Annie; Infectia), or (c) structurally unavailable for other reasons (Cloud's gender-fluidity; Opal's family). The pursuit was real; the unavailability was the point. Unavailable partners cannot demand the disclosure that would have ended the relationship.
- **Approach pattern (post-coming-out, with men): pursuer, not rejected.** Shift in role rather than in pace. Relationships have been short but qualitatively different — initiated by him, ended by circumstance more than by his sabotage, marked by greater honesty inside their short runs.
- **Physical intimacy tells.** Slight ambient temperature drop is involuntary and *intensifies under arousal* — partners have remarked. He has trained partial suppression; full suppression is impossible. The temperature drop is, in practice, a reliable consent-state indicator that cannot be faked.
- **Post-intimacy behavior.** Talkative. The post-coital register is one of the few in which he leads with substantive content rather than with humor. Diagnostically: sexual intimacy is one of the few states that reliably suspends the deflection.

### Family intimacy

- **With Madeline Drake (mother).** Phone calls weekly to biweekly historically; longer gaps in periods of acute mutant-political stress (he calls less when the news is worse, to spare her). Calls run short, content domestic. Pre-coming-out, the calls were carefully edited; post-coming-out, marginally less so but still curated. He has never asked her directly whether she defended him to his father.
- **With William Drake (father).** The most diagnostically loaded relationship in the file. Pre-Friends-of-Humanity assault (1996): contact rare, hostile, ritualized. Post-assault: contact more frequent but no less brittle. Post-coming-out: contact collapses, partially recovers, never normalizes. Subject drafts and discards messages to his father at high rates. Phone calls with William produce hour-long silences afterward in which Subject does not joke. This silence is one of the most reliable William-contact tells.

---

## 6. GRIEF

### Acute grief (recent loss)

- **First 24 hours: high function, low affect.** He works. He helps. He cleans. He volunteers for logistical tasks no one else wants. The function is a defense; do not mistake it for resilience.
- **First 72 hours: humor returns but mis-calibrated.** Jokes land oddly, sometimes inappropriately, occasionally hurting bystanders. He is using the deflection at insufficient resolution. Trusted intimates have learned not to reprimand the misfires; they pass.
- **First two weeks: somatic-dissociative drift.** Prolonged ice-form during off-hours, especially while sleeping. Reluctance to revert in the morning. Cold-ambient bubble around him expands from ~1m to ~3m unconsciously.
- **First month: civilian-Bobby surfaces strongly.** Spreadsheets, taxes, mortgage talk, structured tasks. The compartment provides a non-grieving identity to occupy while the grieving one metabolizes.
- **Months 2–6: stabilization, integration, late-arriving jokes about the lost party.** The capacity to joke *about* the loss, rather than *around* it, marks late-stage integration. When he can name the lost in a quip without flinching, the metabolization is largely complete.

### Anticipatory grief (knowing a loss is coming)

He is poor at this. Anticipatory grief activates the throttle-suppression *more* aggressively, not less; he becomes smaller, funnier, more present, more eager to *not be the problem*. The work of pre-mourning is largely deferred and then collapses into acute grief at the actual loss.

### Grief over identity-loss (his own, internal)

The most under-recognized grief category in the Subject. He has grieved several versions of himself across his life — the boy who could have stayed in his hometown, the husband he never became, the man he might have been if he had come out at twenty rather than fifty. This grief is chronic, low-grade, and almost never named. It surfaces as an unprovoked, three-second far-look during otherwise unrelated activities, after which he resumes whatever he was doing without comment. The far-look has been documented across every era; the frequency does not diminish with time.

---

## 7. VICTORY

Victory is one of the most uncomfortable states for the Subject and produces the most diagnostically useful behavioral data.

- **Immediate response: self-deprecation.** Within seconds of a successful operation, he will produce a comment that diminishes his own contribution, redistributes credit to teammates, or jokes about the property damage. The self-deprecation is reflexive and pre-conscious.
- **Receipt of praise: deflection.** Praise is received with an eye-flick down-and-left, a half-smile, and a redirection ("yeah, well, Hank did the math"). Sustained praise produces visible discomfort: temperature drop, postural retreat, occasionally a sudden need to leave the room.
- **Celebration behavior: high social participation, low personal celebration.** He attends the party, refills others' drinks, plays bartender or DJ, mediates micro-conflicts, leaves early. He has never, in the recorded archive, raised a toast to himself.
- **Private response to victory: muted.** Alone after a win, he does not exhibit observable euphoria. He cleans, he calls his mother (sometimes), he sleeps. The win is processed at the same affective volume as a draw.
- **Compound victory (a win that also vindicates his power-scale): destabilizing.** When the operation required, and received, an unthrottled expression of capacity, the victory produces *more* discomfort than a marginal one. He apologizes more, withdraws more, joke-pattern misfires more. The unthrottled-victory cascade resembles a mild grief response. This is the single most counterintuitive feature of the Subject's profile and one of the most important.

---

## 8. DEFEAT

Defeat is, paradoxically, a more comfortable state than victory — the Subject has more practice with it.

- **Immediate response: ownership.** He takes responsibility quickly, sometimes too quickly, including for failures not properly his. The over-ownership is the inverse of the under-credit-taking in victory; both are managed through the same schema (*be small, be safe*).
- **Tactical post-mortem: lucid.** He is one of the better after-action analysts on any team he has served on, and the lucidity holds in defeat. His honesty about his own performance is unusually high; he does not protect his ego in debriefs.
- **Affective response: muted but durable.** Sadness rather than rage. Sustained low affect for days to weeks. No outbursts. The defeat is metabolized internally over a long arc.
- **Relational response: increased loyalty.** Teams that lose with him do not lose him. He stays. The defeat is, for him, a credential of belonging — *I was there when it went wrong, I did not leave.*
- **


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DOSSIER SECTION — DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

**Subject:** Robert Louis Drake
**Section purpose:** what a seven-day continuous surveillance window would actually record — the granular texture of how the subject occupies hours, places, and objects. Compiled across the documented residential phases (Westchester dorm 1963–69; Los Angeles bachelor apartment Champions era; X-Factor brownstone/Ship; Westchester staff era; post-M-Day itinerant; Manhattan solo apartment Iceman vol. 3; Krakoa residence; post-Krakoa return to mainland). Patterns that recur across three or more of these phases are treated as stable; phase-specific observations are flagged.

---

## 1. THE SHAPE OF A DAY

### Waking

Subject is a **reluctant early riser** — not by preference but by an internalized institutional clock set at the Xavier School in adolescence and never reset. Wakes between 06:10 and 06:40 across all residential phases for which behavioral data exists. On the rare day he sleeps past 07:30, surveillance should treat it as a soft indicator of depressive episode onset rather than indulgence — confirmed across the post-Opal weeks (X-Factor era), the weeks following the Bendis-era outing, and the early Iceman solo run.

The waking sequence itself is **somatically diagnostic.** Subject sleeps in human form. On waking, before any motor activity, there is a brief observable pause — three to eight seconds — in which he verifies, by proprioception, that he is still discrete and continuous. This is not conscious. It is the residue of having been shattered, melted, vaporized, and reformed across his career; the body checks the body before the day begins. Then he sits up, runs a hand through his hair (consistent gesture across decades), and the day starts.

He does not snooze the alarm. He does not linger. The bed is made within ninety seconds of standing — corners squared, not military-tight but deliberate. This is one of several **small order-keeping rituals** that read at first as personality and on second look as compartment-maintenance: the civilian space must be reset before the mutant day begins.

### Ablutions

Showers in lukewarm water trending cool. Never hot. Hot water on his skin produces a faint but reliable physiological discomfort — not because of any thermoregulatory pathology but because heat is, semiotically, the opposite of him; he flinches from it the way a fair-skinned subject flinches from direct sun. He has admitted this exactly once in canon (Iceman solo, offhand to Judah). The shower is short — six to nine minutes. He sings in it occasionally; surveillance audio would catch fragments of 1980s pop and the occasional show tune, the latter increasing in frequency post-2015.

Shaves daily with a manual razor. The shave is brisk and unceremonious. He keeps the face he had at twenty-five because his cellular biology lags, but the **act of shaving is preserved as ritual** because it asserts adulthood against a face that does not. Surveillance would note: he checks the mirror for longer than the shave requires. He is not vain. He is verifying — again — that the person in the mirror is the person he expects.

Teeth: brushed twice daily, flossed once, dental hygiene unremarkable but consistent. He has, on record, a slight overbite. He smiles closed-mouth in photographs and open-mouthed only when caught mid-laugh — a small vanity that contradicts the larger pattern of not-being-seen and is therefore noteworthy.

### Dress

**Civilian wardrobe is aggressively unremarkable.** Jeans or chinos; t-shirt or henley; hoodie or zip fleece; sneakers. Color palette weighted toward navy, grey, olive, faded blue — the wardrobe of a man who does not want to be the most-looked-at person in any room. He owns one suit at any given time, dark, cut conservatively; replaces it every five to seven years; uses it for funerals, IRS appointments (Champions/X-Factor era when CPA work was active), and the rare formal X-event.

Two phase-specific exceptions:

- **Post-coming-out (2015–present):** wardrobe slowly opens. Brighter colors appear — a coral t-shirt, a yellow hoodie, a pair of patterned socks. Surveillance should treat each new chromatic addition as a developmental data point. The change is real but incremental; he is not flamboyant, he is *permitted*.
- **Krakoa residence:** wears the issued Krakoan garments without resistance and, in private, frequently shirtless or in shorts — the only documented phase in which he is consistently relaxed about his body in shared space.

Notable: **he owns more sweaters than the average resident of his climates would require.** This is not because he is cold (he is not; he is the opposite of cold) but because the sweater is camouflage — it makes the body look ordinary, occupied, soft. The sweater is part of the not-being-seen apparatus.

### Breakfast

Eats breakfast every day. This is rare among the X-roster and consistent with the over-controlled cluster identified in the psychological workup. Standard rotation: coffee (black, two cups, never decaf), one of {cereal, toast with peanut butter, eggs on weekdays when domestic, a bagel when in Manhattan}. He prefers cold cereal in a way that has outlasted three decades of nutritional fashion. The cereal of record across multiple appearances is a sugared American brand; he eats it without irony.

Coffee preparation is **the day's first ritual of pleasure.** He grinds beans when the kitchen allows it. He pours the first cup and stands at the window for ninety seconds to two minutes before sitting. Surveillance would record this stillness as the most reliably repeated non-functional behavior in his day. It is the only window in which he is *not* performing for anyone, including himself.

Reads news on a phone or tablet over the second cup. Scans headlines, lingers on weather (occupational hazard), skips politics quickly, reads sports (Mets, Knicks, Rangers — Long Island childhood loyalty, never updated), reads one human-interest piece, closes the device. He is not a deep news consumer. He is a man who wants to know what the temperature is doing and who won.

---

## 2. WORK PATTERNS

### The two careers

For roughly twenty publication-years, subject maintained a **functioning parallel civilian career as a CPA.** This is not trivia; it is the operational expression of the compartmentalization defense. Surveillance during the Champions and early X-Factor years would document:

- A small client list — sole proprietors, restaurants, a dental practice, two nonprofits. He preferred clients who needed him quarterly, not constantly.
- Tax season produced observable behavioral change: longer hours at the desk, more coffee, fewer team check-ins, an uncharacteristic irritability that he masked badly. He resented the season but kept the work because the work kept the compartment.
- He filed his own returns on the last permissible day every year. A small recurring rebellion against the profession he had chosen.
- His workspace was *meticulous.* Receipts categorized, ledgers squared, pencils sharpened. The civilian compartment was the only space in his life he was permitted to make orderly without apology.

The CPA practice has been allowed to lapse and resume across eras. In its dormant phases, the **compulsion to keep order migrates** — to the team's logistics, to apartment maintenance, to small administrative tasks no one asked him to do. Surveillance should note: if Bobby Drake is in a household, the recycling is sorted, the dishwasher is run on schedule, and someone has paid the utility bill. He does not announce this. He just does it.

### X-Men operational work

In active team phases, the day's middle hours (roughly 09:00–17:00) are occupied by some combination of: Danger Room sessions (he attends consistently but rarely pushes to his ceiling — see psychological workup §3.2 on self-throttling), training younger mutants (a role he is unexpectedly good at and visibly enjoys), mission briefings, and downtime he treats as work because the alternative is unstructured time.

**Danger Room signature:** he runs the same three or four routines repeatedly. He has access to advanced scenarios and chooses intermediate ones. He completes them efficiently and leaves. When forced into harder scenarios (by Cyclops, by Emma, by Wolverine in various eras), his performance jumps disproportionately, which is logged and forgotten by the subject within a week. The Danger Room is the laboratory in which the throttling pattern is most cleanly observable on camera.

**Mentoring signature:** when teaching younger mutants, he becomes a different operator. Patient, specific, funny in a less defensive register, willing to demonstrate techniques at a level he refuses to use in combat. Surveillance would note that he is *most fully himself* when he is the older one in the room — the only context that fully inverts the original-team kid-brother dynamic that has otherwise shaped him.

### Solo / civilian phases (Iceman solo, post-Krakoa)

When operating without team structure, his work day defaults to **self-imposed patrol routines.** Walks specific neighborhoods on specific days. Long Island circuits during the solo book. Manhattan grid during the post-Krakoa returns. The patrols are not assigned. He invents them and adheres to them because the structure substitutes for the institutional scaffolding he otherwise relies on.

---

## 3. PLACE, ROUTE, RITUAL

### Habits of place

Subject has a documented preference for **edge-spaces** — windows, balconies, fire escapes, rooftops, doorways. In any room, surveillance would find him within two meters of an exit or a window seventy-plus percent of the time. He is rarely the person seated at the center of a couch; he takes the end. He is rarely the person facing the wall in a restaurant; he takes the seat with the view of the door. This reads tactically and is partly that, but it is older than tactics — it is the lynch-mob residue. He needs the egress visible.

He gravitates to **water-adjacent environments** disproportionately. Apartments overlooking rivers, harbors, reservoirs. Long Island as a homing instinct. He is calmer near large bodies of water and surveillance audio would record a measurable drop in verbal tic frequency (see §6) when he is within sight of a coastline. Whether this is mutant-physiological resonance with available moisture or a more ordinary somatic preference is unresolved in the record; it is observably real.

Indoor temperatures: he keeps his thermostat low. 16–18°C in winter, no air conditioning in summer unless a guest is expected. He does not *need* the cold but he is *at home* in it the way most subjects are at home in a familiar smell. Visitors complain. He apologizes and does not change it.

### Routes

Walks rather than drives whenever the geography permits. Knows transit systems intuitively. In Manhattan phases, surveillance would document repeat use of the same three to four subway stations, the same coffee shop (he is a regular somewhere within four weeks of moving to any new neighborhood; the barista learns his order), the same grocery (a mid-tier chain, never a bodega for staples, bodega for emergencies and ice cream).

He is **route-loyal to the point of vulnerability.** A hostile actor with two weeks of observation could predict his Tuesday and Thursday evenings within a fifteen-minute window. He knows this and does not change it; the comfort of the route outweighs the operational risk in his internal accounting, which is itself diagnostic — he undervalues threats to himself in a manner consistent with the broader self-diminishment pattern.

### Recurring rituals

- **The window pause.** Morning coffee, as noted. Also recurs at dusk in most residential phases — a two-to-five-minute stop at a window with no apparent purpose. The most reliable contemplative interval in his day.
- **The kitchen sweep.** Before bed, every night, he passes through the kitchen and confirms: stove off, sink empty, dishwasher running or empty, lights off. Takes ninety seconds. Performed even in hotels, where there is no kitchen — the route adapts to the geometry but the loop is run.
- **The Hank call.** Across every phase in which both are reachable, subject contacts Hank McCoy at a frequency that surveillance would clock at roughly twice weekly minimum, often higher. The calls are not crisis calls. They are maintenance. They run long. They are the most consistent relational ritual in his life and predate every romantic partnership by decades.
- **Sunday.** Sundays are observably different from other days. Slower start, longer breakfast, a walk that is not a patrol, a movie or a game on in the background. This is the single day on which the Catholic-Irish substrate is faintly visible — not church attendance (he stopped young) but the *shape* of the day, the protected idleness. Surveillance would not catch him in a pew. It would catch him observing Sunday's edges.
- **The annual hometown drive.** Once or twice a year, subject travels to the Long Island town of his childhood. He does not always visit his parents. Sometimes he drives the streets and leaves. The trip is rarely announced. Its frequency increases when he is in distress and decreases when he is well; surveillance can use it as an inverse mood indicator.

### Sleep

Goes to bed between 22:30 and 23:30 on weeknights. Reads for ten to thirty minutes before sleep — paperbacks, mostly genre fiction, the occasional history. He is not a literary subject; he is a competent and consistent reader. Sleeps on his back, single pillow, lightweight covers. **Does not sleep well after combat days** — surveillance would catch longer pre-sleep windows, more frequent kitchen sweeps, occasionally a second shower. He does not take sleep aids. He has been offered them.

Dreams are not on record but the post-combat insomnia pattern is consistent enough to suggest unintegrated combat material. He does not discuss this with anyone, including Hank.

---

## 4. EATING, DRINKING, CONSUMPTION

Eats three meals daily in structured phases; two and grazes in solo phases. **Prefers carbohydrate-dense, low-spice food** — pasta, sandwiches, pizza, diner breakfasts, cereal. This is the palate of a Long Island adolescent that has never been updated, and it is a tell: most of his consumption patterns date to before the lynching, as if the body kept the menu of the last era in which he was uncomplicatedly a kid.

Eats ice cream more than is dignified. This is documented across multiple eras and is one of the few self-indulgences he allows without irony. Flavor of record: vanilla, occasionally with chocolate sauce. He will eat fancier flavors when offered and prefers vanilla when choosing.

**Alcohol:** light social drinker. Beer in team settings, wine when a partner is pouring it, the occasional cocktail. Never to excess on record. Surveillance would not document a single substance-driven incident in sixty publication-years. This is unusual for the affective load he carries and is consistent with the over-controlled cluster — he does not permit himself the chemical avenues other subjects use because the somatic-dissociative avenue is already available and free.

**Caffeine:** two morning cups, occasional afternoon cup, no late-day consumption. Disciplined.

**Tobacco, recreational drugs:** none on record.

Grocery patterns: shops weekly, lists prepared in advance, sticks to the list with one or two reliable impulse additions (ice cream; a snack food). Pays attention to prices in a manner consistent with the middle-class Long Island origin; the CPA in him does not turn off in the grocery aisle.

---

## 5. DOWNTIME

### Solitary downtime

- **Television:** watches sports (Mets, Knicks, Rangers — see above), cooking shows (low-stakes affective register), the occasional procedural. Avoids news programming after dinner. Avoids horror. Avoids anything involving angry fathers, which surveillance would chart as a quiet but consistent avoidance pattern.
- **Reading:** as noted, genre paperbacks. Has a slow, persistent affection for mystery novels in particular — orderly puzzles solved by a competent outsider who is underestimated. The genre choice is not subtle.
- **Music:** late-1970s through mid-1980s pop and rock, with a gentle post-2015 expansion into music his younger partners introduce. Sings in the shower, hums in the kitchen, does not perform musically for others.
- **Gaming:** in modern phases, plays casual video games — the kind that reward steady competence rather than reflex mastery. Avoids competitive online play.
- **Skating:** documented in multiple eras. Subject will, when alone and unobserved (he believes), generate ice and skate — sometimes in apartments, sometimes outdoors at night. This is the closest thing in his life to an unselfconscious expression of his mutation for its own sake, and it is invariably done in private. Surveillance catching him at this is catching him at his most undefended.

### Social downtime

Card nights, movie nights, team dinners. He is reliably present and reliably the one organizing the logistics no one else wanted to organize. He is the friend who books the restaurant, picks up the cake, remembers the birthday. This is **affection expressed through administration**, and it is one of the most consistent prosocial behaviors in his record.

He drinks coffee with Hank in long sessions whenever geography permits. These are the highest-information conversations in his life and the ones in which his defenses are thinnest.

### Romantic downtime

In partnered phases — historically rare, more frequent post-2015 — he is observably attentive to small domestic gestures: cooking breakfast, leaving notes, remembering preferences. He is **better at the dailiness of partnership than at its escalations.** Surveillance would catch him stalling at thresholds — moving in together, meeting families, defining the relationship publicly — even when the underlying relationship is functional. The stall is not malice; it is the avoidant overlay on the anxious base.

---

## 6. MICRO-PATTERNS, TICS, TELLS

A total-surveillance file would catalogue the following granularities:

- **Verbal:** a high baseline rate of quipping — surveillance audio would log a quip approximately every ninety seconds in social settings, dropping to near-zero when he is alone or with Hank. The quip rate is an inverse intimacy indicator: more quips means less safety.
- **Hand to back of neck.** When asked a question he does not want to answer, the right hand goes to the back of the neck before the mouth opens. Consistent across decades. Surveillance would clock this as a primary tell of incoming deflection.
- **The half-step back.** When complimented — particularly on power or capacity — subject's body translates approximately fifteen to thirty centimeters backward within two seconds. Often masked as a shift in posture. Reliable enough to use as a calibration tool.
- **The closed-mouth smile.** Default. The open laugh is rare and indicates genuine release.
- **Ice in the fingertips.** Under stress he does not consciously register, surveillance with thermal imaging would catch faint cooling at the fingertips and the tip of the nose — a sub-threshold expression of power he is not aware of leaking. The leak increases in the presence of his father, in conversations about power-ceiling, and in the first weeks of any new romantic relationship.
- **Looking up and to the right** when constructing an answer that is not the true answer. Inconsistent in adolescence, stabilized by adulthood. Not a reliable lie detector across all subjects but is reliable for him because his lies are nearly always defensive-comedic and follow a predictable cognitive route.
- **Touches doorframes.** Passing through doorways, his hand brushes the frame about forty percent of the time. A small grounding habit. He is unaware of it.
- **Apologies for small things.** Bumps a chair, apologizes to the chair. Drops a fork, apologizes to the room. The diffuse apology is a residue of having been raised to take up less space; surveillance would log dozens per day in social settings.
- **Does not apologize for large things easily.** The disproportion between micro-apology frequency and macro-apology difficulty is one of the cleanest behavioral contradictions in his record.
- **Phone habits.** Holds the phone in his left hand, scrolls with the left thumb. Texts in full sentences, capitalized, punctuated — the CPA showing. Uses periods. Younger partners have teased him about this. He has not changed.
- **Walking pace.** Brisk on patrol, slow when thinking, very slow when approaching anything that frightens him emotionally. Surveillance can read the affective valence of his destination from his approach speed alone within a hundred meters.

---

## 7. THE SURVEILLANCE WEEK — A COMPOSITE

A representative seven-day window, in a stable mainland residential phase, would look approximately as follows. The shape is consistent enough across decades that this composite can be treated as predictive rather than illustrative.

**Monday.** 06:25 wake. Coffee, window pause, news scan. Out the door 08:10. Team training or client work depending on phase. Lunch alone or with one teammate. Afternoon administrative. Evening: gym (light), home by 19:00, dinner alone, television, paperback, lights out 23:00.

**Tuesday.** Same morning shape. Mid-week patrol or extended training. Evening call with Hank — long, slow, the day's deepest conversation. Bed slightly later.

**Wednesday.** Grocery day. List prepared Tuesday night. Predictable route, predictable purchases, the impulse pint of ice cream. Evening domestic — bills, small repairs, recycling. The CPA day.

**Thursday.** Operational day in active phases. Higher quip rate, higher tic frequency, fingertip cooling on uptick. Post-mission decompression: long shower, second meal, longer-than-usual kitchen sweep before bed.

**Friday.** Social evening. Team dinner, card night, or in partnered phases a date. The week's highest open-laugh count. Stays up later. Sleeps later Saturday.

**Saturday.** Slower morning. Skating in private if alone and the geometry allows. Errands. Afternoon with friends or partner. Evening movie or game.

**Sunday.** The protected day. Long breakfast. Walk that is not a patrol. Window time at dusk. An early call to a parent or a sibling-figure in phases when that is possible. Reads longer. Bed earlier. The week resets.

Across this week, a competent observer would identify subject within ninety minutes of beginning observation, predict his locations at any given hour within a fifteen-minute confidence interval by day four, and identify his three primary attachment relationships (Hank, the current partner if any, the institutional family) by day six without ever hearing a name spoken. The life is legible. The man inside the life is the harder problem, and the surveillance week is the first chapter of that problem, not its solution.

— END SECTION —


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*UATU Dossier, Subject: Robert Louis Drake. Section 7a of 14.*

The family-of-origin file on this subject is unusually short in headcount and unusually dense in pathology-per-relationship. He is an only child; he has no offspring; he has lost no immediate kin to death within the published record. The complete primary family unit consists of three people — William Drake, Madeline Drake, and the subject — and one extended figure of operational significance (paternal-line uncle, intermittent). Every wound, every defense, every script the subject runs in adult attachment was lathed inside that triangle on Long Island between approximately 1948 and 1963. What follows is the granular mapping.

---

## 7a.i — WILLIAM ROBERT DRAKE (Father)

**Provenance.** Born early 1920s, Fort Salonga / Port Washington corridor, Nassau County, NY. Irish-Catholic, second-generation. Likely WWII service (Pacific theater inferred from incidental dialogue, Iceman vol. 3); blue-collar-to-lower-management trajectory; insurance adjusting and small-business bookkeeping in the working record. Lifelong Long Island resident; never crossed the Hudson with intent until the 2017 solo arc. Registered Democrat by birth, Nixon Democrat by 1968, Reagan Democrat thereafter; reflexive, not ideological, conservatism — the politics of grievance rather than doctrine.

**History with subject — phase one (1948 — c. 1960, pre-manifestation).** Documented and inferred: a father who loved his son in the manner of his generation — present, providing, withholding. Catch in the yard on weekends; little league through age ten or eleven; church on Sundays at St. Aidan's or its corollary. No documented physical abuse. The injury was atmospheric: a household in which masculine adequacy was the only currency of paternal approval and in which the subject — bookish, slight, sensitive, quick with a joke — was always trading at a slight discount. The father's affection was conditional on the son being a particular kind of boy, and the son was approximately that kind of boy, but not quite, and knew it.

**Phase two (c. 1961 — manifestation; X-Men #44–47 / Iceman vol. 1 retcon).** The lynch-mob event. William Drake's behavior during the incident is the foundational data: he did not lead the mob, but he did not stop it either. The record across retellings is consistent — William is at the periphery, ashamed and paralyzed, when the neighborhood comes for his son. Madeline weeps. William stands. The subject sees this. **The subject saw his father choose the neighborhood over him in the moment of greatest possible stakes, and has never, in sixty years of published behavior, fully un-seen it.** Every subsequent paternal interaction is overlaid on that frame.

**Phase three (1963–1996, the long silence).** Visits home are infrequent, formal, short. Holidays observed; conversation kept to weather, the Mets, the subject's CPA studies (which the father approves of with relief — *normal son, normal job*). Mutant identity is the unmentionable center of the table. The subject sustains this for thirty-plus publication years with no recorded breakdown of the protocol. He shows up, plays the son, leaves. The father drinks one beer with dinner, watches the news, does not ask.

**Phase four (Uncanny X-Men #340, 1996 — the beating).** William Drake is hospitalized by the Friends of Humanity after publicly defending his son. This is the inflection point and it is unfinished. The subject's reaction is layered: rage at the assailants, guilt at having been the catalyst, a thawing toward the father that the father reciprocates incompletely, and — crucially — *resentment that the father's first defense of him arrived only after thirty years and only at the cost of a hospital bed.* The subject does not voice the resentment. He sits at the bedside. He brings coffee. He leaves before the conversation can become real.

**Phase five (2005–2015, intermittent).** William's bigotry recurs in episodic regressions (Generation X cameo; X-Factor revival; Astonishing X-Men #51 wedding scene). The pattern: a gesture of acceptance under direct pressure, then a return to the old register when the pressure lifts. The subject learns not to trust the gestures. He visits less.

**Phase six (Iceman solo, 2017–2019 — the coming-out).** The subject comes out to William as gay. William's reaction is bad in the specific way that William's reactions are always bad: not violent, not theatrical, *small* — a tightening of the jaw, a turning away, a refusal to look at the son's face, a muttered objection routed through the mother. The subject leaves. They reconcile partially, then again partially, then again. The arc ends with William ill (cardiac event), the subject at the bedside, both men exhausted, neither having said the actual sentence either one needs to say.

**Dynamic.** Asymmetric proximity-seeking from the son toward a father who is constitutionally incapable of being the kind of father the son needs, and who occasionally — under duress — produces fragments of that father, which the son cannot help but reach for, and which the father then withdraws. It is the classic intermittent-reinforcement schedule, the cruelest of the operant patterns, the one that produces the most durable attachment to the most unsatisfying object.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust: low and structural. The subject does not tell William the truth about anything that matters and has not since age fifteen. Safety: physically high in adulthood (William is not dangerous); psychologically low (every interaction risks the small withdrawal that the subject is sensitized to detect at sub-clinical thresholds). The subject reads William's face the way a hostage reads a guard's.

**Failure mode.** Recurrent. Each time the subject offers a piece of himself — mutant identity, sexual identity, professional achievement outside the CPA frame — and William fails to receive it, the subject collapses inward for between three and nine days (estimable from publication cadence across solo arcs). He becomes quieter, jokes get bleaker, ice-form duration extends. He does not reach out for support during these periods. He metabolizes alone.

**Leverage.** Anyone seeking to destabilize the subject through this vector requires only one thing: the appearance of William's voice expressing rejection, or the appearance of William's voice expressing acceptance and then withdrawing it. The second is more destructive than the first. Telepaths who have attempted the first (various) have produced rage; the second has never been weaponized against him at scale, and would, in this analyst's estimation, produce a Stage 3 dissociative collapse within hours.

---

## 7a.ii — MADELINE BEATRICE DRAKE (Mother, née surname unspecified in canon; Irish-Catholic Long Island stock)

**Provenance.** Born mid-1920s. Housewife, parish volunteer, occasional part-time retail (a department store on Northern Boulevard, inferred). Soft voice, soft hands, an eye for cake decoration, a habit of putting a hand on the subject's forearm when she wants him to stop talking. The household's emotional thermostat — set permanently to *avoid temperature changes*.

**History with subject — phase one (infancy through manifestation).** The favored parent in early childhood, by all behavioral indication. Madeline is the one who sat with him through illnesses, who read to him, who let him stay up late watching the late movie when William was working. The early bond is warm, regressive-tinged, and slightly enmeshed — she made him her companion in a marriage that had cooled by the time he was six. He learned to read her moods before he learned to read her books.

**Phase two (the lynch-mob night).** Madeline weeps. Madeline does not act. Madeline is, in the retelling across multiple writers, *behind* William on the porch as the neighborhood gathers; she is a half-step further from the threshold than her husband, which is psychologically definitive. The subject's mother did not protect him either. She suffered visibly while not protecting him, which is a different and arguably worse data point than William's stoic non-protection, because it taught the subject that *love without agency does not save you* — a lesson he has applied, with quiet devastation, to every romantic relationship of his adult life.

**Phase three (1963–2015, the long collusion).** Madeline becomes the household's translator. She softens William's bigotry in transmission to the subject, softens the subject's mutant news in transmission to William, runs a private back-channel diplomacy that allows the family to maintain surface function at the cost of any actual encounter between father and son. She means well. She is the architect of the family's most damaging structural feature: *the conversation between the men never happens because Madeline keeps having it for them, separately, in the kitchen.* The subject is aware of this from approximately his mid-twenties. He permits it because the alternative is worse. He resents it. He calls her every Sunday at 4 PM Eastern, a ritual that survives all upheavals.

**Phase four (coming-out, Iceman solo).** Madeline's reaction is the more painful one, against expectation. William is gruff and turns away; Madeline weeps and asks if it is something she did, which routes the subject's coming-out through her guilt and back into his caretaking — he ends up comforting *her* for *his* identity, which is the family pattern in its purest distillation. The arc reaches a partial reconciliation in which Madeline becomes a slow, fumbling ally; she still uses the wrong words; she tries.

**Dynamic.** Enmeshed-passive. Madeline loves the subject without limit and without effective action. The subject loves Madeline with a protective tenderness that has shaded, across decades, into a low-grade contempt he refuses to examine. He is angry with her for not having been larger than she was. He will never say this.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust: high in intention, low in operational reliability. He tells her more than he tells William, less than he tells Hank. Safety: physically absolute; psychologically dangerous in a specific way — Madeline is the person most able to make him feel responsible for someone else's distress about him, which is the precise mechanism that produces his deepest self-suppression.

**Failure mode.** When Madeline expresses distress about the subject's identity or choices, the subject's response is to *shrink the choice* — to minimize, to reassure, to perform okayness, to leave the room mentally even when present physically. The Sunday-call ritual is consequently long on weather and short on substance; the subject finishes each call slightly diminished and does not connect the diminishment to the call until hours later.

**Leverage.** Anyone wishing to manipulate the subject through Madeline needs only to threaten her wellbeing or to route a message of distress *about him* through her voice. The second mechanism is more efficient. He will defer his own needs indefinitely to manage her affect.

---

## 7a.iii — THE MARRIAGE (William × Madeline as a structural object the subject inhabited)

A relationship category in its own right because the marriage *as a system* shaped the subject as decisively as either parent individually.

**Structure.** A 1950s Long Island Catholic marriage of obligation-fidelity: neither parent considered leaving, neither parent was happy, both parents organized their lives around the appearance of the contrary. William handled the public face; Madeline handled the private temperature; the subject was the buffer state between them, recruited early into the role of conversation-starter, peace-keeper, and emotional weather-vane. He learned to enter a room and sample the air for tension before speaking. The habit persists at fifty-plus publication-years.

**Effect on subject.** A child who is the buffer in his parents' marriage learns three things, and the subject learned all three: that his own needs are subordinate to system-stability; that affect is something to be managed rather than expressed; that love can be sustained indefinitely without intimacy, which is a lesson that has destroyed every long-term romantic prospect of his adult life until very recently. The marriage was the subject's first model of partnership, and it taught him that partnership is what you maintain when intimacy fails. He has been trying to unlearn this since approximately 2015 and is making uneven progress.

**Failure mode.** The subject still, in his forties (publication-functional), defaults to buffer behavior in any household he occupies — Krakoa cohabitation arcs document this. He cleans up after others' conflicts, redirects difficult conversations with a joke, exits the room when temperatures rise. The behavior is not chosen; it is conditioned at a depth below choice.

**Leverage.** None directly — the marriage is not an entity that can be threatened — but anyone reconstructing the subject's templates would model partnership-as-management and predict his romantic behavior from it with high accuracy.

---

## 7a.iv — UNCLE (paternal-line, name variously rendered; secondary canon)

**Provenance and function.** A paternal uncle, intermittently present in the Long Island household across the subject's childhood, who functioned as the more permissive masculine figure — the one who slipped him comic books, took him to a Mets game without making it a lesson, did not flinch when the powers manifested in the way the subject's father flinched. Appears in flashback fragments across Iceman vol. 1 and vol. 3. Probably deceased by mid-publication-timeline; the death is unmarked in the record, which is itself diagnostic.

**Effect on subject.** This figure is the subject's only childhood evidence that masculine adulthood could contain warmth without conditionality. Every subsequent male attachment of consequence — Hank McCoy preeminently, but also Warren Worthington in the better moments, Northstar, Christian Frost briefly — bears the imprint of this template: *the man who lets you be what you are without comment.* The uncle's absence from the adult record suggests the subject has not consciously integrated this template; he replicates it without naming it.

**Failure mode.** The uncle's death — unmarked, ungrieved on page — represents an unprocessed loss that likely contributes to the subject's pattern of forming intense, brief male attachments and then losing them without overt mourning. He metabolizes male loss the way he metabolized this one: silently.

**Leverage.** Low. The figure is too peripheral to the current operational record to weaponize, and the subject's memories of him are protective rather than vulnerable in structure. A skilled telepath could potentially access the figure to *soothe* the subject — an unusual leverage vector, but a real one. Anyone seeking to *destabilize* via this memory would fail; it is one of the few clean rooms in the house.

---

## 7a.v — JUDY HARMON (the date at manifestation; quasi-family by virtue of formative co-presence)

**Status.** Not biological family, but included in this section because she was the only other person physically present at the foundational trauma and therefore occupies a structural position in the subject's origin-bond constellation analogous to a sibling-of-event.

**Provenance.** Long Island teenager, contemporary of the subject; ordinary girl by every available indicator; the date that ended in a near-lynching when the subject's powers manifested in defense of her honor against another boy.

**History.** Single documented interaction of consequence. The subject took her on a date, defended her, manifested his powers, was pursued by a mob, was rescued. Judy Harmon's fate is barely recorded; she returns home, she presumably tells the story, the neighborhood mobilizes. She is not the villain; she is the witness who could not testify on his behalf because the testimony would not have mattered.

**Effect on subject.** Pattern-defining. Judy Harmon was the first woman the subject tried to be a man for, and the attempt produced his near-death. Every subsequent heterosexual pursuit of his fifty-year closeted period replicates the structure: *perform masculinity toward a woman, fail visibly, be punished.* The repetition compulsion is textbook, and it is unbroken until the 2015 outing creates a context in which the performance is no longer required.

**Failure mode / leverage.** Negligible directly (she is a non-actor in the adult record), but the memory of her — and of what happened with her — is the buried template the subject has been running unconsciously for decades. Surface the template to him and he reorganizes; he has done some of this work post-2015 and would do more under skilled clinical pressure.

---

## 7a.vi — THE ABSENT: CHILDREN HE DOES NOT HAVE; SIBLINGS HE DOES NOT HAVE; DEAD HE HAS NOT BURIED

A negative inventory, because the *absences* in this subject's family file are as diagnostic as the presences.

**No siblings.** Only child. He has no horizontal family attachment of origin and has spent his adult life recruiting one — the original five X-Men function as siblings, with Hank McCoy preeminently as the brother-of-choice. The intensity of his attachment to the original team is partly attributable to the sibling-vacancy in his developmental history. Threats to the original five register at the somatic depth at which actual sibling-threats would register in a subject with siblings.

**No children.** The subject is, at functional age forty-plus, childless and has been visibly disinterested in fatherhood across the entire record. The disinterest is not stated; it is *enacted* by the total absence of the subject from any storyline involving the question of his reproduction. Diagnostically: a man who has spent his entire life metabolizing a difficult father, and whose own identity is structured around the wound of paternal conditionality, is unlikely to volunteer for the role until that wound is closed. The wound is not closed. He has not volunteered. The Krakoa-era resurrection protocols make biological parenthood functionally moot, which has further deferred the question.

**No buried dead in the primary family.** Both parents are alive in the most recent canonical record. The uncle's death is unmarked. The subject has never publicly grieved a member of his family of origin, which means his mourning capacity for that specific category of loss is *untested* at a publication-age where most subjects have been tested two or three times. When William dies — and he will — the subject's response is genuinely unpredictable from the existing record, and represents the single largest unscripted variable in his future behavioral envelope.

**The Drake family home (Fort Salonga / Port Washington corridor).** A physical object that operates in this file as a family member. Modest split-level or colonial, brown carpet in the den, framed school photos along the staircase, a kitchen table at which every consequential family conversation has occurred and at which the subject still, in adulthood, takes a specific chair (the one facing the door — vigilance posture, learned at fifteen). He visits the house approximately four times a year per the inferable cadence. He stays no more than thirty-six hours. He always sleeps in his childhood bedroom, which Madeline has not redecorated. He always leaves before Sunday dinner if he can engineer it. The house is the most stable object in his attachment field and the one he is most consistently relieved to leave.

---

## 7a.vii — SUMMARY OF ORIGIN-BOND CONFIGURATION

The subject's family-of-origin is a closed three-body system with one peripheral satellite (the uncle), one structural witness (Judy Harmon), and a defining absence in every other direction. The system produced exactly the subject it was engineered to produce: a child who learned that visibility is lethal, that love is conditional on smallness, that affect is to be managed rather than expressed, and that the only safe response to a difficult conversation is a joke or a closed door. He has been working against the engineering since approximately 1996 and accelerating since 2015, with measurable but incomplete progress.

**The single most operationally significant fact in this section** is that William Drake is still alive and the conversation between father and son has still not happened. Until it does — or until William dies without it happening — the subject's deepest developmental work remains pending, and the throttle on his power, his identity, and his capacity for sustained intimacy remains, by his own unconscious hand, partially engaged.

— END SECTION 7a. Continues §7b: Relationships II — Chosen Family & The Original Five. —


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*Filed under SUBJECT: ROBERT LOUIS DRAKE. Section maps non-romantic, non-adversarial human bonds across the published longitudinal record (1963–present). Each entry: history → dynamics → evolution → trust/safety architecture → failure mode → leverage (defined here as **what an actor — benevolent or hostile — could move the subject with**, not endorsement of its use).*

The organizing observation, established in the Workup and substantiated below: Subject does not distribute attachment evenly. He maintains a small, brightly-lit inner ring (one, possibly two members), a working ring of original-team siblings (three or four), and a wide acquaintance ring he charms into believing they are closer than they are. The humor frame functions as a permeable membrane — it lets warmth out and keeps depth in. Persons who have ever penetrated the membrane are listed first.

---

## 1. HENRY "HANK" McCOY — THE PRIMARY ATTACHMENT

**History.** Met September 1963, X-Men #1. Recruited to the school within weeks of each other; Hank was already in residence when Xavier extracted Bobby from the holding cell. They were assigned adjacent rooms in the original mansion dormitory; in early Lee/Kirby issues they are paired in nearly every off-mission scene — diner trips, training-room pranks, study sessions where Hank tutors Bobby through subjects Bobby pretends not to understand. The "Beast and Iceman" pairing was so structurally embedded by 1968 that when Roy Thomas extracted them from the team into the *Amazing Adventures* run, neither character was given a separate book — they were treated, editorially, as a unit. That editorial gesture mirrors the subject's internal architecture: Hank is not a friend, Hank is a *category of person*, and the category contains exactly one entry.

**Dynamics.** Asymmetric in surface, symmetric in floor. Hank is the more verbally fluent, more credentialed, more publicly impressive of the two; Bobby is the one Hank loosens around. Hank's polysyllabic register collapses into actual Brooklyn vowels and dad-jokes only in Bobby's presence — across writers as different as Claremont, Simonson, Morrison, Whedon, and Duggan. Bobby, conversely, is the only person who teases Hank's vanity without producing a defensive response. The exchange-rate is well-established: Bobby gives Hank a place where intelligence is not the price of admission; Hank gives Bobby a witness who saw him before the armor was fully installed.

**Evolution.** Five identifiable phases.

1. *1963–1969, dorm-room phase.* Pranking, snowball-fights-on-Beast, joint pursuit of girls neither of them got. Bobby orbits Hank.
2. *1970s Amazing Adventures / Avengers split.* Hank mutates (blue fur), joins the Avengers; Bobby drifts into the Champions. Letters and phone-calls are referenced off-panel. The first long separation. Bobby's behavioral record in this period — the Champions instability, the Defenders cameos — correlates suspiciously well with the absence of Hank.
3. *1986–1991, X-Factor.* Reunited. Bobby acts as Hank's emotional ground during the "cured" period and again when the blue fur returns. Hank acts as Bobby's first-call confidant about Opal. This is the *peak* phase of the bond.
4. *1990s–2000s, divergence.* Hank's intellectual life accelerates (Morrison's X-Men, Whedon's Astonishing); Bobby's plateau extends. The bond persists but becomes one-sided in disclosure — Hank confides in Bobby; Bobby still does not disclose the closet to Hank, the one person he could have. *This is a load-bearing observation about the depth of the closet:* Hank was safe, and Bobby still did not tell him. The omission is not about Hank. It is about the lesson.
5. *2010s–Krakoa onward, dark-Beast complication.* Adult Hank's ethical drift (compromised by the time-displaced young Hank's idealism and by his own post-Krakoa transgressions) places Bobby in the unfamiliar position of being the more ethically reliable McCoy-Drake partner. He grieves the version of Hank he had. The bond persists as memory and as obligation; the working friendship is wounded but not severed.

**Trust/safety architecture.** Total, with one structural caveat: trust is *bidirectional in friendship matters and unidirectional in confidence matters.* Hank tells Bobby everything; Bobby tells Hank what the humor frame permits. Hank has never weaponized anything Bobby gave him. Bobby's body language around Hank is the most relaxed in his entire behavioral record — shoulders down, hands out of pockets, the only person around whom he sits rather than perches.

**Failure mode.** The bond fails the same way both times it has been stressed: by Hank changing in ways Bobby cannot follow and by Bobby refusing to disclose what would let Hank follow him. Each man assumes the other will always be there and underinvests in maintenance. They have never had a stated, deliberate conversation about what they are to each other; it has been left assumed for six decades, which means a single bad rupture could erase the asset because nothing has been said aloud that could be appealed to.

**Leverage.** The single largest pressure point in the file. Threats to Hank's life produce sharper, less-deflected responses from the subject than threats to his own — confirmed across multiple eras. Conversely, evidence of Hank's ethical compromise produces *withdrawn* affect (not rage), which is the more dangerous register because it suppresses rather than expresses. An actor wishing to motivate the subject moves Hank. An actor wishing to break the subject demonstrates Hank's irreversible moral fall.

---

## 2. WARREN WORTHINGTON III — THE LATERAL SIBLING

**History.** Co-original-five. Recruited shortly before Bobby. The wealth differential was salient from week one — Warren paid for outings, Bobby pretended not to notice, the prank-economy substituted for reciprocity Bobby could not afford. Through the '60s they are a secondary pairing behind Bobby-and-Hank.

**Dynamics.** Bobby is one of very few people who has consistently *not* envied Warren — neither his wealth, nor his appearance, nor his confidence with women — and Warren registers this and relaxes accordingly. The bond is built on Bobby's refusal to play the status game Warren is constantly inside of. In return, Warren treats Bobby with a fraternal gentleness rare in his other relationships; he does not condescend to Bobby even when others do.

**Evolution.** Survived: the original team's dissolution, the Champions (Warren was the financial backstop), X-Factor, Warren's Apocalypse-driven mutation into Archangel, the Death persona, the multiple personality fractures of the Remender Uncanny X-Force run, and the Krakoa-era resurrections. The bond *deepened* during the Archangel periods — Bobby was one of the few teammates who continued to address Warren as Warren regardless of which face he was wearing, which is the same operation Bobby would want performed on himself.

**Trust/safety architecture.** High trust, medium depth. Warren is in the inner ring but in a different chamber than Hank — Warren is the brother Bobby would call in a logistical or physical crisis; Hank is the one he would call (eventually, if pushed) in an emotional one. Warren is also one of the very few people Bobby has accepted material help from without subsequent corrosive guilt, because Warren makes the giving frictionless.

**Failure mode.** Drift, not rupture. Long periods without contact, picked up where left off. The risk is not loss of bond; it is that the bond's elasticity has never been tested by a *deliberate* betrayal because none has occurred. Bobby has no calibrated response for Warren-failing-him.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Less acute than Hank but with a particular sub-mode: Bobby is unusually protective of the *original* Warren — the pre-Apocalypse self — and any threat framed as "we will take more of Warren away from himself" produces uncharacteristic operational intensity.

---

## 3. SCOTT SUMMERS — THE OLDER BROTHER AND THE TRANSFERENCE OBJECT

**History.** Scott was already at the school when Xavier extracted Bobby. Scott is, in the strict text, the *first* person who tried to talk the lynch mob down before Xavier intervened — meaning Scott is fused with the rescue event in implicit memory. This is not negligible. Subject's parental transference onto the X-Men routes through two figures: Xavier and Scott. Scott, being closer in age and physically present in daily life, carries more of the load.

**Dynamics.** Mixed. Bobby defers, resents the deference, sublimates the resentment into snark, then defers again. The snark register *at Scott specifically* is sharper than at any other teammate — a tell. The classical pattern of an anxious-attached younger sibling toward a competent older sibling who was conscripted into a parental role too early: love and irritation as a single complex affect, never untangled.

**Evolution.** Bobby has, across every era, occupied the role of *Scott's ethical mirror within the original five.* When Scott drifts (Utopia, AvX, Inhumans vs X-Men), Bobby is reliably the dissenter — quietly, persistently, without ever quite leaving. Schism is the clean example: Bobby goes with Wolverine to Westchester, ethically distancing himself from Scott's militarization, while clearly grieving the distance. Inhumans vs X-Men, he again opposes Scott-aligned positions while still framing them with grief rather than contempt. He has never publicly disavowed Scott; he has never followed him uncritically. The Krakoa era partially repaired this — both men older, both with the gay-and-mutant identity question (Scott's polycule, Bobby's openness) defused.

**Trust/safety architecture.** Trust in Scott's *competence* is total; trust in Scott's *judgment* is conditional and has been since approximately 2005. Safety is moderate — Scott has never been a person around whom Bobby can be small in the way he can be with Hank.

**Failure mode.** The transference itself. Bobby will under-criticize Scott in private (deferring to the older-brother frame) and over-criticize Scott in jokes (leaking the resentment), and never have the conversation that would resolve either.

**Leverage.** Scott's approval still moves Bobby. He will pretend it does not. It does. Conversely, Scott's *disapproval* — when sustained — produces a particular form of withdrawal in Bobby that includes uncharacteristic operational risk-taking, as if the cost-benefit recalibrates when the older-brother voice is no longer auditing.

---

## 4. JEAN GREY — THE ORIGINAL UNREQUITED AND THE WITNESS

**History.** Bobby's adolescent infatuation, X-Men #1–8. Lost cleanly to Scott. The interesting datum is that Bobby *retained* the friendship without the resentment that usually corrodes such losses. He attended Jean's wakes (multiple, Marvel being Marvel), grieved each, and integrated her back into the working friendship each time without recalibrating the underlying warmth.

**Dynamics.** Sibling-coded post-1965. Jean is one of the few telepaths Bobby has actively trusted to be in his head — and the one who, in time-displaced teenage form, opened the closet without consent (All-New X-Men #40, 2015). The handling is morally complicated; the *relational* fact is that Bobby forgave her, repeatedly, in both timelines.

**Evolution.** Friendship → mild romantic flicker → friendship → grief-cycle → restored friendship → outing event → restored friendship again. The remarkable steadiness of the affection through multiple violations (the outing was a violation; Bobby treated it as a clumsy gift) is itself diagnostic of Bobby's anxious-attachment forgiveness register and Jean's specific protected status in his hierarchy.

**Trust/safety architecture.** Cognitive trust very high; bodily-privacy trust permanently asterisked after the outing. He is more guarded around her telepathy than he displays.

**Failure mode.** Over-forgiveness. Bobby will absorb a Jean-Grey violation he would not absorb from anyone else, which means Jean is structurally capable of harming him in ways neither of them will register as harm at the time.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Less than Hank, comparable to Warren. Jean's safety provokes immediate operational response; Jean's *requests* produce compliance Bobby would refuse from others.

---

## 5. CHARLES XAVIER — THE RESCUER

**History.** Extracted Bobby from a holding cell during a near-lynching. This is the founding event of the subject's adult existence. Whatever else Xavier later became in the wider X-narrative, he is in Bobby's implicit memory the man who walked in when the door was about to be kicked down by neighbors.

**Dynamics.** Filial transference, heavy, never directly examined. Bobby's deference to authority generally is shaped by this specific event. Bobby has rarely criticized Xavier publicly; the closest he has come is the post-Onslaught and post-mind-wipe revelations periods, where his expressed disappointment was *measured* in a way that revealed how protected the underlying figure was.

**Evolution.** Largely stable until the Krakoa era, where Xavier's behavior becomes increasingly Procrustean and Bobby's deference does not visibly erode. He continues to operate inside Xavier's frame even when other original-five members (notably Hank, ironically) more openly dissent.

**Trust/safety architecture.** Cognitive trust diminished post-revelations; emotional debt undiminished. The two are not the same channel and do not cancel.

**Failure mode.** The debt is structurally unpayable, which means Bobby will tolerate from Xavier what he would tolerate from no one else. A weaponizing actor could exploit this and Bobby would be slow to recognize it.

**Leverage.** High in a narrow band: appeals framed in the language of *protecting young mutants from what almost happened to him* land with unusual force. Xavier-issued instructions in that register receive minimal questioning.

---

## 6. ORORO MUNROE — THE SISTER OF EQUAL WEIGHT

**History.** Joined the school after Bobby had already left; their direct co-team time is intermittent but their cross-team familiarity is dense (X-Factor crossovers, X-Men reunions, Krakoa).

**Dynamics.** Storm is one of the very few people who *does not* receive Bobby's clowning register. He speaks to her more plainly than to almost anyone else, possibly because her own dignity makes the clowning fall flat and the failure-to-deflect is then taken as permission to be direct. This is a small but persistent observation across writers.

**Trust/safety architecture.** High mutual respect, modest emotional disclosure. Storm is one of the people whose *good opinion* Bobby tracks without seeking; he calibrates against her without performing for her.

**Failure mode.** Distance. They have never had a generative crisis together that would deepen the bond beyond its current dignified midrange.

**Leverage.** Storm's direct request will be honored without humor-frame negotiation. This is the strongest version of "permission" in his file outside the institutional Xavier-channel.

---

## 7. KURT WAGNER — THE ETHICAL COMPANION

**History.** Extensive cross-team service across decades. The bond is built on a structural similarity neither has fully named: both men were nearly killed by mobs of normal people for what they could not hide. Kurt's visible mutation and Bobby's once-visible powers manifestation map onto the same trauma class.

**Dynamics.** Quiet, warm, mutually respectful. Kurt's Catholicism is one of the very few channels through which Bobby's own Catholic-Irish background resurfaces; conversations with Kurt occasionally elicit theological language Bobby uses with no one else.

**Trust/safety architecture.** High. Kurt is in the working inner ring without being in the Hank-chamber.

**Failure mode.** Underused. Bobby could have processed substantial identity material with Kurt and largely has not.

**Leverage.** Appeals to fundamental decency, framed without pressure, succeed with Bobby when Kurt makes them. The Kurt-channel is one of the few that can ask Bobby to act *against his own protective instincts* and receive compliance.

---

## 8. LOGAN — THE UNEXPECTED OLDER BROTHER

**History.** Initially distant — Logan joined the team that displaced Bobby's generation. The bond develops slowly across the '80s and '90s and consolidates at Schism, where Bobby follows Logan to Westchester.

**Dynamics.** Logan is one of the few people who has *named*, in the text, that Bobby is throttling himself, and one of the very few from whom Bobby accepts that observation without deflection. The Logan-channel is paradoxically *less defended* than the Scott-channel because Logan does not occupy the parental transference slot and therefore his approval does not carry the same disabling charge.

**Trust/safety architecture.** Higher than reputation would suggest. Bobby has been physically vulnerable around Logan in ways he is not around most teammates.

**Failure mode.** Logan's recurrent deaths and absences. Bobby grieves each in a register he does not announce.

**Leverage.** Logan-style appeals — terse, demanding, ungilded — produce responses Bobby's other channels cannot. Logan can ask Bobby to be larger than he is performing and be obeyed.

---

## 9. ANGELICA JONES (FIRESTAR) — THE CHOSEN SISTER

**History.** Met during the Champions/X-Factor adjacencies and consolidated as a pairing during the New Warriors → X-Men crossings and the various "old friends" reunions. The thermal-opposite framing (fire/ice) is structural shorthand for a real complementarity.

**Dynamics.** Angelica is one of two younger-mutant figures (Northstar being the other in a different register) toward whom Bobby has been *unguardedly* fraternal. He does not perform for her, does not flirt with her, does not posture; the role he occupies with her is the older-sibling role he never quite let himself occupy on the original team.

**Trust/safety architecture.** High, with low intensity. The friendship is durable precisely because it is not load-bearing.

**Failure mode.** Distance. They go years without sustained contact and resume without friction; the bond is undertested.

**Leverage.** Angelica is one of the rare actors who can ask Bobby to *show up* — physically, immediately, without explanation — and receive it.

---

## 10. JEAN-PAUL BEAUBIER (NORTHSTAR) — THE OUT ELDER

**History.** Acquaintance for decades; significance changes after All-New X-Men #40 and the Iceman solo runs. Northstar is the longest-out gay man in the X-roster and one of the very few who could function as an experienced witness to what Bobby was beginning.

**Dynamics.** Northstar's astringency cuts through Bobby's humor frame in a way that few other registers do. He does not coddle Bobby's late arrival to his own identity; he models that being out is not in itself a personality. This is one of the most useful gifts Bobby has received and he knows it.

**Trust/safety architecture.** Increasing. Started as professional respect; consolidating into genuine friendship across the Krakoa-era and post-Krakoa runs.

**Failure mode.** Bobby's tendency to import the unspoken-respect framework into a relationship that benefits from spoken directness. Northstar is supplying the directness; Bobby has not fully reciprocated.

**Leverage.** Northstar can name Bobby's deflections out loud and be heard. Few others can.

---

## 11. KITTY PRYDE — THE YOUNGER SISTER AND THE BRIEF MIRROR

**History.** Bobby was one of the earliest figures to befriend Kitty when she joined the school as a child; the brief romantic flicker during the Australian era was an aberration in what was otherwise an older-brother bond.

**Dynamics.** Bobby's most successful sustained mentorship of a younger mutant, ironically because Kitty quickly outgrew needing mentorship and the relationship rebalanced into peer-sibling. The aborted romance was, in retrospect, a closet-era misfire — an *available* partner he predictably failed to commit to.

**Trust/safety architecture.** High, with a small ongoing awkwardness from the romantic episode that both parties manage gracefully.
