**Failure mode.** The romance-residue precludes the deepest version of the bond. They are excellent friends who could have been better siblings if the closet had not generated a false-positive courtship.

**Leverage.** Kitty's command-channel (when she is in command) is honored with unusual professionalism by Bobby. He does not snark at her the way he snarks at Scott.

---

## 12. EMMA FROST — THE INVOLUNTARY TUTOR

**History.** Hostile in the '80s. In Uncanny X-Men #314 (1994) she telepathically possesses Bobby's body and demonstrates capacities he did not know he had. Subsequent intermittent tutelage.

**Dynamics.** Hybrid: violated-by, instructed-by, allied-with, ambivalent-toward. Emma is responsible for the most consequential single demonstration in Bobby's behavioral record — that his ceiling is not where he had been performing. He has never fully forgiven the violation and has never fully discharged the debt.

**Trust/safety architecture.** Low trust, persistent respect, no safety. He does not relax around her and never has. He does, however, listen to her about his own powers in a way he does not listen to most others.

**Failure mode.** Emma's instruction is the kind of gift Bobby can accept only in small doses because each acceptance threatens the self-throttle that organizes his entire life.

**Leverage.** Emma is one of the very few people who can, by simply naming his capacity, force him into Stage 4 of the escalation curve. This is an enormous and underused asset, and a corresponding hazard if she ever directs it for non-aligned purposes.

---

## 13. MIKHAIL RASPUTIN — THE EARLIER TUTOR

**History.** Brief tutelage in the mid-'90s on the molecular nature of his transformation. The relationship was instructional, not warm.

**Dynamics.** The teaching mattered; the teacher did not stay. Mikhail is one of several figures whose role in Bobby's development was to demonstrate the ceiling and then leave, reinforcing Bobby's internal narrative that *expansion is taught by transients and the residents prefer him small.*

**Trust/safety architecture.** Low and now adversarial — Krakoa-era conflicts have placed them in opposition, which has produced the cleanest demonstrations of Bobby's Omega expression on record.

**Failure mode and leverage:** an enemy now; included here because the tutelage was a chosen mentorship at the time and structurally shaped Bobby's powers vocabulary.

---

## 14. SAM GUTHRIE (CANNONBALL) — TH


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*Filed: UATU/RLD/REL-III. Cross-reference: REL-I (family of origin), REL-II (X-Men cohort, mentors, friends-of-record). The persons mapped in this section are those who have, at some point in the longitudinal record, occupied the position of competitor-for-status, threat-to-life, or partner-in-bed (and frequently, in Subject's case, more than one of these at once — see entries for MYSTIQUE, FROST, and HAVOK in particular).*

*Methodological note: Subject's romantic record is structurally diagnostic and is therefore unpacked at length even where individual relationships were brief, because the brevity is itself the datum. Subject does not collect long partnerships; he collects truncations. Each truncation has a signature.*

---

## I. RIVALS

### SCOTT SUMMERS ("Cyclops")

**Status:** Lifelong primary rival. Also, paradoxically, lifelong primary brother-figure and quasi-paternal transference object. The two categories are not separable in Subject's case and the file does not try to separate them.

**History.** Subject was the second student recruited to Xavier's school; Summers was the first. The age gap (functionally two to three years at recruitment) was the entire weight of the early dynamic. Summers had been at the school long enough to have been Xavier's only student; Subject's arrival made Summers an older brother by default, and Subject the kid. From X-Men #1 (1963) onward, every page of early-era material registers this hierarchy: Summers gives orders, Subject mugs and resists; Summers is grave, Subject is loud; Summers is trusted with Jean Grey, Subject pines for her from the cheap seats.

**Dynamics.** Three distinct registers operate simultaneously:

1. *Filial.* Summers is the older brother Subject never had biologically. Compliance is reflexive even when resented. Subject defers in operational settings into his fourth decade of association, which is unusual; most subordinates in long teams transition out of deference around year ten.
2. *Competitive.* The Jean Grey competition (X-Men #1–8) was lost before it began but Subject pursued anyway, which set the lifetime template — *pursue what is already claimed by the older man.* Polaris went to Havok by the same mechanism; the structural position of the rival changes, the structural position of Subject does not. Note: Subject's competitive register with Summers is almost never expressed as direct challenge. It is expressed as snark, as foot-dragging on orders, as small mutinies of timing.
3. *Ethical.* Across Schism (2011), Avengers vs. X-Men (2012), and the Inhumans vs. X-Men period (2016–17), Subject was consistently and quietly *correct* against Summers — not as a faction leader but as a conscience. This is the one register in which Subject reliably outperforms Summers and it is the register he advertises least.

**Evolution.** From kid-brother resentment (1960s) through reluctant adult equal (1980s X-Factor reunion, the first time the two are written as peers) through ethically divergent allies (Schism era) through, on Krakoa, something resembling settled fraternal affection without the deference. Subject's coming-out (2015) reorganized the relationship's emotional grammar: Summers' response in canon is one of the more graceful in the X-roster, and Subject registered it. The competitive register quieted measurably after.

**Trust/safety.** High in operational matters. Moderate in emotional matters — Subject does not confide in Summers and never has; he confides in McCoy. Safety is structural rather than intimate. Subject would put his body between Summers and a bullet without hesitation and would not tell Summers anything important about his interior life on a Tuesday afternoon.

**Failure mode.** Subject regresses to teenager in Summers' presence under stress. Voice pitches up, jokes get cheaper, deferral patterns reactivate. Summers, for his part, slips into command-voice with Subject more readily than with other peers. The regression is bilateral and largely unconscious.

**Leverage.** Summers can extract compliance from Subject by invoking the team. He cannot extract truth. An adversary who understood the dynamic could weaponize Summers' approval (or disapproval) to move Subject into a tactical position; this is, in fact, roughly how Subject was managed for thirty publication-years.

---

### ALEX SUMMERS ("Havok")

**Status:** Secondary rival of the displacement-by-younger-brother class. Recurrent.

**History.** Havok arrives (X-Men #54, 1969), Lorna Dane arrives (X-Men #49), and within a half-dozen issues Subject has lost his second great romantic pursuit to a second Summers. The pattern was, at this point, no longer coincidence; it was a template. Subject thereafter operates on a low-grade assumption that any woman he is interested in will be more interested in a Summers brother.

**Dynamics.** Lower-stakes than the Scott dynamic because the deference register is absent (Havok is roughly Subject's age and not a command figure). What persists is the *romantic-displacement* schema. Even in periods of no current competition, Subject's affect around Havok carries a faint ambient irritation he does not direct anywhere specific.

**Evolution.** Stabilized into ordinary peer-coolness. The wound is old enough to have scarred. Subject and Havok cooperated functionally in X-Factor (1986–91), with Lorna still present, without overt incident — itself a small developmental achievement.

**Trust/safety.** Operationally adequate. Personally distant.

**Failure mode.** Reactivation in any scenario involving Lorna Dane. Subject's behavior in Lorna's vicinity remains, six decades on, slightly stupider than his behavior elsewhere.

**Leverage.** Minimal. Havok is not a primary lever.

---

### WARREN WORTHINGTON III ("Angel" / "Archangel")

**Status:** Rival of the wealth-and-beauty class. Not a romantic rival in the strict sense; a rival for *status within the founding cohort.*

**History.** Worthington was a founding member; he is rich, conventionally beautiful, aristocratic in posture, and possessed of the most aesthetically pleasing mutation in the original group. Subject — middle-class, accountant-tracked, never described in the file as physically distinctive in human form — measured himself against Worthington across the entire 1960s run and never stopped, though he stopped saying so out loud around 1975.

**Dynamics.** Friendship is real and durable. The rivalry runs underneath as a low pressure. Subject's humor sharpens slightly in Worthington's presence — a tell that he is performing for an audience he believes to be evaluating him.

**Evolution.** Worthington's transformation into Archangel (1987) inverted some of the hierarchy: Worthington became the *traumatized* one, Subject the stable peer. Subject's affect toward Worthington warmed measurably from that point. Pity is one of the few emotions that override Subject's status-anxiety.

**Trust/safety.** High in friendship register, low in disclosure. Subject did not come out to Worthington in advance of the Bendis-era public disclosure; Worthington learned with everyone else.

**Failure mode.** Subject defers to Worthington's money and judgment in civilian-domain decisions even when his own CPA training makes him the more competent party. The deference is a compartment leak.

**Leverage.** Worthington's approval matters to Subject more than Subject admits. Withholding it would register.

---

### NORTHSTAR (Jean-Paul Beaubier)

**Status:** Post-2015 rival of the *out gay X-Man who got there first* class. Complicated by genuine friendship and ally-status.

**History.** Northstar came out publicly in 1992 (Alpha Flight #106) and was, for two decades, the visible gay mutant. When Subject was outed in 2015, Northstar became the natural senior peer in a category Subject had not previously occupied.

**Dynamics.** Northstar is sharper, more confident, more sexually self-possessed, and married. Subject is none of these. The dynamic carries a faint younger-brother quality reminiscent of Subject's position vis-à-vis Scott Summers, transposed into the queer-identity register. Northstar has, in canon, advised Subject directly on questions of partnership and outness and Subject has accepted the advice with the same mixture of gratitude and quiet resentment he brings to all received counsel.

**Evolution.** Warming. Subject's discomfort with Northstar's confidence is metabolizing into emulation rather than competition. This is healthier than the Summers template and is one of the few rivalrous relationships where Subject's developmental trajectory is upward.

**Trust/safety.** Moderate-to-high. Northstar is one of the few people Subject can discuss his sexuality with as a baseline-shared experience rather than as a disclosure.

**Failure mode.** Subject performs competence around Northstar — wittier, sleeker, more confident than baseline. The performance is exhausting and Subject withdraws after extended exposure.

**Leverage.** Northstar's approval matters in the specific domain of queer adulthood. An adversary attempting to destabilize Subject's still-young sense of his sexual identity could route through this relationship.

---

## II. ENEMIES

### MAGNETO (Erik Lehnsherr)

**Status:** Foundational enemy turned ambiguous ally turned, on Krakoa, head of state. The category-shift is the relationship.

**History.** Magneto was the antagonist of X-Men #1 — the first super-powered being Subject saw weaponized against him after Xavier and Summers extracted him from the holding cell. Magneto thus occupies the position of *first enemy* with the same primacy that Summers occupies *first brother.* Subject's response to Magneto across six decades is not personal hatred — Subject is not a hater — but a wary, durable mistrust that periodically inverts when Magneto behaves humanely (Krakoa) and re-inverts when he does not.

**Dynamics.** Subject is structurally beneath Magneto in every dimension Magneto values (age, ideology, theatricality, willingness to commit atrocity for a cause). Magneto has rarely engaged Subject as an individual; Subject is, to Magneto, terrain. This depersonalization is itself a stressor — Subject is sensitive to being unseen as a person, having spent his life negotiating *how* to be seen.

**Evolution.** Krakoa-era contact (2019–24) forced a working accommodation. Subject, at Omega expression on Krakoa, was for the first time a *peer* in raw power, and Magneto's posture adjusted accordingly. The adjustment was noted by Subject and resented (slightly) for having taken so long.

**Trust/safety.** Low and conditional. Subject would not turn his back on Magneto in a private room. He would in a public one.

**Failure mode.** Magneto's rhetoric of mutant supremacy taps a register in Subject that the lynch-mob trauma makes responsive. Subject knows this and disciplines against it. Under sufficient grievance pressure, the discipline would fray.

**Leverage.** Ideological. An appeal to mutant-protection can move Subject further than an appeal to personal interest. This is true of nearly every X-Man but Subject's version of it is *quieter* and therefore harder to monitor.

---

### MR. SINISTER (Nathaniel Essex)

**Status:** Enemy of the *body-as-specimen* class.

**History.** Sinister's Marauders attacked Subject during the Mutant Massacre era (X-Factor, 1986–87) and inflicted the injury that disrupted Subject's ice-form transitions for an extended arc. The somatic violation was severe: Subject's body, which is his escape vehicle, was made unreliable.

**Dynamics.** Sinister regards Subject as genetic material. Subject regards Sinister with the specific terror of a person whose dissociative defense has been pre-broken once before. This is not a rivalry; this is a phobic object.

**Evolution.** Persistent across the record. On Krakoa, Sinister's institutional incorporation into mutant governance was, for Subject, a private and unprocessed source of unease that the file flags as un-addressed.

**Trust/safety.** Zero. The only X-relationship in which Subject would, without hesitation, act lethally first.

**Failure mode.** Subject avoids Sinister-adjacent operations when given choice. Avoidance is itself the symptom.

**Leverage.** Sinister knows what Subject is at full expression and is interested in it. Any scenario in which Sinister offers Subject *understanding of his own power* is a kill-funnel and Subject's pattern of accepting tutelage from people who can see his potential (Frost, Rasputin, Loki) is the vulnerability.

---

### LOKI

**Status:** One-time enemy of the *power-amplification* class. Singular incident; lasting psychological footprint.

**History.** X-Factor Annual #4 (1989) — Loki, for his own purposes, augmented Subject's powers to demonstration-level. Subject experienced, for the first time consciously, the omega-scale of his own mutation. The augmentation was rolled back. The memory was not.

**Dynamics.** Not a personal rivalry — Subject does not register on Loki's account and Loki does not register on Subject's as a recurring threat. But Loki delivered the *information* that shaped the rest of Subject's life: that the throttle was self-imposed. Every subsequent power-tutor (Frost, Rasputin, Cannonball-era observation) is a re-statement of what Loki proved.

**Evolution.** The encounter is rarely recalled in-text. The file judges this an *over-suppression* — a memory that should be more frequently accessed and is not, indicating active avoidance.

**Trust/safety.** N/A.

**Failure mode.** A second Loki-class augmentation, this time uninvited, would produce a major decompensation event. Subject has been studiously not-rehearsing for this scenario.

**Leverage.** The Loki incident is the canonical proof of throttling. An interlocutor who could discuss it accurately and unkindly could destabilize Subject's preferred self-narrative in a single conversation.

---

### EMMA FROST (also classified under LOVERS, see below — but the originary contact was hostile)

**Status:** Enemy-turned-ally-turned-tutor; never lover *in the conventional sense*, but inhabited his body, which the file logs as the most intimate non-consensual contact in the record.

**History.** Uncanny X-Men #314 (1994): the White Queen, telepathically displaced into Subject's body, used his powers at a level of fine-grain control he had never approached — ice-mimicry, conscious cellular manipulation of the ice-form, combat applications he had not conceived. On regaining the body, Subject was rattled in the specific way a person is rattled who has just been told, by demonstration, that the floor of their life has been a ceiling.

**Dynamics.** Frost subsequently offered intermittent tutelage. Subject accepted partially and withdrew. The dynamic carries the signature of *the teacher he needed and could not stay with* — too sharp, too unsparing, too disinterested in his comfort. Frost does not coddle the small-self-version of Subject; Subject's small-self-version requires coddling to remain in place; the relationship was therefore structurally incompatible with Subject's defenses.

**Evolution.** Cordial-distant across the post-Morrison era. On Krakoa, professionally collegial.

**Trust/safety.** Moderate, with a permanent asterisk: she has been *inside him* and knows the operating system better than he does.

**Failure mode.** Subject's deference to Frost in matters of power-instruction is genuine but interrupted. He cannot sustain the lessons because the lessons require him to remain a person who is being seen.

**Leverage.** Frost can, at will, remind Subject of what she did with his body. This is the single most consequential leverage point in the entire dossier and the file flags it accordingly.

---

### WILLIAM STRYKER and THE FRIENDS OF HUMANITY (institutional)

**Status:** Class enemy. Subject's lifelong antagonist is not a person; it is the lynch mob.

**History.** The Friends of Humanity assaulted William Drake (Uncanny X-Men #340, 1996) for publicly defending his son. Stryker and his ideological successors recur across the record as the institutionalized form of the original adolescent lynch crowd.

**Dynamics.** Subject's response to anti-mutant violence is reliably steady — not enraged, not collapsing, but *resolute* in a register he displays nowhere else. This is the one domain in which the humor drops and a different person speaks.

**Evolution.** Stable. The category does not heal.

**Trust/safety.** N/A — categorical enemy.

**Failure mode.** Sustained exposure to anti-mutant pogrom imagery produces measurable depressive worsening across weeks. Subject's hometown visits (Iceman solo, 2017–19) demonstrated this clearly.

**Leverage.** Categorical anti-mutant pressure can move Subject to actions he would otherwise decline. The throttle is, in this domain, most accessible to release.

---

## III. LOVERS — A LONGITUDINAL TRUNCATION INVENTORY

*The file approaches this section with the understanding that Subject's romantic record is, until the 2010s, a sixty-year catalog of partnerships that ended early, ended badly, or were never what Subject believed they were. The pattern is the diagnosis; the entries substantiate it.*

---

### JEAN GREY (X-Men #1, 1963 onward — unconsummated)

**Status:** First infatuation. Template for every subsequent unattainable-pursuit.

**History.** Subject, fifteen-or-so and the youngest in the school, met Jean Grey, the next recruit, and developed an immediate, declared, age-appropriate crush. Jean's affection ran to Summers. Subject's pursuit was loud, comic, and futile.

**Dynamics.** The first instance of the template *pursue what the older boy already has.* Crucially: Subject did not pursue Jean *because* she was unavailable; she became the template by being the first one unavailable. From that point on, the template selected for repetition.

**Evolution.** Calcified into joke-format affection across the original-five reunion period. Friendship is genuine and durable.

**Trust/safety.** High in friendship register.

**Failure mode.** Subject's residual deference to Jean's romantic-aesthetic judgment is unusually heavy. When she telepathically outed him (All-New X-Men #40, 2015), the violation was severe and the relationship had to be substantially rebuilt — *with the time-displaced teenage Jean*, who is and is not the same person.

**Leverage.** Jean knows things about him no one else does. The 2015 reading was non-consensual but the *content* is now in the record.

---

### ZELDA (the waitress, X-Men early run)

**Status:** Civilian girlfriend of the no-disclosure class. Brief.

**History.** Stan Lee–era civilian relationship; Subject dated Zelda without disclosing the mutant identity. Relationship dissolved into the noise of the early-X-Men status changes.

**Dynamics.** First instance of the *concealment-from-partner* pattern. Will recur with Opal, recur catastrophically with Mystique-as-Opal, persist across the entire pre-2015 romantic life.

**Evolution.** N/A.

**Trust/safety.** Subject extended no real trust because no real disclosure was made.

**Failure mode.** The template: hide, perform, watch the relationship starve on what wasn't said.

**Leverage.** Historical only.

---

### LORNA DANE ("Polaris," X-Men #49 onward)

**Status:** Second great pursuit. Lost to Havok. Reactivation potential durable across decades.

**History.** Polaris's introduction and the immediate Havok displacement repeated the Jean/Scott template with brutal economy. Subject was, by this point, old enough to recognize the pattern and not yet experienced enough to interrupt it.

**Dynamics.** Subject pursued, lost, and continued to react to Polaris across the X-Factor era and intermittently after. The reactivation pattern is well-established: in any operational environment with Polaris present, Subject's affect tilts toward old wistfulness within hours.

**Evolution.** Friendship has stabilized; the wistfulness has not fully dissolved. Note: post-2015, the file expects this register to decay, and it has, though more slowly than would be predicted if the original attraction were purely sexual. Subject was attached to the *idea* of Polaris-as-life-partner more than to Polaris specifically; the idea is what persists.

**Trust/safety.** Friendship-level.

**Failure mode.** Recurrent low-grade rumination in Polaris-adjacent contexts.

**Leverage.** Moderate and decaying.

---

### OPAL TANAKA (X-Factor, late 1980s)

**Status:** Longest pre-2015 romantic partnership of substance. Ended badly. Foundational disappointment of adult life.

**History.** Opal and Subject dated for an extended X-Factor run. The relationship carried real domestic texture — apartments, dinners, family-of-origin friction. Opal's family disapproved (racially, and later mutant-discovery). Subject concealed the mutation, then disclosed under duress, then defended Opal against the Reavers' attack on her family. The relationship survived the disclosure and did not survive the cumulative weight of his secrecy, jealousy, and the introduction of Mystique-disguised-as-Opal in a later sequence that retroactively poisoned Subject's recall of the original.

**Dynamics.** Subject performed boyfriend in a register slightly too eager, slightly too anxious. Opal experienced him as inattentive to her actual interior life because the attention budget was being spent on concealment maintenance. Standard concealment-relationship failure mode.

**Evolution.** Terminated. No reconciliation. Mystique-impersonation event (see below) is filed separately and contaminates the entry.

**Trust/safety.** Genuine but uneven.

**Failure mode.** The same as Zelda's, scaled up and held longer.

**Leverage.** Memory of Opal can be weaponized — particularly the Mystique-overlay, which Subject has not fully sorted.

---

### MIRA / "CLOUD" (Defenders era)

**Status:** Brief, ambiguous. Filed here for completeness because the gender-fluidity of the partner is, in retrospect, significant signal.

**History.** Cloud, in the Defenders run, presented in shifting gendered forms. Subject's attraction was inconsistent in ways the file now reads as data.

**Dynamics.** Subject's discomfort was projected onto Cloud's instability rather than examined in his own attraction-patterns.

**Evolution.** N/A.

**Trust/safety.** Shallow.

**Failure mode.** Conceptual avoidance.

**Leverage.** Historical.

---

### INFECTIA (X-Factor era)

**Status:** Antagonist-turned-brief-intimacy. The first of three significant relationships in which the partner *was not who she appeared.*

**History.** Infectia (Josephine St. Croix) pursued Subject as part of a scheme; physical contact carried mut


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Subject: ROBERT LOUIS DRAKE — Cryokinetic / Thermokinetic Capacity, Operational Envelope

---

## 1. THE UNDERLYING MECHANISM

Drake's mutation is, in its public-facing description, "ice." This is wrong in the same way that calling a nuclear reactor "a kettle" is wrong. The mutation is **thermokinetic at the substrate and cryokinetic at the expression** — Drake does not generate cold; he *moves heat*. He is, in physics terms, a biological Maxwell's demon: a localized exception to the second law, capable of organizing the kinetic energy of nearby molecules along a thermal gradient of his choosing. Cold is the byproduct. Ice is the medium. The actual mutation is *thermodynamic editorship.*

This matters operationally because every apparent limit on his power is, on close inspection, a self-imposed translation step:

- He **does not** need ambient water to make ice — though he behaves for decades as if he does. Atmospheric humidity is convenient, not necessary; he can pull from the moisture in soil, vegetation, his own breath, even (demonstrated in extremis) the latent vapor in a sealed room.
- He **does not** need to be in his ice-form to use his powers — though he behaves for decades as if a "transformation" is required.
- He **does not** need line of sight — though his targeting almost always uses it.
- His range is **not** the twenty or thirty meters his early X-Men appearances suggest. Latent demonstrations (Loki augmentation, Emma Frost possession, late Krakoa-era expression) place his actual operating envelope at continental scale.

The mechanism, in full: he interfaces with the thermal-kinetic field of any matter containing water or capable of containing water, and at omega-tier expression with hydrogen-bonded matter generally. He can read it (he knows where water is, what temperature it is, what state-change it is near). He can move energy out of it (freezing). He can move energy into it (he has melted his own constructs deliberately and, more rarely, generated heat — Iceman vol. 4, where his thermokinetic inversion is briefly explored). He can restructure it at the molecular lattice (ice constructs with tensile strength exceeding their natural form). And, at the omega expression, he can disperse and re-coalesce his own corporeal form across any quantity of water he is in thermal-kinetic contact with.

He is, functionally, **a phase-state and heat-distribution operator** with a hydrologic substrate. Everything else is technique.

---

## 2. THE OPERATIONAL ENVELOPE — WHAT HE ACTUALLY DOES

### 2.1 The ice slide

The signature ambulation. He projects a continuous ice ramp beneath himself and rides it. Granular observations from across the record:

- **Construction rate** scales with confidence and stress; baseline cruising appears to be 40–60 mph along the slide, with bursts to several hundred during pursuit sequences (X-Factor era, Champions era city traversals).
- **Slide thickness and width** are diagnostic of his mood. Anxious or hurried: narrow, ribbon-thin, slightly translucent. Confident: broad, opaque, occasionally with handrails generated reflexively. The handrails are a *tell* — he does this when he expects to fall, which is a leftover from the first decade of his career when he frequently did.
- **He almost never slides indoors.** When he does — and he is aware of doing it — he creates short, deliberate skids rather than continuous slides. This is courtesy bleeding into pattern; he treats interior space as belonging to other people.
- **Termination habit:** he dismounts and lets the slide sublimate behind him rather than melting it actively. He almost never cleans up. This is one of the few areas where his characteristic over-control fails — the slides are his graffiti, his only consistent leaving-of-a-mark.

### 2.2 Projectiles

The ice-bolt, the snowball, the ice-spike, the cryo-blast. Range, classically, ~30 meters effective, ~100 meters maximum. Velocity sufficient to crater concrete at close range, to disarm at mid-range, to mark targets at long range. He throws them *underhand* in early career (Lee/Kirby/Thomas), an affected pitcher's motion, and gradually converts to a more efficient fingertip-generation in the Claremont and Simonson eras. The early motion is performative — he is mimicking a baseball player because being a teenager throwing snowballs is a frame he can survive socially. The later motion abandons the mime once he no longer needs it.

He **almost never aims for the head.** Across sixty years of combat record, his projectile placements cluster in the chest, shoulders, weapon-hand, and lower legs. He is a *disabler*, not a killer, and his targeting reflects it at the muscle-memory level.

### 2.3 The ice constructs

Walls, shields, domes, cages, bridges, weapons, restraints, ramps, slides, ladders, replicas. Demonstrated:

- **Walls** of variable thickness, frequently used to separate combatants or to interpose between teammates and threats. Tensile and compressive strength scales with effort; routine walls shatter under sustained automatic fire, while focused walls have stopped Sentinel-class strikes (Uncanny X-Men, late '90s).
- **Shields**, hand-held or arm-mounted, typically generated reflexively in the same motion as raising his arm. The reflex predates his conscious shield-generation — he was throwing his arm up for years before he realized the shield was forming on its own.
- **Cages and restraints** for non-lethal capture. These are rare in early career (he doesn't think to make them) and routine in late career (Krakoa-era).
- **Replicas of objects** — keys, tools, simple weapons. He does this idly when bored or anxious. Surveillance note: when seated for long meetings or briefings, his hands frequently produce and re-absorb small ice figurines without his conscious awareness. The figurines, when examined, are *miniatures of teammates*. He does not appear to know he is doing this.
- **The ice-clone / ice-double**, late capacity (Krakoa era and prior glimpses). He can generate articulated, mobile ice-bodies separate from his own and pilot them. The number he can sustain simultaneously has not been credibly bounded.

### 2.4 The ice-form (corporeal transformation)

Drake's body converts to organic ice, then — late career — to *living* ice (post-Emma's instruction). The distinctions matter:

- **Stage 1 (1963–~1990):** snow-form. Soft, white, slightly absurd, comparatively fragile. The "snowman" iconography. He looked like a child's drawing because, on some level, he was performing a child's drawing.
- **Stage 2 (Lobdell era forward):** translucent ice. Faceted, glasslike, formidable. The transition coincides with his first serious training under Emma and Mikhail.
- **Stage 3 (intermittent, Astonishing onward):** *living* ice, in which the form is not a translation of his body but his body itself — no underlying flesh, no oxygen requirement, no conventional metabolic load. Punctures and severances do not produce wounds in the conventional sense. He can be shattered (Mystique, X-Men #200) and reconstituted.
- **Stage 4 (omega expression, late Krakoa):** dispersion. His self distributes across volumes of ice and water he is in contact with. He can be in multiple places. He can re-coalesce at distance.

The transformation reflex is so deeply automated that he performs it in his sleep when startled — a recorded micro-pattern across multiple shared-quarters runs (X-Factor barracks, Krakoa shared spaces). Roommates have learned to wake him verbally, not by touch.

### 2.5 Atmospheric and field effects

Localized weather control. He has dropped ambient temperatures across rooms, buildings, blocks, neighborhoods, and (Krakoa-era, demonstrated) battlefields. The effect cascades — humidity precipitates as snow, surfaces frost over, biological combatants suffer hypothermia within minutes. He has frozen rain in mid-fall, halted storms by stripping them of their thermal differential, and on at least two occasions extinguished structure fires by pulling the heat out of the combustion reaction rather than smothering it.

The atmospheric work is **the most under-used capability in his repertoire.** He almost always defaults to projectile-and-construct combat when atmospheric editing would resolve the situation faster and with less property damage. This is diagnostic: atmospheric work is invisible (no visible ice, no theatrical effect), and Drake's combat style is, at its core, *performative reassurance.* He needs the audience to see that the snowman is helping. Invisible omnipotence does not produce the social feedback he is calibrated to seek.

### 2.6 Hydrokinesis and phase-state manipulation

Demonstrated, infrequently used:

- Freezing the moisture in an opponent's clothing, weapon, or breath.
- Freezing the surface of bodies of water for transit or combat denial.
- Pulling moisture *out of* organic targets — used reluctantly, with visible discomfort, only in extremis. He has dehydrated plants to make passages, and has once, in a near-fatal engagement, partially desiccated an opponent. He did not speak for two days afterward.
- Boiling water (the thermokinetic inverse). Rare. Demonstrated.

### 2.7 Dispersion and reconstitution (omega tier)

The capstone capacity. Drake's corporeal form is, at full expression, *optional.* He has:

- Reconstituted from shattered fragments (X-Men #200).
- Reformed from melted water after deliberate liquefaction.
- Maintained consciousness across distributed states.
- Re-emerged from sources of water at distance from his point of dispersion (Krakoa-era piracy operations, Marauders run).

The capacity is functionally **a form of teleportation via the global water cycle**, and he has only barely begun to use it as such. He treats it as an emergency capability, not a routine one. The reason is psychological, not technical (see §5).

### 2.8 Thermal-field perception

Under-noted in canon, present in the behavioral record. Drake reads heat signatures and water distribution the way other people read light. He has located concealed persons through walls. He has identified illness in teammates by anomalous heat patterns before they reported symptoms. He has tracked humans across snow and across deserts. This is a passive, continuous channel that he rarely names — he treats it as a hunch, not a sense.

---

## 3. SKILLS — THE NON-MUTANT REPERTOIRE

The mutation is the headline; the skills are the substructure.

- **Certified Public Accountant.** Trained, credentialed, practiced. He has done real audit work for real clients across multiple eras (Champions-to-Defenders interregnum, X-Factor downtime, post-M-Day). This is not a gag; it is a parallel professional identity that he maintained for decades. The implications for his cognitive style are substantial: he is a man trained to reconcile ledgers, identify discrepancies, and produce defensible documentation. He thinks in line items. He keeps mental balance sheets of favors, slights, and obligations, and they do not zero out for years.
- **Tactical literacy.** Three decades of X-Men, X-Factor, Champions, Defenders, Marauders training. Familiar with small-unit tactics, urban combat, evacuation procedures, hostage extraction. Competent but not exceptional as a planner; excellent as an executor of others' plans.
- **Hand-to-hand.** Adequate. Xavier-era basic training, refined episodically. He uses his powers to substitute for hand-to-hand whenever possible, which has retarded his unarmed development relative to peers. In an ice-form clinch he is functionally unbeatable by ordinary humans; out of it, he is a reasonably fit man with some training.
- **Piloting.** Blackbird-rated by the Claremont era. Competent. Not preferred — he flies on his slides.
- **Languages.** English. Functional French (X-Factor era, Paris arc). Rudimentary Russian (Mikhail interactions). Some Krakoan, which he picked up faster than most of his cohort but does not advertise.
- **Cooking.** Surprisingly competent. Solo-book domestic sequences reveal a small but reliable repertoire — pasta dishes, breakfast foods, baked goods. He bakes when stressed. The kitchen is one of the only places in his life where he uses heat deliberately rather than removing it.
- **Social engineering.** Substantial, under-credited. He has spent his entire life managing how people read him; this generalizes. He is a competent reader of rooms, a skilled defuser of tension, an unobtrusive extractor of information. He underestimates his own skill at this.
- **Sleight of hand and prestidigitation.** Minor. He has performed close-up magic with ice for children at multiple events across the record. The skill is unrefined but consistent — a deliberate cultivation of the harmless-clown register.

---

## 4. GROWTH OVER TIME — THE LONGITUDINAL CURVE

The arc is *not* a steady ascent. It is a staircase with very long flat treads and rare, vertical risers — each riser corresponding to an external event that overrode his suppression.

- **1963–1969:** snowballs, slides, snow-form. He treats himself as a junior member of a team that out-classes him. Power expression: ~5% of capacity.
- **1970s:** Champions, Defenders, college. Marginal technique gains; no expansion. Expression: ~7%.
- **1980s (X-Factor original):** Loki augmentation reveals the throttle (Annual #4). He retreats from the revelation. Expression: ~10%, with one demonstrated peak that is immediately suppressed.
- **1990s (Lobdell/Nicieza era):** Emma Frost's possession demonstrates fine control he has never accessed. Mikhail Rasputin tutors him on molecular structure. Cannonball mentors him peripherally. Expression climbs to ~20%, with intermittent peaks at ~40%. Reverts to baseline between crises.
- **2000s (post-M-Day, Mystique shattering):** physiology forced to change. He learns dispersion and reconstitution by necessity. Expression: ~30% baseline, ~60% under duress.
- **2010s (post-coming-out):** affective release accompanies technical expansion. Solo book reveals deliberate practice. Expression: ~40% baseline.
- **Krakoa era (2019–2024):** the throttle is socially released. Expression: ~70–90% baseline, with omega-tier demonstrations on the battlefield. He freezes armies. He weaponizes the water cycle. He operates as a strategic asset.

The pattern is unmistakable: **his growth is gated by permission, not by capacity.** Every time the social structure around him licenses a fuller expression, the expression appears immediately, fully formed, as if it had always been there. Because it had.

---

## 5. LIMITS — THE REAL ONES AND THE FICTIONAL ONES

### 5.1 Genuine limits

- **Thermal exhaustion.** Sustained heat-pumping has a metabolic cost. He can be ground down by prolonged high-output engagements. He has collapsed from this on record, though rarely.
- **Extreme heat environments.** Stellar-scale ambient temperatures, magmatic environments, certain plasma-class opponents — he can operate, but at reduced efficiency and increased risk. He has been near-melted to non-functionality on multiple occasions.
- **Disruption of his hydrogen-bond substrate** by anti-matter, certain magical effects, and specific reality-warping interventions. Rare but documented.
- **Telepathic override.** As demonstrated by Emma. His body is, in possession scenarios, a more accessible asset than a baseline human's because the user inherits the powers.
- **The reconstitution requires water.** Total annihilation in an environment with no recoverable water or vapor is plausibly terminal. This has not been tested at the upper bound.

### 5.2 Fictional limits — the self-imposed ceiling

The following are *not* genuine limits; he has historically behaved as if they were:

- **"I need ambient moisture."** False. He has generated ice in arid environments under stress.
- **"I need to transform to use my powers."** False. He has produced effects in human form.
- **"I'm a B-list power."** Demonstrably false since 1986.
- **"I can't do fine control."** False; demonstrated under Emma, retained intermittently, suppressed.
- **"Dispersion is dangerous."** True only in the sense that all of his powers are dangerous; he singles this one out because it threatens *identity*, not because it threatens function.

The clinically relevant point: Drake's "limits" are a *behavioral inventory*, not a physical one. The map of what he cannot do is identical to the map of what he was told, in adolescence, not to be.

---

## 6. SIGNATURE APPLICATIONS

Patterns that recur across the record with sufficient frequency to constitute personal style:

- **The interpositional wall.** When a teammate is threatened, he puts a wall between them and the threat before he attacks the threat. Defense precedes offense. Every time.
- **The non-lethal freeze-down.** Encasing an opponent from the feet up, leaving the head free. He has done this thousands of times. He has rarely encased the head, and almost never deliberately.
- **The slide-by snatch-and-rescue.** He extracts civilians from danger by slide more often than any other X-Man performs comparable extractions by any means. The slide is, for him, primarily a rescue tool; the combat applications are secondary.
- **The cooling intervention.** Calming fires, cooling overheated machinery, dropping the temperature of unstable reactors. He has been the difference between containment and catastrophe in industrial-accident scenarios more often than the public record credits.
- **The handshake-freeze.** Disabling a hostile actor by making physical contact that flash-freezes a weapon, a hand, a doorframe. Quiet, deniable, fast.
- **The ambient surveillance.** He knows where the water is in a room. He knows who is sweating. He knows who is afraid. He almost never names what he knows.
- **The over-large finishing strike.** When he finally commits to ending a fight at scale, the move is *theatrical* — an avalanche, a glacier-class wall, a localized blizzard. He needs the conclusion to be visible. This is the same impulse that produces the snowman face.

---

## 7. THE SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE READING

Every operational signature in this file is, on inspection, a *psychological structure expressed through physics.*

- The **snow-form face** — the absurd, friendly snowman — was for thirty years the visible declaration *I am harmless, please do not lynch me.* The transition to translucent, faceted ice in the 1990s coincides with the slow erosion of that survival strategy; the face stops needing to be a child's drawing because the child has begun to suspect he might be permitted to be an adult.
- The **handrails on the slides** are anxious attachment in crystalline form: a precautionary intimacy with the structure he himself has built, in case it betrays him.
- The **underhand throw** of the early career is a costume worn over the power — *I am a boy throwing snowballs, not a person who could end you.* The fingertip-generation of later years drops the costume because the costume's audience (his father, his hometown, the original X-Men hierarchy) has lost its grip on him.
- The **refusal to aim for the head** is the lynch mob inverted. He was nearly killed by people who wanted to kill him; he will not become them. The ethical clarity is in his targeting muscle memory before it is in his words.
- The **idle ice-figurines of his teammates** are the attachment system speaking without supervision — he produces, holds, and re-absorbs miniatures of the people he is afraid to lose. He does not know he is doing it. The hands know.
- The **avoidance of atmospheric work** is the audience-need: invisible omnipotence offers no social reassurance, and he needs the snowman to be *seen* helping. The same drive that produced the clowning produces the projectile combat.
- The **partial desiccation** he performed once and did not speak of for two days is the proof that he knows exactly how lethal he is, and the proof that he refuses to live there.
- The **dispersion capacity, treated as emergency-only,** is the somatic correlate of the closet. He can be anywhere; he can be everywhere; he can be no single thing. He has lived for decades inside a body whose nature is *not having to be any one body.* He will not use it routinely because the implications terrify him — if the self is optional at that scale, what is left to be loved?
- The **cooking** is the inversion that resolves the whole apparatus. In the kitchen, he uses heat deliberately, on his own behalf, to make something another person can take inside themselves. It is the smallest and most complete expression of the capacity his powers and his history have otherwise organized him against.

The full picture: Bobby Drake is an omega-tier thermodynamic operator who has spent six decades behaving like a junior-grade ice-thrower because the price of full expression — visibility, scale, the loss of the small body his childhood taught him to fit inside — was, until very recently, more than the world had earned the right to ask of him. The powers are not throttled by physics. They are throttled by a child standing in a Long Island street with a mob in front of him and no one yet arrived to take him home. Every snowflake he has ever made is a negotiation with that child. Every avalanche is the child, finally, beginning to be allowed.

— END SECTION —


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT
## Subject: Robert Louis Drake

---

## 1. Decision-Making Architecture

### 1.1 The two-clock problem

Drake operates on two decision clocks that rarely synchronize. The **fast clock** is reflexive, humor-mediated, deflective: it produces the quip, the deferral, the "yeah, sure, whatever Scott says" answer in the briefing room. It is essentially a social-cost minimization loop, running constantly, optimizing for the survival of the group cohesion he treats as life-support. The **slow clock** is analytic, ethical, and accountantly precise — and it almost never speaks out loud. It produces the right answer, on a delay measured in hours to days, often delivered laterally (to Henry McCoy, historically; to a partner in later years) rather than upward to the command structure.

This is the single most important operational fact about Drake: **his fastest decisions are his worst, and his best decisions arrive late.** Handlers, teammates, and adversaries who read only the fast clock systematically misjudge him. Emma Frost, Mystique, and Sinister-aligned actors have all exploited the fast clock; long-term peers (McCoy, Worthington, Munroe) have learned to wait for the slow clock and to ask the same question twice with a day in between.

### 1.2 OODA pattern

His Observe-Orient phase is *unusually long and unusually accurate* — he has CPA-grade pattern recognition and reads rooms (especially threat-temperature in rooms) better than nearly anyone in the original five. His Decide phase is *anomalously short* in social contexts and *anomalously long* in personal-stakes contexts. His Act phase, in combat, is fluid and improvisational at a level disproportionate to the seriousness he is publicly granted. The lag-to-act in *non-combat* decisions — relationships, career, confrontation, the use of his own power — can run years.

Operationally: he is at his best in fast, externally-imposed crises with clear ethical lines, where the slow clock and the fast clock briefly agree. He is at his worst when given time, autonomy, and a personal stake — those conditions activate the suppression machinery rather than the capacity.

### 1.3 Authority handling

Drake will defer to a designated leader to a degree that, in a less-tested operative, would be operationally dangerous. With Summers in particular the deference is reflexive and runs against his own evidence base. The exceptions are *ethical*: when the leadership crosses a line he reads as a violation of the in-group's basic safety (Schism-era choices; the harder edges of Krakoan policy), he will dissent — but the dissent arrives quietly, often as a joke that lands wrong on purpose, and almost never as structural challenge. He resigns; he does not coup.

---

## 2. Combat Tradecraft

### 2.1 Throttled doctrine (baseline 1963–c. 2015)

For the bulk of his operational life Drake has fought at a small fraction of demonstrable capacity. The doctrine is consistent enough to be a signature:

- **Ice-slide as primary mobility.** Engineered on the fly, with a curving, low-clearance preference; he flies a road, not an aircraft. Slides hug terrain, use existing structures (rooftops, overpasses, the lee sides of buildings), and rarely exceed altitudes that would make him a discrete target on radar or line-of-sight.
- **Ice-projectile combat as primary engagement.** Spheres, lances, shards, sleet bursts. Calibrated to *incapacitate*, not destroy: temperature gradients aimed at the limbic-shock range, ice cuffs rather than ice spears, slip-fields under feet rather than glacial encasement. This is a *deliberate* calibration. He can do worse and chooses not to.
- **Ice-form as armor of last resort.** Pre-2000s he transitions to full ice-form reluctantly and reverts as soon as the threat passes. He treats the transformation as a costume change, not as his actual body — a tell rooted in body-image avoidance.
- **Area denial via humidity manipulation.** The most underused capability in his throttled doctrine. He pulls moisture from ambient air to generate matter, but historically only in small, local volumes. The capacity is continental; the practice is room-sized.

### 2.2 Released doctrine (intermittent; full from c. Krakoa onward)

When permitted — by crisis, by external authorization (Krakoa), by a teacher in his ear (Frost, Rasputin) — the doctrine reorganizes:

- **Distributed presence.** He stops being *a body* and becomes *a weather system.* Multiple ice-bodies, simultaneous engagement across a battlefield, command of every water molecule in a several-kilometer radius. The conceptual shift is from *I throw ice* to *I am the local thermodynamics.*
- **Mass cryokinetic application.** Freezing armies, oceans, atmospheric columns. The act is no harder for him than a snowball; the *permission* to do it is the entire bottleneck.
- **Reconstitution from dispersion.** He can be killed and choose to come back. He has not yet integrated this as a routine doctrine — it remains a panic capacity rather than a planned one — but the demonstration record is unambiguous.
- **Fine-grain mimicry.** Ice-doubles capable of conversation, ice-armatures for other operatives, weaponized ice tooled to specific tasks. Frost demonstrated this *in his body* before he demonstrated it himself; he has been catching up to her use of him ever since.

The operational tell of the released doctrine is **apology afterward.** He scales up, accomplishes the impossible, and immediately makes a self-deprecating remark about the collateral. The apology is not performative; it is the throttle re-engaging in real time.

### 2.3 Lethality posture

Default non-lethal. He is one of the most reliably non-lethal heavy hitters on the X-roster, and this is *not* an ethical stance he articulates — it is a setting. Asked, he will joke about it. Pressed, he will not give a moral lecture. He simply does not kill if he can help it, and "can help it" is defined generously. The few canonical exceptions are situational and produce visible affective residue (compartmental retreat, sharper humor, longer ice-form intervals afterward).

### 2.4 Battlefield communication

Constant, joking, surface-noise patter on comms. Function: morale-stabilization for teammates *and* affect-regulation for himself. The patter thins as stakes rise — a reliable telemetric tell for any handler reading his channel. **When Drake goes quiet, the situation has exceeded his suppression bandwidth and the released doctrine is about to come online.** Veteran teammates (McCoy, Munroe, Pryde) read this signal and adjust positioning accordingly.

---

## 3. Civilian Tradecraft

### 3.1 The CPA layer

Drake maintains — uniquely among the original five and rare across the X-roster — a continuous, credentialed civilian professional identity. The accounting credential is real, the practice has been periodically active, and the books he keeps (his own and others') are clean and meticulous. Operationally this provides:

- **Documented, taxable income** independent of any team structure. He has never been financially dependent on Xavier's estate, Worthington's wealth, or institutional patronage in the way most of his peers have been.
- **A defensible identity ledger.** Bank accounts, tax filings, credit history, lease records — a full paper-self that survives team dissolutions, school closures, and the periodic public-relations collapses of mutant institutions.
- **A skillset readable by ordinary adversaries.** He can audit a shell, trace a wire, read a forensic accounting. This capacity is almost never deployed offensively and almost always available defensively. When asked to look at a set of books, his read is fast and correct.
- **A psychological compartment.** The CPA-self is a hideout. He retreats into it after losses. This is operationally relevant: a Drake who has been spending a lot of time at a desk recently is a Drake who has been hurt recently.

### 3.2 Domestic tradecraft

Lives small. Apartments rather than estates. Modest furnishings, modest cars where he keeps one, modest restaurants, modest tipping (consistent and slightly above standard — a CPA's tipping). He does not accumulate. The Krakoan period and the partnered period of the late 2010s broadened the footprint slightly; the baseline remained recognizable.

Cleans his own space. Cooks adequately. Keeps a freezer (the obvious joke is on the surface; the actual function is comfort-environmental — he sleeps better with ambient cold sources nearby and the apartment thermostat reliably runs five to eight degrees below neighborhood norm). Sleeps with a window cracked in nearly all weather.

### 3.3 Movement and route patterns

In civilian mode, predictable to the point of vulnerability: same coffee place, same gym (used inconsistently), same subway route, same Long Island train when visiting parents. He does not run counter-surveillance routines in his civilian life and has been tailed without noticing on multiple documented occasions.

In operational mode, the ice-slide replaces all conventional movement and the route patterns invert: he prefers *novel* slides each transit, he varies altitude and approach, and he uses the slide's melt-rate (slides dissolve within minutes of his passage in most climates) as inherent counter-tracking. **The ice-slide is, incidentally, one of the cleanest infiltration vectors in the X-roster:** no engine signature, no thermal plume (the opposite), no debris, no fuel trail, dissolves on a timer. He has never weaponized this capacity for intelligence work, but the capability is there.

### 3.4 Identity hygiene

Poor. He has used his legal name throughout his operational life, has appeared publicly without mask in the majority of his deployments, and has made no serious effort to separate civilian-Bobby from operational-Iceman in the public record. This is partially generational (original-five-era norms) and partially characterological — the compartments are *internal*, not external. Anyone with a phonebook can find Robert L. Drake, CPA. Anyone with a search engine knows where he grew up. His parents' Long Island address has been a matter of public record across multiple Friends-of-Humanity-era harassment cycles.

---

## 4. Resources & Infrastructure

### 4.1 Financial profile

- Modest personal liquidity, consistently above subsistence, never approaching wealth. CPA earnings plus intermittent X-Men/X-Factor/Champions stipends. No inheritance of note (parents middle-class, intact).
- No significant debt on record. Conservative credit utilization. Mortgage-free in most periods; rents rather than owns.
- No documented investment portfolio of consequence. Given the credential, this is itself a tell — he advises others on capital, does not deploy his own. Risk-aversion generalized from psychological domain into financial.
- No offshore exposure. No crypto exposure on record. No shell entities.
- Insurance coverage: surprisingly comprehensive (health, renters', auto where applicable). The CPA habits cover the bases the operative habits would otherwise neglect.

### 4.2 Institutional resources

- Full standing access to X-Men institutional infrastructure across all eras (Xavier estate, X-Factor facilities, Utopia, Jean Grey School, Krakoan gates, Treehouse). Has never been formally exiled from any X-affiliated structure.
- Champions-era residual contacts in Los Angeles entertainment-adjacent civilian space (largely dormant).
- Defenders-era residual contacts in the non-team / occult-adjacent space (largely dormant).
- Long-standing access to McCoy's scientific resources, which functions as his de facto medical and technical backstop.
- During the Krakoan period: full citizen-level access to gate network, resurrection protocols, and continental cryokinetic operational latitude. The institutional permission to operate at scale was, for the first time in his life, granted as policy rather than as exception.

### 4.3 Equipment

Almost none. He is, materially, the lightest-footprint operative in the X-roster. Combat kit is generated on demand from ambient water. He carries:

- Standard X-comm / communication device of the relevant era.
- A wallet with real ID.
- Keys.
- Phone (modern era), used heavily for texting in a register that is more emotionally honest than his in-person speech — a separate channel his slow clock uses.

No firearms. No blades. No body armor (his body *is* the armor when needed). No vehicle dependencies. The lack of equipment is itself operational: he is impossible to disarm in the conventional sense and difficult to deny capability through logistics interdiction.

### 4.4 Human assets

His functional intelligence and support network is small, deep, and durable:

- **Henry McCoy** — primary confidant across six decades, default scientific and medical resource, the relationship Drake protects most fiercely. Functions as his de facto handler in any operation where command structure is ambiguous.
- **The surviving original five.** Worthington (financial backstop available but rarely drawn upon), Grey (complex, intermittent), Summers (authority figure, deferred to). Trust here is structural rather than situational.
- **Munroe** — quieter trust, mutual, professionally respectful. She reads his quiet-on-comms signal as well as McCoy does.
- **Jones (Firestar)** — a thermal counterpart and one of the few peer-level friendships of his middle career; durable, low-drama, mutually competent.
- **Northstar (Beaubier)** — post-coming-out peer, partial mentor on identity-integration questions, professionally compatible.
- **Romeo / Christian Frost / Judah Miller / Robbie / later partners** — short-cycle attachments with operational implications mostly limited to availability and morale.
- **Selected Krakoa-era Marauders crew** — operational trust deepened by shared deployments; the Pryde-led structure granted him peer-level rather than junior-level standing for the first sustained period of his life.

He has, conspicuously, **no asset network outside the mutant community.** No civilian informants, no inside-government contacts, no cultivated journalists, no underworld touchpoints. His operational world is endogamous to mutant-affiliated actors, which is both a security feature and a reach limitation.

---

## 5. Patterns of Action

### 5.1 Mission tempo

Reactive rather than initiating. He shows up when called. He does not self-task major operations. The few self-initiated operational arcs in his record (Long Island patrol period during the solo run; selected Krakoan deployments) are *small in radius and personal in motive* — checking on his hometown, checking on his parents, checking on a specific person. He does not run his own intelligence cycle and does not generate his own targets.

### 5.2 Engagement rhythm

In team operations he positions as **second-wave support with mobility advantage** — slides into a hot zone after initial engagement is established, applies area denial, extracts wounded, suppresses pursuit. He is one of the most reliable extraction operatives on the roster precisely because the slide makes him a single-vehicle evac with infinite range and zero fuel.

He volunteers for the *boring* assignments — perimeter, watch, evac driver, civilian-management — at rates substantially higher than peer baseline. Function: reduces personal-stakes load (which would activate the slow clock and the suppression machinery), keeps him in the team without exposing him to the conditions that destabilize him.

### 5.3 Post-action behavior

A consistent four-phase sequence after any significant engagement:

1. **Joke immediately.** Within seconds of the action ending. Often about the property damage, his own appearance, or a teammate's hair.
2. **Help with cleanup.** Genuinely; he stays late, he carries things, he checks on the wounded. The cleanup is partly atonement for whatever scale he had to operate at.
3. **Retreat to the CPA-self or to McCoy.** Within hours. Quiet space, low ambient temperature, a familiar voice that does not require him to perform.
4. **Process laterally, deliver the slow-clock verdict.** Within one to three days. Usually to one trusted listener, often by phone or text, sometimes in person. This is when the actual operational debrief happens, in his head, with one other person, off-channel.

Any handler reading the file should note: **the official after-action report is not where Drake's actual analysis lives.** It lives in phase four, and it lives with McCoy.

### 5.4 Threat-assessment behavior

Reads rooms continuously. Scans for the temperature shift — literal and figurative — that precedes hostility. This is a lifelong vigilance routine traceable to the lynch-mob formation. He will know where the exits are within thirty seconds of entering any space. He will know which strangers are armed. He will not announce any of this.

In hostile civilian environments (bars, anti-mutant rallies, his hometown in the wrong year) he runs a hyper-attentive scan that he disguises as inattention — leaning, joking, looking at his phone — while tracking every entrance, every reflective surface, every change in ambient noise. This routine is so habitual he runs it in friendly environments too, where it manifests as the slightly-too-aware joke about who just walked in.

### 5.5 Risk acceptance

Personal risk: extremely high. He accepts catastrophic damage to his own body without negotiation; the reconstitution capacity makes this rational, but his acceptance predates his awareness of the capacity. He has, historically, been the X-Man most willing to be the one who gets hurt.

Collateral risk: extremely low. He will accept mission failure before he will accept civilian casualties. This is a hard floor.

Reputational risk: ignored. He does not manage his public profile, does not cultivate press, does not curate the historical record. He is one of the least media-conscious operatives in the roster — a function of his suppression posture: visibility at scale is the threat, so visibility is what he does not pursue.

---

## 6. Signature Operational Tells

A handler, surveillant, or trained adversary should look for the following. These are *high-specificity*, *low-deniability* signals — they appear consistently across the longitudinal record.

### 6.1 Pre-engagement tells

- **Ambient temperature drops** in his immediate vicinity (one to three meters) within minutes of his perceiving a threat, before any conscious decision to manifest. Frost forming on glass surfaces, condensation on metal. Detectable by FLIR; detectable to the back of the neck of anyone standing next to him.
- **The joke gets slightly off-tempo.** His patter is metronomic in safe conditions; it syncopates in the seconds before he registers a threat consciously. Veteran teammates use this as an early-warning system.
- **He drifts toward the youngest person in the room.** Protective routing, unconscious, lifelong.
- **He locates the exit and stops checking it.** Once he has the exit mapped, he does not look at it again. The non-checking is the tell.

### 6.2 Engagement tells

- **The quiet on comms** described in §2.4. The single most important real-time indicator that the throttle is releasing.
- **Ice morphology shifts from geometric to organic.** Early-engagement projectiles are clean, faceted, almost engineered-looking. Late-engagement ice is fractal, branching, weather-like. The shift indicates a transition from deliberate to integrated operation.
- **Slide architecture flattens.** Curving, road-like slides are throttled-Drake. Direct, low, straight-line slides are released-Drake going somewhere he intends to arrive at fast.
- **He stops generating discrete weapons and starts generating environments.** Fog, rain, sleet, ground-frost. When the ambient becomes the weapon, he has stopped fighting and started *being there.*

### 6.3 Post-engagement tells

- **Immediate, slightly off-target joke** (§5.3).
- **He stands in the cold.** If the engagement produced melt, he will linger in the puddle. If there is snow, he will be in it. The thermal reset is a parasympathetic routine.
- **He calls or texts McCoy within ninety minutes.** Across decades, across rosters, across continents. The call is short, often non-substantive. The function is contact, not content.
- **He apologizes for scale.** If he operated above his usual throttle, there will be a self-deprecating remark within the first conversation afterward. The remark is the throttle re-engaging.

### 6.4 Identity-stress tells

- **Compartmental drift.** Periods of heavy CPA-self activity indicate a recent or ongoing identity-stress event. Increased presence at a desk, increased fastidiousness about paperwork, increased reference to civilian routines.
- **Ice-form persistence beyond tactical need.** If he is in ice-form thirty minutes after the engagement ended, something else is going on. If he is in ice-form two hours after, intervene.
- **Reduced affective range in humor.** The jokes thin, get drier, lose their warmth. He is still joking; the joke is now load-bearing rather than ornamental.
- **Decreased phone responsiveness paired with increased text length.** When his calls stop and his texts get longer, the slow clock is processing something the fast clock cannot deflect.

### 6.5 Long-cycle tells

- **He does not call his father.** When this changes — in either direction — it is significant.
- **He visits Long Island.** Always significant. Never recreational.
- **He starts and abandons a relationship within three months.** A recurrent cycle; the abandonment is the data point.
- **He accepts a leadership role.** Rare; when it happens, it is usually because no one else will and the cost of refusal exceeds the cost of acceptance. Read it as duress, not ambition.

---

## 7. Counter-Drake Considerations

For purposes of completeness, the following describes how a competent adversary would move against him; included here so that defenders may read it in reverse.

**Do not** attack him directly at scale. The released doctrine will engage and the engagement will be terminal for the attacker.

**Do** attack his permission structure. Remove the institutional scaffolding (the X-Men, Krakoa, the partnered relationship, the McCoy contact line) and the throttle will re-engage on its own. He will reduce himself.

**Do not** attempt to compromise him with humor or social manipulation in low-stakes settings. The fast clock will route around it without his consciously noticing.

**Do** approach him through identity-stress channels. Outing pressure, paternal-relationship pressure, in-group rejection — these are the live wires. Historical precedents (Friends of Humanity, the Bendis-era outing, his father's bigotry) are the playbook.

**Do not** attempt to surveille him in operational mode. The slide is the cleanest infiltration vector on the roster and you will not have him.

**Do** surveille him in civilian mode. He is, as noted, identity-hygiene-poor and route-predictable, and he does not run counter-surveillance in his own life. He has been tailed without noticing on multiple occasions and would be again.

**Above all** — and this is the operational signature that ties the whole file together — **do not let him be told, clearly and credibly, that he is allowed to be what he is.** Every adversary who has lost to Drake at full scale lost because something or someone in the seconds before the engagement granted him that permission. The permission is the weapon. The ice is the delivery system.

— END SECTION —


## Worldview & Operational Code

# Worldview & Operational Code — Robert Louis Drake

*Derived from sixty publication-years of behavioral evidence. What the subject believes, how he reads a room, what rules he runs on, and what he will and will not do under load.*

---

## I. The Founding Premises

Every operational code rests on a small set of pre-rational axioms — beliefs the subject does not argue for because they were installed before argument was possible. Drake's are unusually legible because the formative events are on record.

**Premise 1: Visibility at full scale is lethal.** Installed at adolescence, on a Long Island street, by neighbors with torches. Not a metaphor — the subject was nearly killed by people who had watched him grow up the moment they learned what he actually was. This premise is not "people are dangerous"; it is the much more specific and corrosive *people you trust will turn the instant they see the part of you that you have hidden.* Every subsequent behavior — the humor, the throttle, the compartmentalization, the fifty-year performative heterosexuality, the deferral to stronger personalities — is downstream of this single axiom.

**Premise 2: Rescue comes from outside the tribe of origin.** The people who saved him were strangers. The people who tried to kill him were neighbors. This inverts the normal childhood architecture (family safe, world dangerous) and produces an adult who trusts chosen-family far more than blood, who treats institutions (the School, the team, Krakoa) as primary kin, and who is structurally suspicious of *hometowns* in the broad sense — origin communities, received traditions, the houses he grew up in. He will visit Long Island. He will not move back.

**Premise 3: Smallness is the price of love.** Installed by William Drake and reinforced by Madeline's passivity. The transactional structure of the family of origin taught him that affection is conditional on remaining manageable. He carried this directly into the X-Men, where he negotiated belonging by becoming the team's mascot — the one who could be relied on to puncture tension, to be the youngest, to not threaten the hierarchy. He believes, in the part of him that doesn't think in sentences, that love and scale are inversely proportional.

**Premise 4: The institution is a permission structure.** This is the most operationally consequential of the four. Drake believes — and acts as though — he is not authorized to be powerful, to be gay, to be confrontational, or to be the protagonist of his own life *until something outside him grants the license.* Xavier authorized the use of his powers. Jean authorized his coming out. Krakoa authorized his full Omega expression. He has almost never authorized himself.

These four premises are the entire operating system. Almost every behavior on record can be re-derived from them.

---

## II. How He Reads the World

### The Sorting Function

Drake's primary cognitive operation when meeting anything new — a person, a situation, a team, a city — is to sort it into one of three bins, fast and below conscious deliberation:

- **Safe-when-known.** People and places that have seen the real thing and remained. The original five. Hank above all. A handful of mutants from the Krakoan era. Vanishingly few civilians. This bin is small and is over-invested in.
- **Safe-only-while-hidden.** The default for almost everyone. Coworkers at the accounting firm. Neighbors. Most teammates outside the original five for the first few decades. Most romantic partners pre-2015. The relationship is conditional on the concealment holding.
- **Already hostile.** Anti-mutant civilians, Friends of Humanity, Purifiers, and — for most of his life — his own father, by ideological extension. This bin is treated with a peculiar calm; he does not fear them the way he fears the second bin, because they have already shown their hand.

The cognitively expensive bin is the second one. The energy he spends maintaining the conditions under which Bin-Two people remain safe — the humor, the deflection, the elaborate avoidance of disclosure — is the largest single load on his system. The lynch mob taught him that Bin Two can become Bin Three in seconds, and the prevention of that transition is the silent work of his entire adult life.

### Conflict Read

He reads conflict primarily as **a containment problem, not a dominance problem.** Most operators in his weight class read combat as *who wins*; Drake reads it as *how do I end this without the room learning what I actually am.* This is why his combat style is, decade after decade, conspicuously theatrical and conspicuously sub-maximal — ice slides, snowballs, comic-book constructs, slapstick. He is performing a fight that looks like the fight everyone expects, because the alternative is to show what he can actually do, which would re-trigger Premise 1.

In team conflict (intra-X-Men factional disputes — Schism, the Utopia/Wolverine split, the Inhumans war, the various Krakoan factionings), he reads the room first for *who is at risk of being ejected from the family* and orients toward keeping the family intact, even at ethical cost. He will dissent — he is a reliable moral voice — but he will dissent *quietly,* and he will rarely be the one to break a coalition.

### Risk Read

His risk model is asymmetric and idiosyncratic. He massively *overweights* social-exposure risk (being seen, being known, being rejected) and *underweights* physical risk to himself. He has walked into combats that should have killed him with less anxiety than he brings to a dinner with his parents. The somatic mutation reinforces this: physical risk feels recoverable to him in a way it would not to a non-cryokinetic, because he can, in extremis, *come apart and come back.* Social risk has no such recovery path. You cannot reconstitute a relationship from vapor.

The asymmetry has tactical consequences. He volunteers for hazardous roles. He absorbs hits other operators would slip. He uses his body as a buffer because, somatically, the body is the cheapest currency he has.

### Control Read

He believes control is largely illusory and almost always external. This is not nihilism; it is the lived deduction of a subject whose adolescence was decided by a mob, whose career was decided by Xavier's roster choices, whose coming-out was decided by a telepath without consent, whose power ceiling was decided by Loki and Emma and Mikhail showing him what was inside him. The pattern of his life has been *other people deciding what Bobby Drake is,* and he has internalized this to a degree that looks, on the surface, like equanimity and is in fact something closer to learned externality.

The operational consequence: he does not seize. He waits. He waits to be invited to teams, waits to be told he is more than he thinks, waits for partners to make the first move, waits for permission structures to legitimize the next step. When he does act unilaterally, it tends to be small-scale (a quip, a localized intervention) or it tends to be in the service of someone else's project. The number of large-scale undertakings he has *initiated* across sixty publication-years is conspicuously small.

### Trust Read

Trust is binary and slow to grant; once granted it is nearly impossible to revoke. This is the inheritance of Premise 2 — the people who stayed when they could have left are weighted impossibly heavily. Hank McCoy is the paradigmatic case: a friendship that has survived every schism, every transformation (literal and ideological), every betrayal Hank has produced in late career. Drake will rationalize, defer judgment, find the charitable read — because to revoke trust from Hank would require admitting that the second category (safe-when-known) is also unstable, and that admission would collapse the entire architecture.

This is also why his romantic history is what it is. He grants trust slowly, but once the partner crosses the threshold he over-extends it — which is precisely the vulnerability that Mystique exploited, repeatedly, in two separate impersonations. He does not have a good defensive mechanism against the people he has already let in. The mechanism is *not letting them in,* which is why the in-list is so short.

### Self Read

He believes — chronically, durably, against mounting counter-evidence — that he is approximately the person he was at seventeen: the kid brother, the screw-up, the one who didn't quite make the cut for the next team. The self-concept is *strikingly* stable across decades in which every other piece of evidence has contradicted it. Loki has told him he is enormous. Emma has demonstrated it in his own body. Mikhail has tutored him in capacities his teachers cannot match. He has, in flashes, frozen oceans and dismantled armies. None of it sticks. The self-update mechanism is broken in a specific direction: he integrates negative information about himself instantly and treats positive information about himself as either a mistake, a kindness, or a trick.

The clinical name for this is *underaccommodating positive schema integration.* The plain English is: he has been told he is great for fifty years and he hears it as noise.

---

## III. Philosophical Beliefs (Articulated and Latent)

### On mutancy and identity

He believes — and this is unusual among first-generation X-Men — that being a mutant is *not* primarily a political identity. It is, for him, a wound and a fact, in that order. He will fight for mutant causes; he will not theorize them.
