If forced to choose between Hank and a current partner during such a crisis, will choose Hank in private grief while publicly choosing the partner — and will not survive that compromise intact. Risk window for Stage-3 dissociative escape elevated for weeks. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN: Cyclops makes a strategic decision that crosses Bobby's ethical line (Utopia-era, Schism-class, IvX-class).**
**EXPECT:** Dissent will be voiced, but late and softly. Will spend days drafting the disagreement internally before externalizing. When externalized, will be delivered with humor-buffering ("Hey, so, weird question, but —") followed by surprisingly clear ethical articulation. Will choose the opposing faction *if and only if* a permission-structure figure (Storm, Wolverine, Kitty) has already chosen it. Will not be the first defector; will be among the first ten. Loyalty pattern: continues to love Scott while opposing him; the *love-while-opposing* capacity is unusual and stable. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN: The institution itself betrays him (X-Men leadership conceals something material to him; Krakoa-class systemic deception).**
**EXPECT:** This is the form of betrayal he is *least* equipped for, because the institution is the parental transference and the corrective family-of-origin in one. Likely response: extended confusion phase, attempted re-rationalization, denial. When the denial finally breaks, expect a flat affective state lasting weeks, accompanied by reactivation of every prior identity-concealment defense — the closet schemas come back online whether they fit the situation or not. Will seek out the original five reflexively. Will not, on his own, leave the institution; would need to be *pulled out* by an attachment figure. **Confidence: moderate-high.**

**GIVEN: A romantic partner outs him publicly without consent (a re-enactment of the Bendis telepathic outing).**
**EXPECT:** The most precise trigger in his file for the binocular wound. Predicted sequence: 30–90 seconds of frozen non-response; immediate physical departure from the scene; 24–96 hours of unreachable retreat, often somatic (ice-form, geographically distant); reemergence with a constructed, *over-rehearsed* version of acceptance that masks the actual injury. The partnership will not survive even if he says it has. Long-tail effect: regression in trust extension to *all* new partners for 12–24 months. **Confidence: very high.**

---

## 7.b.4 — Temptation Predictions

**GIVEN: Offered a permanent civilian life — full identity concealment, no mutant disclosure, no team obligations.**
**EXPECT:** Visible, prolonged temptation. He will not accept, but he will *consider it longer than is comfortable to watch.* The CPA compartment is the prefigured architecture of this offer; he has rehearsed it for decades. Refusal will come, but it will come after a measurable interval of grief for the life he is declining. Predicted decision driver: presence or absence of Hank in the offered future. If Hank is included, temptation rises sharply. If team and Hank are excluded, decision tilts toward refusal within 48 hours. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN: Offered Omega-level expansion under tutelage (Emma-class, Mikhail-class, or external mentor of comparable caliber).**
**EXPECT:** Initial acceptance, three to eight weeks of measurable progress, then engineered self-sabotage — missed sessions, plateau performances, return of self-deprecating framing. He has done this at least four times in canon. The mechanism is not laziness; it is the felt sense, at a certain threshold, that he is becoming *too visible at full scale.* Predicted breakpoint: roughly the moment the tutor begins discussing him in terms that imply he has surpassed peer capacity. The lynch-mob schema fires on the *language* of exceptionality, not on the power itself. **Confidence: very high.** This is, in some ways, the central tragedy of the profile.

**GIVEN: Offered a path to confront and destroy a primary tormentor (Friends of Humanity figure, anti-mutant politician, the original mob).**
**EXPECT:** Will not accept. Will deflect with humor and reframe the offer as someone else's problem. *However:* if the same target threatens Hank, a partner, or a younger mutant he has mentored, the calculus inverts. Expect competent, focused, lethal-capable execution against threats to others that he would never marshal against threats to himself. This is the protective-mentor compartment overriding the suppression schema. Will minimize the action afterward. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN: Offered the ability to retroactively rewrite a single past event (reality-warp class temptation, time-travel class).**
**EXPECT:** First instinct will be the lynch-mob night, but he will not name it. He will name something smaller — a teammate's death, a missed opportunity to help — performing the deflection even in fantasy. If pressed, the underlying preference is uncertain: there is a non-trivial probability he would choose *to have come out earlier,* not to have undone the lynching, because the closet years are the wound he has had more time to articulate. **Confidence: low-moderate.** Genuine uncertainty in the record.

**GIVEN: Offered a leadership role with autonomy (his own team, his own school, his own jurisdiction).**
**EXPECT:** Will decline initially. Will be talked into it by a permission-figure. Will perform competently but spend the entire tenure waiting to be replaced by someone "more qualified." Will mentor exceptionally well, command adequately, and quietly engineer his own succession. Krakoa-era expansions are the partial counter-evidence; even there, his comfort with command lagged his demonstrated capacity by months. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN: Offered reconciliation with his father on the father's terms (partial, conditional acceptance).**
**EXPECT:** Will accept. Will accept far more than is healthy. Will accept on terms that re-impose the small-to-be-loved schema. Will rationalize the cost. Hank and current partner will see this clearly and Bobby will resent their seeing it. Predicted long-tail: the conditional reconciliation hollows out other relationships rather than the paternal one, because the paternal one is uncriticizable. **Confidence: moderate-high.** One of the more painful predictions in the file.

---

## 7.b.5 — Direct Contact with the Wound

The following stimuli touch the core wound directly. Responses are not modulated by ordinary social calibration; the schema fires beneath the humor frame.

**GIVEN: He is asked, sincerely, why he holds back.**
**EXPECT:** Joke first, always. If the asker holds — does not laugh, does not move on — second response is a smaller joke, then a deflection into the asker's life, then, if the hold continues for upwards of 30–60 seconds of silence, a partial truth delivered fast and quietly, often while looking elsewhere, often phrased as a hypothetical ("I guess maybe…"). Full disclosure is reserved for perhaps three people in his life. **Confidence: very high.** Interrogator's tool: silence, not pressure.

**GIVEN: He is publicly identified — by name, in front of strangers — as gay, as mutant, or as both, in a non-hostile context.**
**EXPECT:** Brief affective flush, scanning behavior (peripheral check for hostile faces; an old vigilance), then a joke calibrated to the room. The vigilance scan is involuntary and will occur even in objectively safe rooms (a Pride event, a Krakoan gathering). The body remembers the mob. **Confidence: very high.** This is permanent. Therapy could reduce the amplitude; nothing will erase the reflex.

**GIVEN: He encounters a child in the situation he was once in — mid-manifestation, frightened, surrounded by hostile civilians.**
**EXPECT:** Immediate, total deployment. No deferral, no permission-seeking, no suppression. The compartments collapse. He will physically place himself between the child and the crowd. He will not de-escalate verbally first; he will establish dominance of the space with cold and then negotiate from there. Will speak to the child specifically, not the crowd. Afterward: hours, sometimes days, of unsettled affect; the encounter retraumatizes by reactivation but also produces some of the few moments in his record in which the schema is contradicted by his own action. *These encounters are the strongest available therapeutic input in his life,* and a sufficient density of them could, over time, reshape the schema. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN: His father is dying or critically ill.**
**EXPECT:** Will go. Will sit. Will not say what needs to be said until after. The unfinished business will not be finished in time. Predicted grief profile: anomalous duration (years, not months), low surface expression, recurrent return to the hometown, possibly the purchase or retention of a property there — a somatic anchoring of the unresolved relationship. Will require Hank's presence at the funeral or some equivalent stabilizer. Risk of Stage-3 dissociative episode in the week following the death is elevated. **Confidence: high.**

**GIVEN: Someone he loves tells him, sincerely and without conditions, that they see him at full scale and want him there.**
**EXPECT:** This is the rarest stimulus and the one with the most volatile response. Initial disbelief, often verbalized as deflection ("you don't have to say that"). If the speaker repeats, holds, and is credible: affective overflow — tears, often unexpected to him, sometimes ice-form fluctuation as the body's regulation lags the emotion. The window opened by such a statement is narrow and precious; subsequent 24–72 hours are the period in which the deepest disclosures of his life have historically occurred. The window closes through self-protective re-narration ("they were just being nice"). **Confidence: moderate-high for pattern; window engineering is the single highest-leverage intervention in his profile.**

**GIVEN: He is accused — credibly or not — of having failed to save someone he could have saved at full capacity.**
**EXPECT:** Catastrophic. The accusation maps perfectly onto the schema's central anxiety: that the suppression has a moral cost, that the smallness he has practiced for survival has been purchased with other people's lives. Whether the accusation is true is nearly irrelevant; the schema accepts it. Predicted response: extended depressive episode, withdrawal from operations, possibly resignation from the team, refusal of comfort from partners. Recovery requires either (i) external evidence that the accusation is materially false, *delivered by Hank or a permission-figure,* or (ii) a contradicting action — a subsequent save at full capacity that resets the schema's accounting. Self-comfort is insufficient. **Confidence: very high.** This is, in the inverse, the *deepest* attack vector against him; anyone studying this file for hostile purposes would converge here.

**GIVEN: A telepath reads him, with or without consent, in a way that surfaces concealed material.**
**EXPECT:** The Bendis template. Initial denial, escalating to admission, followed by a *grateful-resentful* dual affect that he cannot fully integrate. He will be quietly furious at the violation and quietly relieved at the disclosure, and the two will not resolve. Long-term relationship with the telepath will be permanently altered — not severed, not whole. Pattern with Jean and Emma both bears this signature. **Confidence: high.**

---

## 7.b.6 — Decompensation Edge: The Sequence

The escalation curve in §5 was schematic. The granular sequence below is the predicted full decompensation cascade if no intervention occurs and stressors compound. Surveillance markers indicated for each stage.

**Stage 0 — Baseline.** Joke-rate normal (subject-specific high baseline). Ice-form deployment situational and brief. Civilian compartment intact. Sleep, eating, social engagement nominal. *Marker: presence of unprompted humor at meals.*

**Stage 1 — Mild stress.** Joke-rate elevated, sharper edge, slight directional targeting (Scott, authority figures). Marginal increase in solo time. Slight uptick in ice-form duration in non-combat contexts. Sleep mildly disturbed. *Marker: sarcasm replaces silliness.*

**Stage 2 — Moderate stress.** Joke-rate begins to *decrease.* This is the inflection point. Humor becomes bleaker, occasionally hostile, then sparse. Civilian compartment surfaces in inappropriate contexts (mentioning tax season during a mission). Ice-form retained for hours when minutes would suffice. Withdrawal from group meals. Hank-seeking behavior. *Marker: cessation of the unprompted joke.*

**Stage 3 — Significant stress / dissociative-somatic.** Ice-form sustained beyond functional need; partial dispersion at edges (fingers, hair) tolerated rather than corrected. Civilian-Bobby and Iceman-Bobby de-compartmentalize messily — wrong identity in wrong setting. Verbal affect flat. Sleep disrupted; eating sporadic. Refuses physical contact. Will answer direct questions but will not initiate. *Marker: he stops correcting his own dispersion.* Intervention window: rapidly closing.

**Stage 4 — Acute / extremis.** The throttle releases. Omega-scale expression in response to immediate threat. Tactical capacity surges; affective range collapses to a single cold flat note. Demonstrates abilities outside prior demonstrated range — large-area effects, fine-grain control, possibly molecular-scale operations. Duration: minutes to perhaps an hour. *Marker: the air temperature in his vicinity drops without his apparent attention to it.*

**Stage 5 — Post-release retraction.** The most dangerous stage for him personally. Shame floods, suppression schema reasserts violently. Self-isolation, often somatic — refusal to reconstitute, geographic flight, ice-form retreat into remote cold environments. Window of non-reconstitution attraction opens (cf. §7.b.2). Apologies, often disproportionate, delivered to bystanders and teammates. Promises to himself, internally, never to do that again. *Marker: he disappears for 48–96 hours and returns with the joke-rate artificially elevated to baseline plus 20%.*

**Stage 6 — Re-armoring.** Return to baseline humor, baseline suppression, baseline civilian-mutant compartmentalization, often with the suppression dialed slightly *tighter* than before. Each Stage 4–6 cycle leaves the suppression schema marginally reinforced unless the post-release period is met with witness, validation, and explicit permission to have been what he was. *Marker: he will not discuss what happened, and he will subtly punish anyone who tries to.*

The cycle is self-reinforcing and has run, by the published record, at least a dozen times. Each iteration delays the developmental work it interrupts. Each iteration also, paradoxically, delivers evidence to the schema that contradicts it — evidence the schema has, until recently, been able to discount. The Krakoa-era data is the first sustained period in the record in which the post-release retraction has been *partially* blocked by external structure. That data is the most hopeful in the file and the most fragile; the collapse of any such structure is, predictively, the highest-risk event he can encounter.

---

*End Section 7.b. Continued in 7.c — Predictive Model III: Growth, Repair & the Conditions of


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM
## Subject: Robert Louis Drake ("Bobby Drake" / Iceman)

*Classification: Internal Use — Protection-Oriented. This compendium catalogues every reliably actuated lever in the subject's psychology, soma, and social field. The orientation is inverted-surveillance: we map vulnerabilities so we can recognize when others are actuating them, and so that those who care for the subject can reach him, steady him, and refuse to weaponize him. Each lever is specified with: trigger, observable response, predicted escalation, and protective countermeasure.*

---

## 1. THE PRIMARY WOUND CLUSTER

### 1.1 The Lynch-Mob Schema

**The core lever.** Everything else in this document is downstream of one fact: at roughly age sixteen, on a date, on a sidewalk, in his own neighborhood, in front of people who had known him since infancy, Bobby Drake was nearly killed by a mob of his neighbors after his powers manifested. He was extracted from a holding cell by a stranger in a wheelchair. This event is the keystone of his interior architecture.

**Trigger profile.** Any scenario in which (a) a crowd turns, (b) an intimate becomes hostile upon revelation, (c) a community he has trusted withdraws permission, or (d) he is cornered indoors with no clear egress while being looked at. Stadium chants, jeering, signs in a crowd, neighbors gathering on a lawn at night, the phrase "we knew him since he was a kid" delivered with hostile inflection — all of these register at threat level disproportionate to immediate danger.

**Observable response.** Pupil dilation, breath-hold of two to four seconds, hands going to mid-temperature (subclinical ice manifestation along the knuckles and the underside of the forearm — visible as a faint fog rather than crystallization), and a stepwise rearward shuffle of roughly half a stride. He will crack a joke within twelve seconds. The joke is the tell.

**Escalation curve.** If the scenario continues he will request egress through humor ("yeah, I'm gonna…"), then through deflective story ("I have a thing"), then through ice-form, then through dispersal. The window from joke to dispersal under sustained crowd-hostility is, per the behavioral record, roughly three to seven minutes.

**Protective countermeasure.** Get him to a smaller room with two exits and one person he trusts. Do not gather around him to comfort; comforting clusters reproduce the geometry of the mob. Speak from across the room first. Lower the lights. Let him stand near a window. Hank McCoy, Warren Worthington, and Jean Grey have historically been the three bodies whose presence in the room dissolves this schema fastest; in their absence, any single trusted person who *sits down and stops looking at him directly* will do most of the work.

### 1.2 The "Being Seen at Full Scale" Inhibition

**Trigger profile.** Compliments on latent power. Telepathic readings of his ceiling. Teachers (Emma Frost, Mikhail Rasputin, Cannonball, on one occasion Jean) telling him what he could do. Footage of his own Omega expressions played back to him. Anyone saying the word "Omega" while looking at him.

**Observable response.** Immediate verbal minimization ("nah, that was a fluke," "the math was wrong that day"), a shoulder-roll forward (postural shrinkage of one to two inches), and a redirection of conversation to the speaker's own competence. If pressed, withdrawal from the room within ten to fifteen minutes, often via bathroom or kitchen pretext.

**Predicted behavior.** He will train for one to three sessions with the person who praised him, demonstrate marked improvement, then quietly drop the practice and resume his prior performance ceiling. This pattern is documented with Frost, Rasputin, and (Krakoa-era) repeatedly. The retreat is not laziness; it is *active* — he is putting the lid back on.

**Protective countermeasure.** Praise his *control*, not his *capacity*. Praise the precision, the restraint, the elegance of a small expression. He metabolizes that praise without retreat because it does not threaten the schema. If you need him at scale, do not ask him to *be* large; remove the *permission structure* against largeness and let him discover the necessity himself. Krakoa worked because it told him he was *allowed* without telling him he was *required*. The institutional grammar matters.

**Leverage warning.** An adversary who understands this inhibition can functionally disarm him in advance of any confrontation by foregrounding his power to him. Telepathic adversaries who broadcast his potential at him have historically reduced his combat efficacy by a measurable margin. This is a known and exploitable vector.

---

## 2. PATERNAL AND FAMILIAL LEVERAGE

### 2.1 William Drake (Father)

**The open wound.** The most reliably actuated single lever in the entire dossier. Any reference to his father produces disproportionate affect, regardless of valence. Praise of his father — affect spike. Criticism of his father — affect spike. News of his father's health — affect spike. Photographs — affect spike. The Long Island accent rendered by a stranger — measurable startle response.

**Specific sub-levers.**
- **The 1996 beating** (William hospitalized by Friends of Humanity for defending his son): produces guilt-affect, never fully discharged. Mention of the Friends of Humanity by name will pull this material to the surface.
- **The coming-out reception** (poor): produces a colder, more controlled response than the beating — this material has been packaged but not metabolized.
- **The unfinished reconciliation**: there is no version of "your father said…" that does not produce immediate full attention. Adversaries fabricating paternal statements have a clear vector.

**Observable response.** Drop in vocal register by roughly a third, slower speech, longer pauses between sentences. Hands go still — unusual for him; his hands are normally in motion. He will not joke for between forty seconds and several minutes, which is the longest sustained non-humor window in his behavioral baseline outside of combat.

**Protective countermeasure.** Do not bring up his father unless he has. When he does, *do not solve it*. He has been offered solutions for forty years and rejected all of them. He needs a witness, not a fixer. Sit, listen, do not pivot, do not joke back at his joke when the joke arrives (it will arrive as the exit signal — let him use it without reinforcement).

### 2.2 Madeline Drake (Mother)

**The quieter wound.** Less actuated because less acknowledged. His mother's passivity during his childhood — her failure to intervene against his father's bigotry — is the deeper structural injury and the one he has done the least conscious work on. He defends her reflexively. Criticism of her produces a snap-response sharper than criticism of his father.

**Trigger profile.** Any framing of her as complicit. Any framing of her as a victim he should have protected (which is the framing he silently holds and refuses to examine). The word "enabling."

**Protective countermeasure.** Do not psychologize her to him. He knows. He will arrive at it in his own time or not at all.

### 2.3 The Long Island Substrate

His hometown is geographically and psychically loaded. The Iceman solo run established that he can patrol it but not comfortably reside there. The substrate-level triggers: Catholic iconography from the specific parish, the particular intersection where his powers manifested, the diner where Judy Harmon worked, the holding-cell building. Adversaries with access to his pre-X-Men records have a map.

**Protective countermeasure.** When he visits, someone goes with him. Not as bodyguard. As witness.

---

## 3. RELATIONAL AND ATTACHMENT LEVERAGE

### 3.1 The Hank McCoy Channel

**The single most stable attachment in his life.** Sixty publication-years of continuous, durable, non-romantic intimacy. Hank is the person who knew him before powers, with powers, before and after every coming-out, before and after every team dissolution. Threats to Hank produce the sharpest, least-deflected response in Bobby's repertoire — quicker access to anger, quicker access to capacity, less humor.

**Trigger profile.** Hank in physical danger. Hank in moral peril (the recent canon of Hank's ethical degradation has produced visible, unresolved grief in Bobby that he has not adequately processed). Anyone speaking dismissively of Hank in Bobby's presence.

**Leverage warning.** An adversary holding Hank McCoy will get a different Bobby Drake than an adversary holding anyone else. The throttle releases.

**Protective countermeasure.** The unresolved grief over recent-Hank is its own pressure point. Someone needs to sit with him about it. He will not raise it. Raise it gently and at the right moment — not after combat, not in public, not in a kitchen.

### 3.2 The Original Five as Family-of-Origin Substitute

Warren, Jean, Scott, Hank — the four other founding students function as Bobby's chosen family-of-origin. Threats to any of the four produce disproportionate response. The structure of the original five is *itself* a lever: any narrative that fractures it (Schism, IvX, the various Scott-Jean entanglements) costs Bobby more than it appears to. He metabolizes by retreating into the *unfractured memory* of the early years, which is itself a partial dissociation.

**Protective countermeasure.** When the founding-five structure is under strain, his risk markers go up across the board — power suppression deepens, humor sharpens into bitterness, dissociative-somatic episodes become more likely. Track founding-five news as a leading indicator of his state.

### 3.3 Scott Summers — The Parental Transference

Scott rescued him from the holding cell. Scott is the older-brother-as-father across every era. Bobby defers to Scott reflexively, dissents from Scott ethically but rarely structurally, resents Scott chronically at low amplitude, and *grieves Scott* whenever Scott is lost. The transference is unresolved at sixty years of publication and will remain so.

**Trigger profile.** Scott in danger, Scott morally compromised, Scott absent. Anyone — including Scott himself — pointing out the transference to Bobby. The latter produces immediate defensive humor.

**Protective countermeasure.** Do not stage interventions about Scott. The transference is load-bearing. Removing it without replacement would destabilize him.

### 3.4 Romantic Leverage — Historical Pattern

The romantic record is long, consistent, and exploitable. Pattern: he pursues unavailable women across decades, then unavailable men across years, accepts deception as cost of proximity (Mystique impersonated his partner *twice* and he did not detect either; the third time it nearly happened, the realization wounded him more than the first two), and flees the available.

**Specific leverage vectors.**
- **The deception-tolerance gap.** He under-detects intimate deception. An adversary capable of impersonation, illusion, or shapeshifting has a documented entry path. Mystique exploited this twice, with full success.
- **The pursuit of the doomed.** He will invest in partners marked as unavailable. An operator presenting as unavailable can secure his investment more reliably than one presenting as available.
- **The post-coming-out window.** His relationships with men are still developmentally compressed — he is doing in his thirties (sliding) the work most do in their twenties. He is exposed in this period to the same dynamics that adolescents face, layered on adult cognition. He will idealize, he will pursue intensely, he will accept partners who are bad for him because the alternative — being alone with the question of who he actually is — frightens him more than the partners do.

**Protective countermeasure.** Anyone who appears in his life suddenly, intensely, and intimately should be evaluated. His friends should ask the questions he will not. The cost of looking foolish for vetting his partner is lower than the cost of a fourth Mystique.

### 3.5 The Northstar / Firestar / Other-Mutant-Peer Channel

His genuine, deep friendships with other mutants who *know him without his having to perform* — Angelica Jones especially, Northstar especially — are protective infrastructure. They are also leverage in the inverse direction: harm to them registers acutely, *and* they are the people most likely to be able to reach him in a Stage 3 dissociative episode. Their presence is a stabilizer; their absence during crisis is a risk factor.

---

## 4. IDENTITY-LEVEL LEVERAGE

### 4.1 The Closet and Its Aftershocks

He spent roughly fifty publication-years performing heterosexual pursuit. The performance left grooves. Even post-coming-out, he is vulnerable along the seams.

**Trigger profile.** Any framing of his closeted period as "fake" or "a lie" — produces shame-affect, defensive humor, withdrawal. Any framing of the Bendis-era telepathic outing as a violation he should have been angrier about — produces conflict-affect; he has not adequately processed his anger at being read without consent because he is grateful for the outcome, and the dissonance is unresolved. Any deadnaming of his prior partnerships as inauthentic.

**Protective countermeasure.** The closeted period is *part of* his life, not a prelude to it. He needs witnesses who treat it as continuous with the man he is now. The Opal years happened. The Polaris infatuation happened. They were not lies; they were the shape grief and concealment took. Frame accordingly.

### 4.2 The Compartmentalization Lever

**CPA-Bobby and Iceman-Bobby.** Two operational identities maintained as separate. The civilian compartment is *protective* — it is where he gets to be a man, not a mutant, not an Omega, not a symbol. Threats to the civilian compartment (mutant identity leaking into the accountancy life, IRS-level scrutiny, journalistic exposure of his civilian routines) are more destabilizing than threats to the mutant identity, because the mutant identity is already structured for threat.

**Protective countermeasure.** Protect the civilian compartment fiercely. Do not let X-business intrude on it without necessity. The compartment is a load-bearing wall of his sanity.

### 4.3 The "Kid Brother" Frame

Every team he has ever served on has, at some point, framed him as the youngest, the least serious, the team mascot. The frame is decades old and he has internalized it. Being patronized produces resentment that accumulates silently and discharges as bitter humor at irregular intervals.

**Trigger profile.** "Bobby will handle the small stuff." "Let the grownups talk." "Snowball fight time?" delivered with condescension. Younger mutants outgrowing him in apparent maturity.

**Protective countermeasure.** Give him work that requires *gravity* and let him do it. He will accept the assignment and rise to it. The frame breaks when it is no longer reinforced, which requires sustained institutional commitment.

---

## 5. SOMATIC AND PHYSIOLOGICAL LEVERAGE

### 5.1 The Reversion Problem

He has, on at least two documented occasions, been unable to revert from ice-form. Each episode produced acute body-image distress disproportionate to the physical inconvenience. The distress is about *loss of the civilian compartment* — if he cannot be Bobby-Drake-the-accountant in a body, the protective architecture of his life collapses.

**Trigger profile.** Any condition impairing reversion. Mirrors during ice-form. Being photographed in ice-form by civilians. Children seeing him and being frightened.

**Protective countermeasure.** During any extended ice-form deployment, schedule reversion checkpoints. Have a familiar civilian environment available immediately on reversion — clothes that fit, a bathroom mirror, food. Routinize the return.

### 5.2 The Dispersal Escape

His body is the most permissive escape vehicle on the X-roster. He *can* disperse. He *has* dispersed under stress. He *has* allowed himself to be shattered without resistance.

**Trigger profile.** Sustained emotional overwhelm with no social egress. Being trapped in a room with unresolved high-affect material (paternal confrontation; coming-out conversations; romantic ruptures). Combat against opponents who personalize the attack (Mystique especially; she shattered him *as a message*, and the message landed).

**Observable response.** Translucence at the extremities, then loss of structural definition in the silhouette, then particulate dispersal. The window from translucence to full dispersal is roughly thirty to ninety seconds depending on stress load. Reconstitution is voluntary; he must *choose* to come back.

**Protective countermeasure.** This is the highest-acuity risk in the entire dossier. Recognize translucence. Lower the affective load *immediately* — change the subject, leave the room, send the right person in. Do not chase him into dispersal verbally. Do not demand he reconstitute. Make the room safe to come back to and he will come back. The recovery is faster when the first voice he hears on return is calm and concerned with something concrete and small ("there's coffee").

### 5.3 Thermal and Environmental Tells

His subclinical thermal regulation broadcasts his internal state to anyone paying attention. Ambient cooling around him by one to three degrees during anxiety; visible breath in temperate rooms during anger; frost patterns on adjacent metal during grief; localized humidity drop during deception (he is a poor liar — the air around him goes dry).

**Leverage warning.** Telepaths, empaths, and observers trained on his physiology can read his state from the environment. He cannot fully mask. He can *partially* mask if warned, but the mask itself is effortful and costs him.

**Protective countermeasure.** In high-stakes social environments (negotiations, family confrontations, press), brief him in advance, give him a focal object (a cold drink — paradoxically, holding something already cold reduces ambient broadcast), and shorten the duration. He fatigues into broadcast.

---

## 6. INSTITUTIONAL AND STRUCTURAL LEVERAGE

### 6.1 Permission Structures

He waits for permission. This is the most strategically important fact about him for any handler, friend, or adversary. Permission to be powerful, permission to be himself, permission to confront his father, permission to leave a relationship, permission to take up space. Krakoa worked because it was a sustained permission structure. The fall of Krakoa removed it.

**Trigger profile.** Collapse of the institutional frame that has been authorizing him. Loss of leadership figures who have been granting permission. The phrase "you can't do that here" lands harder on him than on almost any other X-Man.

**Protective countermeasure.** During institutional transitions, he needs *new* permission structures established quickly. Someone — Hank, Storm, a chosen-family figure — needs to explicitly grant the permissions the institution used to grant. Without it, regression risk is significant: he will revert to throttling, compartmentalization, and the closeted-era affect baseline.

### 6.2 Authority Compliance with Ethical Carve-Out

He defers to authority. He dissents ethically. He rarely dissents *structurally*. Adversaries who position themselves as legitimate authority figures can get substantial compliance from him *until* an ethical line is crossed, at which point compliance terminates abruptly and completely. The line is sharper than people expect. He is one of the most reliable moral compasses on the team precisely because the line, once crossed, cannot be uncrossed by appeal to authority.

**Leverage map.** Authority figures get pre-line compliance. Ethical violators get post-line resistance. Identifying *where* his line is for a given subject in advance is therefore strategically valuable for both protective and adversarial purposes. The line is generally located at: *harm to a person who has not consented and cannot defend themselves.*

### 6.3 Mentor / Younger-Mutant Reversal

When given a mentoring role, he becomes a substantially different person — steadier, less deflective, more strategic, more direct. The role *itself* is therapeutic for him. Removing the role (forced inactivity, lack of younger mutants in his orbit) removes a stabilizer.

**Protective countermeasure.** Keep him in proximity to younger mutants. He needs them more than they need him, and both benefit. The mentoring frame breaks his "kid brother" frame from the other side.

---

## 7. ADVERSARIAL VECTORS — KNOWN AND PREDICTED

A consolidation of the leverage points most actuated by hostile actors, present and historical:

1. **Telepathic intrusion.** Emma Frost (consensually-ish), Jean Grey (non-consensually, Bendis era), Onslaught, others. His mind is permeable and the intrusions have all left marks. Telepathic defense is a chronic gap.
2. **Shapeshifter impersonation of intimates.** Mystique, twice successfully. This vector remains open.
3. **Power-amplification offers.** Loki, others. He has been offered what he is afraid to be. He has always refused. An offer presented in a form that bypasses the fear (necessity, emergency, someone else needing him at scale) is a vector that has not yet been fully exploited.
4. **Paternal manipulation.** William Drake has been used, will be used. Fabricated paternal statements, threats to William, news (fabricated or real) of William's health — all live vectors.
5. **Crowd-hostility staging.** Recreating the lynch-mob geometry — neighbors, signs, jeers, narrow streets at night — is the most direct route to the keystone wound. Anti-mutant operators have already done this.
6. **Outing as weapon.** He has been outed once non-consensually and absorbed it. A second outing — of something not yet disclosed (and there are always things not yet disclosed) — would land differently. Adversaries seeking to destabilize him have a template.
7. **Hank McCoy.** Stated above. Restated for emphasis. This is the highest-leverage relational vector in the file.

---

## 8. CALMING AND REACHING — THE PROTECTIVE TOOLKIT

A consolidated protocol for those tasked with reaching him in distress.

**To calm him at Stage 1 (sharper humor, mild withdrawal):** Joke back, but warmer. Lower the room's social temperature. Offer a small concrete task. Coffee works. Walking works. Hank in the room works.

**To calm him at Stage 2 (compartmental retreat, ice-form longer, bleaker humor):** Stop trying to make him laugh. Sit down. Be quiet near him. Ask about the civilian compartment — accounting, the apartment, the neighborhood. Pull him toward Bobby-not-Iceman.

**To reach him at Stage 3 (dissociative-somatic, refusing reversion, affect flat):** One person only. Trusted. Sit at distance. Do not demand reversion. Speak about something concrete and small. Do not name the wound. Wait. He returns when the room is safe.

**To respond at Stage 4 (Omega release):** Do not interrupt. He is not out of control; he is, for the moment, *in* control of more than usual. Provide a clean target if one is needed. After: do not praise the scale. Acknowledge the necessity. Help him pack it away without shaming the unpacking. He will apologize for property damage; accept the apology lightly and redirect to the people he protected.

**To persuade him:** Frame as ethical, frame as protective of someone smaller, do not frame as requiring his greatness. Give him permission, not pressure.


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# SECTION 7 — STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE

*The Asset Ledger. What the subject is, has, can do, and can withstand — catalogued without the corrective framing of the deficit sections. Some of what follows looks like weakness from another angle; we have already filed that angle elsewhere. Here we file only the load-bearing material.*

---

## 7.1 — POWER ASSETS (THE INSTRUMENT)

### 7.1.1 Raw capacity (Omega-class)

The single largest asset in the file. Per cross-era confirmations (Morrison's *New X-Men*, Bendis's *All-New*, Hickman/Duggan-era Krakoan rosters, the Omega-list canon established in the post-*House of M* documents), Drake's thermo-/cryokinetic ceiling sits at the top tier of recorded mutant capability. Functional inventory, exhaustively:

- **Thermal subtraction at scale.** Demonstrated continental-weather effects (Marauders #1–6, X-Men v.5 Duggan run); freezing of an opposing army outright (Mikhail Rasputin engagement, Marauders); ambient heat draw sufficient to neutralize stellar-temperature attacks (Emma-piloted display, *Uncanny* #314, and self-piloted analogues in Krakoan combat).
- **Matter generation from ambient humidity.** Constructs of ice scaled from a single bullet-block to architecture (ice-sleds, ice-bridges, ice-walls, ice-towers, ice-armor over teammates, ice-cocoons used as transport).
- **Hydrokinesis (latent, periodically expressed).** Conversion to or from any water-bearing medium; manipulation of vapor states; demonstrated remote condensation.
- **Somatic plurality.** The molecular-reconstitution capacity (*X-Men* #200; subsequent confirmations) means he is, at ceiling, not killable by conventional means. This is the rarest single asset in the X-roster outside of Jean Grey.
- **Ice-mimicry of organic forms.** Demonstrated by Emma Frost in his body; subsequently incorporated, intermittently, by Drake himself.
- **Fine-grain control at micro-scale** — frost on a lock tumbler, ice along a fingertip, a single supercooled droplet in a glass. Often demonstrated in domestic contexts (Iceman solo, Grace runs) and underused tactically.

The actuarial value of this instrument is so high that virtually any operational planning around Drake reduces to: *what permission structure unlocks what fraction of capacity, and for how long?*

### 7.1.2 Functional immortality (somatic)

He has been melted, shattered, vaporized, dispersed, telepathically displaced, and rebuilt. The reconstitution is reliable when the will is present. This is not just a survival asset; it is a *strategic* asset — he can take attacks no other body on the team can take, and he can credibly volunteer for them.

### 7.1.3 Tactical economy of force

Even at throttled output, his power per joule of personal stress is favorable. He fights without bleeding stamina the way most physical-class operators do. Endurance in extended engagements is documented across every team era; he is rarely the first one tired.

### 7.1.4 Environmental utility (the unglamorous asset)

Refrigeration, water purification, fire suppression, structural sealing, rapid bridge-construction over water or gaps, emergency cooling of overheating machinery, anesthetic-grade local numbing, food preservation in field. The civilian-utility tail of his power is enormous and underweighted in his self-concept. In a humanitarian deployment he is worth a small infrastructure brigade.

---

## 7.2 — COGNITIVE & TECHNICAL ASSETS

### 7.2.1 The CPA mind

Genuinely trained, genuinely competent. Forensic accounting credential acquired and maintained while on active super-human duty. This is not flavor text; it is a serious cognitive asset:

- **Numerate under pressure.** Comfortable with multi-variable bookkeeping, audit logic, fraud-pattern detection. Translates directly to logistics, mission accounting, and any forensic investigation requiring document-level work.
- **Bureaucratic literacy.** He reads contracts, knows what an indemnity clause does, understands tax exposure. In an organization full of people who do not, this is rare and load-bearing — he was, by reasonable inference, doing the practical paperwork on more than one team's operations.
- **Patience for tedium.** Will sit with a ledger. This is a temperament asset as much as a skill one.

### 7.2.2 Tactical intelligence (concealed)

The deflective humor obscures a consistently *correct* combat-read across decades. Notable instances: early identification of Sinister's Marauder pattern; consistent right-side calls during the Schism/IvX intra-X conflicts; situational awareness during Krakoan engagements where he routinely operates as second or third lead without command friction. He is not a strategist of Cyclops's rank, but he is a sound battlefield reasoner whose calls verify on review.

### 7.2.3 Ethical clarity

Across sixty years of intra-X factional politics — and the X-Men have had ugly ones — Drake's votes track the morally defensible position with unusual reliability. He opposed Cyclops's late-Phoenix-Force overreach without breaking the friendship; he supported the rights position consistently; he did not collaborate with Sinister or Apocalypse factions when others wavered. The clarity is not loud — see §3 — but it is *durable*, which matters more.

### 7.2.4 Slow but real self-update

His self-concept moves geologically, but it moves. The Bendis-era outing, the Grace-era parental confrontation, the Krakoan-era unthrottling — each is a genuine schema revision, not a cosmetic one. The pace is the cost; the fact of revision is the asset.

---

## 7.3 — TEMPERAMENTAL & CHARACTER ASSETS

### 7.3.1 Durable warmth

The single most consistent positive observation across writers. He is *liked*. Not in the political-asset sense — in the sense that other operators want him in the room. New recruits gravitate to him. Children are unafraid of him. The animals on Krakoa-era roster ledgers (the dogs in particular) responded to him without prompting. This is a base-temperament asset that cannot be trained.

### 7.3.2 Humor as social lubricant (the productive face of the defense)

§3 catalogued the defensive function of his humor. The asset side: he reduces interpersonal friction in high-strain environments. Teams with Drake on them have lower observed inter-member hostility than comparable teams without. He pre-empts conflict before it crystallizes. The X-Factor original-five run, the Champions, the Marauders, the various Krakoan deployments — all show this pattern. In a unit full of trauma-loaded specialists, a competent affect-deflector is a structural asset.

### 7.3.3 Loyalty (decadal-scale)

Hank McCoy: continuous attachment, ~60 publication-years, surviving every Beast-form change, every ethical lapse on Hank's part, every separation. Warren Worthington: similarly continuous. Jean Grey: continuous across her deaths and returns. Scott Summers: continuous despite cyclical resentment. This is not nostalgia; it is a documented capacity to *carry* a relationship through long disuse and severe stress without termination.

### 7.3.4 Low corruptibility

No record of bribery vulnerability. No documented compromise by external intelligence (mutant or human). The two compromises on record (Emma's telepathic body-piloting; Mystique's prolonged deceptions) were involuntary and produced no lasting allegiance shift. He has never defected. He has never sold information. He has never accepted a temptation arc that another writer would have given a less stable character. This is a quiet asset and a large one.

### 7.3.5 Low substance vulnerability

Light social drinker, no documented escalation, no record of pharmaceutical misuse. Given his affective load and the X-roster baseline, this is an unusually clean medical column.

### 7.3.6 Embarrassment tolerance

He can be the punchline. He has been, repeatedly, by his own writers and his own teammates. He does not metabolize humiliation into grudge. This is a personality asset with significant downstream operational value — he will take the dignity hit if the mission requires it, and he will not bill it back later.

---

## 7.4 — RELATIONAL & SOCIAL CAPITAL

### 7.4.1 The original five

The most valuable single relational asset in the file. McCoy, Worthington, Summers, Grey — four lifelong, high-trust, mutually-obligated relationships forged in shared adolescent trauma. Each of these people will, on demand, take a call from Drake at 0300 and act on it. This is a network-effect asset: through these four he is one degree from most of the X-roster and two degrees from most of mutant geopolitics.

### 7.4.2 The chosen-family second ring

- **Angelica Jones / Firestar.** Champions-era origin; durable; the closest thing he has to a younger-sister bond. Notably *not* romantic in either direction, which is itself a data point — he can sustain a deep cross-gender platonic bond when the structure permits.
- **Northstar.** Post-coming-out peer; older gay mutant; functional mentor-figure on identity questions Drake's biographical family could not provide.
- **Rogue.** Cross-era teammate; mutual trust across multiple deployments.
- **Kitty Pryde.** Brief romance, durable friendship; rare instance of his successfully *converting* a romantic miss into a stable platonic alliance.

### 7.4.3 Institutional standing

Founder-rank in the X-Men. This is structural seniority that does not depreciate. He has standing — quietly — equivalent to Cyclops, McCoy, Worthington, and Grey, regardless of how he carries himself in the room. On Krakoa this manifested in his being read, by the Quiet Council and the broader citizenry, as a senior figure even when not formally seated. Off Krakoa it persists as reputational capital that opens doors he does not always know are open.

### 7.4.4 The post-out community

Following the Bendis-era disclosure, Drake acquired — without seeking it — a constituency. He is one of the most visible openly gay figures in mutant public life. The Grace-era solo run demonstrated this asset functioning: younger queer mutants approach him; he is recognized in queer civilian spaces in New York and on the Island. Whether or not he leverages it, the constituency exists and is mobilizable.

### 7.4.5 William Drake — partial repair

The father relationship is unfinished but no longer purely adversarial. After the Friends of Humanity assault (*Uncanny* #340) and the post-coming-out reckonings of the Grace run, there is a working channel — wary, imperfect, sometimes worse, but not closed. Late-life parental rapprochement is rare and is, when achieved, a major resilience asset.

### 7.4.6 Madeline Drake

The mother relationship is the lower-friction half of the family-of-origin ledger; passive but not rejecting. Functional channel.

---

## 7.5 — MATERIAL & LOGISTICAL ASSETS

### 7.5.1 Financial standing

Modest by Worthington standards; secure by reasonable ones. The CPA practice generated real income across years when he was not on payrolled X-Men duty. The Iceman solo era documented him capable of independently affording a Manhattan-or-near-Manhattan apartment, vehicle, and discretionary spending. He is not wealthy; he is *solvent without dependency*, which is a different and underrated asset.

### 7.5.2 Property and base-of-operations access

- Long Island childhood home (family-of-origin; intermittent access).
- Various X-Mansion suites across eras (institutional).
- Krakoan residence during that era (lapsed with the island's fall).
- Apartment(s) in the greater NY metro across solo periods.

His baseline is *mobile* — he has rarely been pinned to a single domicile, and his power obviates most travel friction.

### 7.5.3 Documentation and civilian identity

Operationally clean. CPA license, valid identification, tax compliance, the apparatus of a real civilian life. He can credibly pass through a TSA line, rent a car, sign a lease. Most of his roster cannot.

### 7.5.4 Transportation autonomy

The ice-sled. Underweighted as an asset because it is visually goofy. Functionally: continuous self-propelled flight at sustained speed across any terrain with ambient humidity, requiring no fuel, no permission, no infrastructure. He has been, since adolescence, the most logistically self-sufficient mover in the X-roster outside of teleporters.

---

## 7.6 — RESILIENCE FACTORS (WHY THE STRUCTURE HOLDS)

### 7.6.1 Identity continuity through power volatility

Most mutants whose bodies dissociate at his scale lose narrative continuity of self. He does not. Memory is intact across shatterings; personality is intact across body-piloting episodes; affective signature reasserts on reconstitution. The cognitive-self is anchored independent of the somatic-self. This is the single rarest neurological asset in the file and the reason his physiology has not destroyed him.

### 7.6.2 The compartment as protection

§3 framed civilian-Bobby / Iceman-Bobby compartmentalization as a defense. The asset reading: it preserved a non-mutant *life* that most of his peers never built, and therefore preserved a domain of competence, identity, and routine that survives every crisis in the mutant column. When the X-Men collapse, he still has books to balance. When Krakoa falls, he still has an apartment. The compartment is a redundancy system.

### 7.6.3 Slow injury metabolism

He does not flame out. Where peers escalate trauma into volatility, addiction, defection, or breakdown, Drake metabolizes slowly through dysthymic flatness and humor. The cost is sixty years of unfinished developmental work; the asset is that he is *still here, still functional, still recognizably himself* after a biographical load that has broken peers repeatedly.

### 7.6.4 Reliable floor

His worst-day operational floor is high. Even depressed, even compartmentalized, even throttled, he shows up, executes competently, and does not abandon position. The Champions-collapse, post-Opal, and post-shattering periods all show this: degraded affect, intact performance. This is the kind of reliability that fills mission slots when stars cannot.

### 7.6.5 Capacity to receive help

He has accepted tutoring (Emma, Mikhail, Cannonball, Northstar in his way). He has accepted rescue (Xavier, originally). He has accepted disclosure-prompting (Jean). He has accepted partnership offers. The acceptance is slow and often grudging, but it occurs. This is the difference between a subject who can be helped and one who cannot.

### 7.6.6 Permission-structure responsiveness

The Krakoan unthrottling is the proof: given the right external scaffolding, he *can* operate at ceiling. This is an asset because it tells planners exactly what intervention works. He is not a closed system; he is a system with a known unlock condition. Build the scaffolding, get the Omega.

### 7.6.7 Late-bloom trajectory

The developmental curve is still rising at six decades of biography. Most subjects at his publication age are consolidating or declining; he is *acquiring* — partners, identity ownership, power expression, parental relationship. The trajectory itself is an asset: he is one of the few subjects in the archive whose forward arc is still genuinely open.

---

## 7.7 — UNCATEGORIZED POSITIVE OBSERVATIONS

- **Excellent recall for personal-history detail** about teammates: birthdays, prior injuries, ex-partners, family members. Often deflects this knowledge through casual reference. Asset: he is the institutional memory of the original X-Men in a way Cyclops (mission-focused) and McCoy (data-focused) are not. He remembers the *people*.
- **Cooks competently.** Domestic skill noted across the Iceman solo run. Modest, real, present.
- **Comfortable with children and adolescents** in instruction roles when assigned. Generation X cameos, junior-team mentoring on Krakoa. Patient, age-appropriate humor.
- **Aesthetic sensibility for his power.** When unthrottled he produces ice-architecture of genuine beauty — bridges, sculptures, the ice-form itself. The aesthetic dimension is not strategic but it is an asset of *being*, and it is one of the few places his core self expresses without armor.
- **Punctual.** Across eras and writers, Drake arrives when he says he will. In an organization of prima donnas this is non-trivial.
- **Honest under direct questioning** *about everything except his own interior.* Will not lie to teammates about mission-relevant facts. The closet was a sin of omission, not commission; he was never observed constructing active deception about himself toward people he respected. The distinction matters.

---

## 7.8 — SUMMARY ASSET POSTURE

The ledger reads, in aggregate: a top-tier power instrument paired with an unusually clean character column, a deep and durable relational network, a redundant civilian life, a high operational floor, a slow but functional self-revision capacity, and a forward developmental trajectory still actively rising. The deficits filed elsewhere are real and are not erased by this section — but they sit on top of a structure that has not failed in sixty years of continuous load. The instrument is enormous; the operator is decent, durable, liked, trusted, solvent, and improving. The unlock condition is known. The friends are in place. The father is, finally, partially present.

Asset posture: **high, broad, deepening.** Recommend continued observation under the standing benevolent mandate; recommend no intervention beyond the maintenance of permission structures that have demonstrably worked.

*— END SECTION 7 —*


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION — SUBJECT: ROBERT LOUIS DRAKE

*Classification: Behavioral collapse mapping, longitudinal. Derived from sixty publication-years of stress-response data. This section maps not the everyday escalation curve (covered in §5) but the actual decompensation architecture — what breaks, in what order, under what loads, and what the failure looks like from the outside.*

---

## 1. THE GENERAL SHAPE OF HIS COLLAPSE

Subject does not decompensate the way most high-capacity operators decompensate. The standard pattern in comparable subjects is *loss of control* — affect floods, judgment degrades, behavior becomes erratic or violent. Drake's pattern is the inverse and is, in its own way, more dangerous: he decompensates by **losing the ability to stay small.**

His baseline functioning is a continuous, low-effort, self-administered suppression of capacity, identity, and affect. The lifelong work of being Bobby Drake is the work of *not* being what he is. When the load on that suppression exceeds tolerance, the suppression fails — and what emerges is not chaos but *scale.* He becomes accurately powerful. He becomes accurately gay. He becomes accurately depressed. He becomes accurately furious. Each of these is, by his standards, a catastrophic failure, because each of them violates the operational contract he negotiated in adolescence: *don't be seen at full size, or they'll come for you with torches.*

The collapse, therefore, is not a collapse *into* dysfunction. It is a collapse *out of* the dysfunctional containment that has been his functioning baseline. This is why his decompensations tend to be followed not by recovery to baseline but by a forcible re-suppression — he packs himself back into the container, apologizes, jokes, and resumes the throttle. The re-suppression is the real damage. The episode is just the leak.

---

## 2. THE ESCALATION LADDER, RUNG BY RUNG

The escalation curve sketched in §5 is here resolved at finer grain. Each rung is named by its *interior* signature (what is happening psychologically) and its *exterior* signature (what an observer would log).

### Rung 0 — Baseline operating

*Interior:* low-grade dysthymic hum; continuous micro-management of power output; continuous micro-management of which Bobby is in the room (civilian, Iceman, joker, soldier). The hum is so constant he experiences it as the texture of being alive.
*Exterior:* warmth, quips, competent execution, presence at the social periphery of any group. Drinks his coffee. Files his returns. Freezes the doorknob of someone he likes as a greeting.

### Rung 1 — Load increase, defenses tighten

*Interior:* the joke arrives a half-beat faster than the feeling that prompted it. Compartments thicken. He begins to track exits, both physical and conversational.
*Exterior:* sharper, drier humor. Slightly more snark directed at command (historically: Scott). Marginal increase in solo time. The ice he leaves on surfaces gets thinner, more precise, more decorative — fine-control compensation for internal turbulence. He starts cooking, or organizing, or doing his own books on paper.

### Rung 2 — Significant load, compartmental retreat

*Interior:* the civilian-Bobby compartment surfaces involuntarily. He finds himself thinking about apartments, about taxes, about the strip mall on Long Island where he used to know the dry cleaner. This is regression to the pre-mutant self, used as a refuge.
*Exterior:* he spends longer in ice-form than the situation requires. He reverts later than expected. Jokes acquire a bleak undertone the team has learned to register. He volunteers for unglamorous logistical tasks (rearguard, evacuation, perimeter). He calls Hank. He does not say why.

### Rung 3 — Acute load, somatic-dissociative phase

*Interior:* the body stops feeling like a possession. He experiences his ice-form as more comfortable than his flesh-form — *truer.* The throttle on the power becomes effortful in reverse: he must now actively choose to *not* extend, where before extension was the effort. Affect flattens. He is, by his own private metric, somewhere else.
*Exterior:* refuses or delays reversion. Skin remains crystalline in social situations where it doesn't need to be. Eyes hold longer on middle distance. Jokes thin out, then stop. Voice flattens to a near-monotone — the surveillance tell is that he stops doing the slight upward inflection at the end of his sentences that has been a six-decade signature. When he speaks at all, he speaks in declaratives.

### Rung 4 — Decompensation proper, the throttle release

*Interior:* the contract breaks. He stops choosing smallness because he can no longer afford the energy to choose it. What was suppressed surfaces — not as eruption but as *accuracy.* He becomes the size he actually is. There is, briefly, no Bobby Drake in the operational sense: there is the field of cold he has always been, doing the things that field can do.
*Exterior:* environmental temperature drops measurably and continues to drop. He generates ice from ambient humidity at scales that surprise even teammates who have known him for decades. He is suddenly, terrifyingly competent. He freezes things he has historically refused to freeze (atmospheres, oceans, armies, in canonical instances). Speech is sparse, level, exact. The clowning is absent and its absence is the single most alarming data point for anyone reading him.

### Rung 5 — Post-event re-suppression

*Interior:* shame. Not for what he did — typically the action was correct — but for having been *seen at scale.* The lynch-mob schema activates retrospectively. He audits the faces of those who watched and grades them for likely betrayal.
*Exterior:* immediate return to humor, often louder and more aggressive than baseline. Apologies for property damage that nobody asked for. Physical withdrawal within hours — long shower, long walk, long flight. Calls Hank. Does not call his father. Re-engages civilian-Bobby aggressively (does his taxes, balances a ledger, organizes a drawer). The compartments are rebuilt in front of witnesses, and the rebuild is itself the tell.

The unusual feature of this ladder, again: most subjects' Rung 4 is the failure state. Drake's Rung 4 is, by external measure, his most competent state. **His failure state is Rung 5 — the re-suppression — because that is where the developmental injury is re-inscribed.**

---

## 3. THE THREE CANONICAL COLLAPSE MODES

Across the longitudinal record, his decompensations sort into three recurrent shapes. They are not mutually exclusive — a serious enough stressor will produce all three in sequence — but each has a distinct signature.

### Mode A — The Dissociative Withdrawal

The most frequent. Triggered by accumulated emotional load without a clear external enemy: team dissolutions (Champions, X-Factor reshuffles), romantic losses (Opal, Polaris, the Mystique discoveries), identity exposures (Bendis-era outing, parental rejection in *Iceman* solo).

*Course:* Rung 2 → 3, stalls at 3, may persist for weeks. Functional but absent. Goes through the motions of teamwork and conversation with the affect drained out. Spends inordinate time alone or in flight. Ice-form lingers. The compartments stop talking to each other — civilian-Bobby and Iceman-Bobby become so separated that conversations with him in one mode feel as if they did not happen when he is in the other.

*External signature:* the joke is still there but the laugh behind it is not. Friends who know him well (Hank, Warren, Jean historically, Northstar latterly) detect this within hours. Friends who know him less well miss it for weeks because the clowning surface is fully maintained.

*Risk:* low for self-harm in the conventional sense, but elevated for *somatic non-reversion* — the comic-book-canonical version of self-neglect. He will simply remain crystallized and stop attending to the human-form needs (food, sleep, social presence) until something or someone calls him back.

*Resolution pattern:* requires an external pull, not an internal push. Hank arriving with food. A younger mutant needing help. A crisis demanding the throttle. He does not pull himself out; he is pulled.

### Mode B — The Reluctant Apotheosis

Triggered by an external threat severe enough to override the suppression contract — Loki's augmentation in *X-Factor Annual #4*, Emma Frost's possession in *Uncanny #314*, the late-Krakoa continental-scale deployments, the post-shattering reconstitutions in *Astonishing*.

*Course:* skips or compresses Rungs 1–3, lands at Rung 4 within minutes. The release is total. He becomes, briefly, the Omega he has always been. Action is effective, precise, and at a scale that retroactively recontextualizes every previous performance he has given.

*External signature:* ambient cold. The fine-grained ice-mimicry he normally refuses. Sentences shortened to instructions. Eyes look through people. The absence of the upward inflection. Property damage proportional to threat — which is to say, large.

*Risk:* the risk here is *not* in the event. The event is, by his own and others' lights, a success. The risk is in the immediate aftermath — Rung 5 — when the shame floods in. The post-apotheosis re-suppression is when he is most likely to slide into Mode A, sometimes for extended periods. He has, repeatedly across the record, performed at omega-level on a Tuesday and been functionally absent for the next two weeks. The *scale* of the post-event withdrawal correlates with the *scale* of the demonstrated power, which is itself diagnostic — confirmation that the power, not the threat, is what frightens him.

*Resolution pattern:* requires a permission structure to remain in place after the event. On Krakoa, the post-event withdrawals shortened markedly because the institution kept telling him the apotheosis was *allowed.* When the permission structure is absent (e.g. early career), the withdrawals are long and the re-suppression deeper. This is the most clinically important environmental variable in his case file.

### Mode C — The Identity Rupture

The rarest and most damaging. Triggered specifically by *involuntary* exposure of concealed identity. Two clear canonical instances: the adolescent near-lynching (mutant identity exposed by the manifestation of his powers in front of his date and her community) and the Bendis-era outing (sexual identity exposed without consent by an adolescent telepath). The *Iceman* solo book's parental confrontation is a quasi-instance — voluntary, but with involuntary downstream exposure.

*Course:* simultaneous activation of all four lower rungs. He is, in the same moment, defending with humor (Rung 1), withdrawing socially (Rung 2), dissociating somatically (Rung 3), and — variably — releasing the throttle (Rung 4). The presentation is disorganized in a way Mode A and B are not. The disorganization is the diagnostic.

*External signature:* uncharacteristic incoherence. Jokes that don't land because the timing is off. Statements that contradict statements made minutes earlier (the post-Bendis denial-then-acknowledgment sequence is the cleanest example in canon). Physical instability — partial transformations, flickering between forms. Avoidance of eye contact, which is otherwise not part of his baseline.

*Risk:* the highest of the three modes for genuine, lasting characterological damage. Mode C events restructure his self-schema. The lynch mob produced the entire suppression contract. The Bendis outing required years of subsequent solo-book work to metabolize. The parental confrontation is, by the latest available record, *still* incompletely metabolized. Each Mode C event leaves residue that is detectable in subsequent behavior for years.

*Resolution pattern:* slow, requires safe witnesses, requires the new exposed identity to be *re-integrated* rather than re-suppressed. This is where the difference between supportive and unsupportive environments is starkest: in supportive environments (Krakoa; certain post-coming-out periods) Mode C resolves into expanded selfhood; in unsupportive environments (his hometown; his father's house) Mode C resolves into deeper compartmentalization. He has experienced both outcomes and the contrast is legible in the record.

---

## 4. THE LOAD INPUTS — WHAT ACTUALLY BREAKS HIM

Stressors are not equivalent. Different inputs route to different modes via different rungs. The map:

- **Combat threat to teammates** → Mode B, rapid. He skips the ladder. The throttle releases for *them*, not for himself, which is the only condition under which he permits release without subsequent maximal shame.
- **Combat threat to himself alone** → defended with humor at Rung 1; rarely escalates. He has a high tolerance for personal danger; it is the variable he is most habituated to.
- **Romantic loss or betrayal** → Mode A, slow, deep. Particularly when the partner turns out to have been not who they appeared to be (the Mystique sequences) — these route additionally through Mode C because the betrayal is an *identity* betrayal as well as a relational one.
- **Team dissolution** → Mode A, severe. The institution is the family-of-origin replacement; its dissolution is felt as familial loss. The Champions' collapse and each subsequent X-team reshuffle have produced detectable withdrawal periods.
- **Being patronized as the kid** → Rung 1, sustained. Rarely escalates but accumulates a resentment ledger that he does not discharge. The accumulation is itself a long-term decompensation risk — the ledger gets paid in displaced ways (snark at command, withdrawal from leadership opportunities he could have taken).
- **Compliments about latent power** → counterintuitive trigger. Routes immediately to Rung 2 or 3. Being told he is more than he performs is experienced as *threat*, not affirmation, because it points at the very capacity he has organized his life around suppressing.
- **Paternal contact** → unpredictable routing. Can hit any of the three modes depending on the content. The open wound. The single most volatile input in his stressor profile.
- **Threat to Hank McCoy** → unique routing. Bypasses the entire ladder. He becomes immediately, soberly, lethally competent. The deflective humor disappears, the suppression releases, and he does not exhibit Mode B's subsequent shame because the action is felt as legitimate. The relational anchor of his life; threats to it produce his most undefended self.
- **Permission-structure collapse** (the loss of an institutional or relational frame that has told him he is allowed to be himself) → Mode A combined with regression to pre-permission baseline. The most likely route to extended dysfunction. The clearest instance is the post-Krakoa data — to the degree the record extends — where the loss of the structural permission to be fully powerful and fully partnered creates measurable regression toward the older suppression contract.

---

## 5. THE WARNING SIGNATURE — WHAT AN OBSERVER SEES FIRST

For surveillance purposes, the early-detection markers, ranked by reliability:

1. **Loss of the upward inflection at sentence-ends.** Six decades of vocal data confirm this micro-pattern as his single most stable affective tell. Its absence is the earliest detectable sign that he has moved off baseline.
2. **Increased fineness of incidental ice-work.** When the internal pressure is high, the external ice gets precise — frost patterns become more intricate, the rim of a glass freezes more cleanly, the doorknob-frost becomes a fractal rather than a smear. The motor system discharges what the affective system suppresses.
3. **Delayed reversion from ice-form.** Seconds at Rung 1, minutes at Rung 2, hours-to-days at Rung 3. Linear and reliable.
4. **Humor latency change.** At baseline, the joke comes at a measured beat after the prompt. At Rung 1, it comes faster (defensive acceleration). At Rung 3, it comes slower or not at all. The shift in either direction is diagnostic.
5. **Calls to Hank.** Frequency increases at Rung 2. Content shifts from social to vague-emotional at Rung 3. Cessation of calls at Rung 4 — he stops because he does not want Hank to witness the apotheosis or its aftermath.
6. **Civilian-Bobby surfacing.** Accounting work, ledger-keeping, organizing, cooking. The pre-mutant self emerging as refuge. Visible at Rung 2.
7. **Reduction in eye contact.** Baseline is moderate-to-warm; reduction is an early indicator of Mode C activation specifically.
8. **Property-damage apologies that precede any property damage.** At Rung 3, he begins apologizing pre-emptively. The signal that he is anticipating his own release.

---

## 6. WHAT WOULD ACTUALLY DESTROY HIM

Decompensation is not destruction. He has decompensated, in the modes mapped above, many times across six decades and has reassembled each time — often with diminished functional range, but reassembled. The question of what would *not* permit reassembly is separate and important.

The combination most likely to produce non-recoverable collapse:

**Loss of Hank McCoy + loss of institutional permission structure + paternal rejection re-confirmed, in temporal proximity.** Each of these alone is survivable. Two is severe. Three concurrently would remove every external anchor that has historically pulled him out of Mode A withdrawals and would re-confirm the original lynch-mob schema at full force. The likely outcome would be permanent retreat into the somatic-dissociative state — extended or indefinite non-reversion, the ice-form as final compartment. Not death; something more like a chosen absence from the human register of his own life.

The secondary catastrophic scenario: **a Mode B event of unprecedented scale witnessed by a population that subsequently turns on him for it.** A re-enactment, at adult scale and adult capacity, of the original lynching schema. He has organized sixty years of behavior around preventing this exact event. Its actual occurrence would, by his own internal logic, prove that the suppression contract was correct all along and that every release of throttle was an error. Recovery from this would require not therapy but a wholesale rewrite of the schema, which the existing personality structure is not equipped to perform.

The tertiary scenario, slower and more insidious: **the gradual loss, one by one, of every person who knew him before the suppression contract was renegotiated** — the surviving members of the original five, the friends from the closeted decades, the witnesses to his expansion. Without those witnesses, the expansion becomes deniable to himself, and the suppression contract reasserts by default. This is the slow-motion version. It is also, given the publication record's accelerating losses across the team, the most realistic.

---

## 7. THE GENERAL PRINCIPLE

He breaks by becoming accurate. He recovers by becoming small again. The recovery is the wound. The breakage is, perversely, the healing — interrupted each time by the recovery. The clinical task, were anyone tasked with it, would not be to prevent his decompensations but to *prevent the re-suppression that follows them.* Every collapse is a window. Every window has been closed.

The pattern is, across six decades, the same pattern. The man learns the lesson over and over and does not retain it, because the structure that would let him retain it has only intermittently existed in his life. When the structure exists, he retains. When it disappears, he forgets. He has been, in this sense, *waiting* — the entire publication record reads, in the failure-mode register, as the waiting of a man who has been told once that being himself was lethal and has been waiting ever since for the world to tell him, durably and unambiguously, that the rule has changed.

It has been told to him, in pieces. The pieces have not yet assembled into a durable answer. Until they do, the failure modes will continue to recur on the schedule the stressor profile dictates — Mode A on losses, Mode B on threats, Mode C on exposures, the ladder climbed and descended, the throttle released and re-set, the apologies for the property damage offered to an audience that, by now, has stopped asking for them.

— END SECTION —


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT — SUBJECT: ROBERT LOUIS DRAKE

*Classification: Forward projection from longitudinal record. Probabilistic, not deterministic. All forks predicated on documented behavioral pattern + plausible environmental pressure.*

---

## 1. THE CURRENT POSITION — WHERE THE NEEDLE SITS AS OF THIS FILING

To project forward, one must first locate the subject precisely on his own developmental curve. The longitudinal record places him, at present, in an extraordinarily unusual position: **for the first time in his life, the major architectural suppressions have all been at least partially released and then, with the collapse of the Krakoan permission-structure, partially re-imposed.** He has been seen at full scale (Omega-rated, publicly partnered, militarily decisive in continental-scale operations) and survived it. He has also watched the structure that licensed that visibility dissolve. He is, behaviorally, in the position of a man who has been allowed to walk without a cane for several years and is now being handed the cane back and asked whether he still needs it.

This is the central question of his forward trajectory: **does the post-Krakoan Bobby Drake retain the gains, or does he revert to the throttle?** Every other question downstream — partnership, family, role within the X-institution, relationship to his own power, role as mentor, late-life integration — is a derivative of this one.

The base rate, drawn from sixty years of data, favors regression. He has regressed after every prior expansion: after Loki, after Emma's possession, after Mikhail's tutoring, after every telepath who told him what he was. The base rate is brutal and should be respected.

The counter-evidence, however, is non-trivial. Three things have changed that did not change in any prior expansion-and-retreat cycle:

1. **The closet is open.** The single largest energetic drain on his psychic economy — the maintenance of a concealed second identity — is no longer operative. This frees affective and cognitive bandwidth that has been committed elsewhere his entire adult life.
2. **He has had sustained Omega expression, not flash expression.** Prior expansions were episodic — a Loki blessing, an Emma possession, a crisis. Krakoa gave him years of normalized high-output operation. The neural and behavioral grooves are different when capacity is practiced rather than glimpsed.
3. **He has had at least one publicly visible romantic partnership in which he was the pursuer rather than the rejected.** This is a new attachment-experience for him and the data on attachment plasticity in midlife suggests that even one corrective relational experience can begin to re-pattern internal working models.

So the forward picture is: a man at a genuine inflection point, with sixty years of regression pattern pulling one way and three never-before-present integrative factors pulling the other.

---

## 2. LIKELY DEVELOPMENTS — THE NEAR-TERM (18–36 MONTHS OF SUBJECTIVE TIME)

### 2.1 Power expression
